امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب مکفول لا نے اپنا قرضہ کفیل سے وصول کیا تو گویا اس نے کفیل کو اپنے قرضہ کے مال کا مالک کر دیا یا مکفول لڑ نے کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے قرضہ کا مال وصول کرنے میں اپنا قائم مقام کر دیا اور ان دونوں صورتوں میں کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے مال واپس لینے کا اختیار ہوگا کیونکہ پہلی صورت میں کفیل بذات خود مالک ہے اور دوسری صورت میں مالک کا قائم مقام ہے اور یہ آپ کو معلوم ہے کہ مالک بھی اپنا مال لے سکتا ہے اور مالک کا قائم مقام بھی لے سکتا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ کفالہ بغیر امرہ کی صورت میں بھی کفیل، مکفول عنہ سے اپنا ادا کیا ہوا مال واپس لے سکتا ہے ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جس پر قرضہ ہو اس کے علاوہ کو قرضہ کا مالک بنانا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں مکفول لہ کی طرف سے کفیل کو ایسی چیز کا مالک بنانا لازم آئے گا جس کے سپرد کرنے پر مکفول لۂ قادر نہیں ہے پس مکفول عنہ جس پر قرضہ ہے اس کے علاوہ کو یعنی لکفیل کو مالک بنانا جائز نہیں ہے اور جب کفیل کو مالک بنانا ہی جائز نہیں ہے تو کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے مطالبہ کرنے کا اختیار کیسے ہو سکتا ہے اور کفالہ بامرہ میں حکم کفالہ کی وجہ سے کفیل کے لئے مکفول عنہ پر اسی طرح مال واجب ہوتا ہے جیسے مکفول لا کے لئے کفیل پر واجب ہوتا ہے ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ کفیل کا حق اس کے ادا کرنے تک مؤخر ہو جاتا ہے یعنی جب کفیل مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے ادا کر دے گا تب کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے مطالبہ کا حق ہوگا اور یہ بات چونکہ کفالہ بغیر مرد میں محق نہیں ہوتی یعنی کفیل کے لئے مکفول عنہ پر مال واجب نہیں ہوتا اس لئے کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے مال کے مطالبہ کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفالہ بغیر امرہ کی صورت میں کفیل مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے قرضہ ادا کرنے میں مکفول عنہ پر احسان اور تبرع کرنے والا ہے اور احسان کرنے والا اپنا احسان واپس لینے کا شرعاً مجاز نہیں ہوتا اس لئے کفالہ بغیر امرہ کی صورت میں اگر کفیل نے مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے قرضہ ادا کر دیا تو اس کو واپس لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا ہے
Imam Malik's proof is that when the creditor collected his debt from the surety, it is as if he made the surety the owner of the debt money, or the creditor made the surety his representative in collecting the debt from the debtor. In both cases, the surety has the right to take back the money from the debtor, because in the first case the surety is himself the owner, and in the second case he is the representative of the owner. And you know that the owner can take his property, and the representative of the owner can also take it. So it is established that even in the case of guarantee without order, the surety can recover what he paid from the debtor. Our response is that it is not permissible to make someone other than the debtor the owner of the debt, because then the creditor would be making the surety owner of something which the creditor is not able to transfer. So it is not permissible to make the surety the owner, and if it is not permissible, how can the surety have the right to demand from the debtor? In the case of guarantee by order, because of the order, the surety has a claim on the debtor similar to the creditor's claim on the surety, except that the surety's right is deferred until he pays. Since this does not exist in guarantee without order, the surety has no right to demand from the debtor. Our proof is that in guarantee without order, the surety is doing a favor and volunteering, and a volunteer cannot legally take back his favor, so he cannot recover.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute. The issue is whether a surety who guaranteed without the debtor's order can recover from the debtor after paying the creditor. Imam Malik holds yes, based on two arguments: (1) by paying, the surety becomes owner of the debt (like a purchase), and (2) the surety becomes the creditor's representative to collect from the debtor. The Hanafi response refutes both: making a non-debtor owner of the debt is invalid because the creditor cannot transfer ownership of a debt to a third party without the debtor's consent; this would create an obligation on the debtor beyond the original. In the case of guarantee by order, the debtor implicitly consents and a reciprocal obligation arises. Without order, the surety is a mere volunteer (mutabarri'), and Shari'ah does not allow a volunteer to reclaim a gift. This ruling is emphasized by the author of al-Hidayah. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that recovery is not allowed without the debtor's order.

Key Terms
تبرع (tabarru'): Act of charity or voluntary giving; the surety's payment without order is considered tabarru'.
مالک بنانا (malik banana): Making someone owner of something; here, the creditor making the surety owner of the debt.
کفالہ بغیر امر (kafalah bi ghayr amr): Guarantee or suretyship undertaken without the debtor's order or permission.
مکفول عنہ (makful 'anhu): The debtor on whose behalf the guarantee is given.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main Hanafi proof for rejecting the Maliki view that a surety can recover without the debtor's order?
A) The surety is a minor and cannot contract.
B) The surety's payment is a voluntary gift, and a gift cannot be revoked.
C) The debtor is bankrupt.
D) The creditor must consent to the surety's recovery.

Key Takeaway
A surety who guarantees without the debtor's order cannot recover the paid amount from the debtor because his payment is considered a voluntary donation.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
6 min
Understanding the Surety's Right to Recover Without Request
Presents Maliki proof and Hanafi rebuttal on surety's right to recover

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the surety's right to recover in kafalah bighayri amrih, explain the Maliki proof, and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal.

Core Idea
Without the debtor's request, the surety's payment is a gratuitous favor (tabarru') that cannot be reclaimed.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: if someone pays another's debt without being asked, can they later demand reimbursement? The Hanafi school holds that such a payment is a voluntary favor (tabarru'), and a volunteer cannot take back their gift. Imam Malik, however, presents a powerful analogy that would grant the surety a right to recover. We will walk through the Maliki proof, the Hanafi response, and the practical consequences of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the established Hanafi ruling: a surety who pays without the debtor's request cannot recover the amount from the debtor.
This is based on the principle that a gratuitous act cannot be revoked.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Recognize that Imam Malik (and one narration from Imam Ahmad) allows recovery. Understand his proof: when the creditor receives payment, it is as if he made the surety the owner of the debt or his deputy.
3
Follow the opponent's dalil
Trace the Maliki reasoning: if the surety is an owner or deputy, he can claim from the debtor. This is an argument by analogy (qiyas).
The analogy rests on the idea that ownership or deputyship gives a right to demand.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response refutes the analogy: making someone other than the debtor the owner of a debt is invalid because the creditor cannot hand over the debt to a non-debtor. In kafalah bi'amrih (with request), the debtor's request creates an obligation, but without request there is no obligation.
The surety's action is purely voluntary (tabarru'), and a volunteer cannot later demand compensation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is clear: in kafalah bighayri amrih, the surety cannot recover; in kafalah bi'amrih, he can. This affects financial transactions and guarantees.
Both schools have valid evidence, but Hanafi is the mufta bihi position.

اختیار ہے یہی ایک روایت امام احمد کی ہے۔
امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب مکفول لا نے اپنا قرضہ کفیل سے وصول کیا تو گویا اس نے کفیل کو اپنے قرضہ کے مال کا مالک کر دیا یا مکفول لڑ نے کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے قرضہ کا مال وصول کرنے میں اپنا قائم مقام کر دیا اور ان دونوں صورتوں میں کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے مال واپس لینے کا اختیار ہوگا کیونکہ پہلی صورت میں کفیل بذات خود مالک ہے اور دوسری صورت میں مالک کا قائم مقام ہے اور یہ آپ کو معلوم ہے کہ مالک بھی اپنا مال لے سکتا ہے اور مالک کا قائم مقام بھی لے سکتا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ کفالہ بغیر امرہ کی صورت میں بھی کفیل، مکفول عنہ سے اپنا ادا کیا ہوا مال واپس لے سکتا ہے ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جس پر قرضہ ہو اس کے علاوہ کو قرضہ کا مالک بنانا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں مکفول لہ کی طرف سے کفیل کو ایسی چیز کا مالک بنانا لازم آئے گا جس کے سپرد کرنے پر مکفول لۂ قادر نہیں ہے پس مکفول عنہ جس پر قرضہ ہے اس کے علاوہ کو یعنی لکفیل کو مالک بنانا جائز نہیں ہے اور جب کفیل کو مالک بنانا ہی جائز نہیں ہے تو کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے مطالبہ کرنے کا اختیار کیسے ہو سکتا ہے اور کفالہ بامرہ میں حکم کفالہ کی وجہ سے کفیل کے لئے مکفول عنہ پر اسی طرح مال واجب ہوتا ہے جیسے مکفول لا کے لئے کفیل پر واجب ہوتا ہے ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ کفیل کا حق اس کے ادا کرنے تک مؤخر ہو جاتا ہے یعنی جب کفیل مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے ادا کر دے گا تب کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے مطالبہ کا حق ہوگا اور یہ بات چونکہ کفالہ بغیر مرد میں محق نہیں ہوتی یعنی کفیل کے لئے مکفول عنہ پر مال واجب نہیں ہوتا اس لئے کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے مال کے مطالبہ کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفالہ بغیر امرہ کی صورت میں کفیل مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے قرضہ ادا کرنے میں مکفول عنہ پر احسان اور تبرع کرنے والا ہے اور احسان کرنے والا اپنا احسان واپس لینے کا شرعاً مجاز نہیں ہوتا اس لئے کفالہ بغیر امرہ کی صورت میں اگر کفیل نے مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے قرضہ ادا کر دیا تو اس کو واپس لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا ہے
It is a choice; this is one narration from Imam Ahmad. Imam Malik's proof is that when the principal creditor received his debt from the surety, it is as if he made the surety the owner of the debt's property, or as if the principal creditor appointed the surety as his deputy to recover the debt from the principal debtor. In both cases, the surety will have the right to take back the property from the principal debtor, because in the first case the surety is himself the owner, and in the second case he is the deputy of the owner. And you know that the owner can take his property and the deputy of the owner can also take it. Thus it is established that even in suretyship without request, the surety can recover from the principal debtor the property he paid. Our response to this is that it is not permissible to make someone other than the debtor the owner of the debt, because in that case it would necessitate that the principal creditor makes the surety owner of something which the principal creditor is not capable of handing over. Therefore, it is not permissible to make anyone other than the debtor (i.e., the surety) the owner. And when making the surety owner is not permissible, how can the surety have the right to demand from the principal debtor? In kafalah bi'amrih, due to the ruling of suretyship, the property becomes obligatory upon the principal debtor in favor of the surety just as it was obligatory upon the surety in favor of the principal creditor. However, the surety's right is deferred until he pays: once the surety pays on behalf of the principal debtor, he will have the right to demand from him. But this matter is not established in kafalah bighayri amrih, i.e., the property is not obligatory upon the principal debtor in favor of the surety, so the surety will not have the right to demand the property from the principal debtor. Our proof is that in kafalah bighayri amrih, the surety is doing a favor and gratuitous act towards the principal debtor by paying the debt, and the one who does a favor is not legally authorized to take back his favor. Therefore, in the case of kafalah bighayri amrih, if the surety pays the debt on behalf of the principal debtor, he will not have the right to recover it.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute. It begins by mentioning that it is a choice and one narration from Imam Ahmad. Then it presents Imam Malik's proof for allowing the surety to recover even without the debtor's request. Malik argues by analogy: when the creditor receives payment from the surety, it is as if the creditor made the surety the owner of the debt or his deputy. In either case, the surety can claim from the debtor. The Hanafi response refutes this: making someone other than the debtor the owner of a debt is invalid because the creditor cannot hand over the debt to a non-debtor. In kafalah bi'amrih, the surety's right to recourse is established because the debtor effectively requested the suretyship, creating an obligation on the debtor. But without request, the surety acts voluntarily (mutabarri'), and a volunteer cannot demand reimbursement. The Hanafi proof is that the surety is doing a favor (ihsan) and a favor cannot be taken back. Thus the Hanafi position is that the surety has no right to recover from the debtor without the latter's request.

Key Terms
كفالة بغير أمره (kafalah bighayri amrih): Suretyship undertaken without the request or permission of the principal debtor.
كفالة بأمره (kafalah bi'amrih): Suretyship undertaken at the request or with the permission of the principal debtor.
تبرع (tabarru'): A voluntary, gratuitous act without expectation of compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does a surety who pays a debt without the debtor's request have no right to recover?
A) Because the debtor is not legally required to repay.
B) Because the payment is a gratuitous favor (tabarru') that cannot be taken back.
C) Because the surety must first obtain a court order.
D) Because the debt was not valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a surety who pays without the debtor's request cannot recover because it is a gratuitous payment (tabarru').

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
15 min
Surety Recovers Only What He Guaranteed, Not What He Paid
Explains the ruling and proofs that surety recovers only the guaranteed amount.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on surety's recourse and explain the qiyas (analogy) to gift and inheritance that supports it.

Core Idea
The surety recovers only what he guaranteed, not what he paid, because upon payment he succeeds to the creditor's rights.

In Hanafi fiqh, the surety (kafil) who pays a debt on behalf of the principal debtor (makful 'anhu) has a right of recourse. But the extent of that right depends on what he guaranteed, not what he actually paid. This lesson from al-Hidayah clarifies this rule using clear examples and a juristic analogy. You will learn the proof structure and how it resolves a potential objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi rule: the surety can only recover from the debtor the guaranteed amount (ma daman), not the amount he actually paid (ma adda) if they differ.
2
Study the examples
Work through the three scenarios: bad dirhams vs good, dirham debt vs dinar payment, to see how the rule applies in different facts.
Each example illustrates the principle that the surety's right is tied to the original debt, not his substitute payment.
3
Analyze the proof (qiyas)
Identify the analogy: the surety becomes owner of the debt, stepping into the creditor's shoes, just as a donee or heir who receives the debt by gift or inheritance can only claim the original debt.
The illa (ratio legis) is that the surety becomes the successor (qa'im maqam) of the creditor.
4
Examine the objection and response
Understand the objection: gifting a debt to a non-debtor is invalid. Then see the Hanafi response using istihsan: if the creditor permits possession, the gift is valid, and here such permission is implied.
The objection strengthens the analogy by addressing a potential weakness.
5
Apply to hawalah
Extend the same ruling to hawalah (debt transfer): the transferee who pays a different amount can only recover the original guaranteed amount.
This shows the principle's consistency across related transactions.

صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ متن کے قول رجع بما ادی کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر کفیل اس چیز کو ادا کرے جس کا وہ ضامن ہوا تھا تب تو کفیل مکفول عنہ سے ما ادی کار جوع کرے گا لیکن اگر اس نے جس چیز کا ضامن ہوا تھا اس کے علاوہ دوسری چیز ادا کی تو اس صورت میں کفیل کو مادی واپس لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا بلکہ جس کا ضامن ہوا تھا اسی چیز کو واپس لے سکتا ہے مثلا مکفول عنہ پر کھوٹے در اہم قرضہ ہیں مگر کفیل نے کھرے دراہم ادا کئے تو کفیل مکفول عنہ سے کھوٹے در اہم واپس لینے کا مجاز ہے اور کھرے در اہم لینے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ یا مکفول عنہ پر قرضہ تو کھرے دراہم ہیں مگر کفیل نے مکفول لہ کو کھوٹے در اہم دیئے اور مکفول لڑ نے چشم پوشی کر کے ان کو قبول بھی کر لیا تو کفیل مکفول عنہ سے کھرے دراہم وصول کریگا۔
یا مثلاً مکفول عنہ پر ایک ہزار درہم قرض ہیں اور کفیل نے مکفول لا کو ایک سود دینا ر ادا کر دیئے اور مکفول لڑ نے ان کو قبول بھی کر لیا تو کفیل مکفول عنہ سے ماضمن یعنی ایک ہزار درہم وصول کر لے گا۔ اور ما اوصی یعنی ایک سود بیار واپس لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفیل مکفول عنہ کا قرضہ ادا کرنے سے اس قرضہ کا مالک ہو گیا ہے گویا اس نے مکفول لہ کا یہ مال خرید لیا اور جب کفیل اس قرضہ کامالک ہو گیا جو مکفول عنہ کے ذمہ میں ثابت ہے تو کفیل ، مکفول لہ کا قائم مقام ہوگا اور مکفول لۂ مکفول عنہ سے اس چیز کا مطالبہ کر سکتا ہے جو مکفول عنہ پر واجب ہے پس اسی طرح مکفول لہ کے قائم مقام یعنی کفیل کو بھی اسی چیز کے مطالبہ کا حق ہوگا جو ملفول علنیڈ پر ثابت ہے خواہ اس نے ادا کچھ بھی کیا ہو جیسے فیل ہبہ یا میراث کے ذریعہ اس کا مالک ہو گیا ہو بایں طور کہ مکفول اند نے کفیل کو وہ قرضہ ہبہ کر دیا ہو جو مکفول عنہ کے ذمہ میں ثابت ہے تو کفیل اس قرضہ کا مالک ہو جائے گا اور اس کو اسی کے لینے کا اختیار ہوگا دوسری چیز لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا یا مکفول لہ وفات پا جائے اور کفیل اسکا وارث ہو جائے تو کفیل قرضہ کا مالک ہو جائے گا اور و ہملٹول لہ کے قائم مقام ہو کر مکفول عنہ سے ما ضمن کا رجوع کرے گا یعنی اس چیز کا رجوع کرے گا جس کا وہ ضامن ہوا تھا پس جس طرح ہبہ اور میراث کی صورت میں کفیل قرضہ کا مالک ہونے کی وجہ سے مکفول لز کے قائم مقام ہو کہ مکفول عنہ سے اس چیز کو لے سکتا ہے جو مکفول عنہ پر مکفول لڑ کے لئے واجب تھی اور یہ اس کا ضامن ہوا تھا۔ اسی طرح کفیل مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے قرضہ ادا کرنے کے بعد ائی کو واپس لے سکتا ہے جس کا وہ ضامن ہوا تھا۔
اشکال یہاں ایک اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ کٹیل کے لئے مکفول لیا کی طرف سے قرضہ کو ہبہ کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ قرضہ کو اس شخص کے اسطے ہبہ کرنا تو جائز ہے جس پر قرضہ ہو اور جس پر قرضہ نہ ہو اس کے واسطے ہبہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور کفالہ کی وجہ سے کفیل پر صحیح قول کے مطابق چونکہ مطالبہ لازم ہوتا ہے نہ کہ دین اس لئے کفیل پر قرصہ لازم نہ ہو گا۔ اور جب کفیل پر قرضہ لازم نہیں ہوا تو کٹیل کے لئے مکفول لہ کی طرف سے قرضہ کا ہبہ کرنا بھی درست نہ ہوگا اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ ہبہ ایسی چیز کا صحیح ہوتا ہے جس کے سپرد کرنے پر واہب (بہ کرنے والا ) قادر ہو اور جس کے سپرد کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو اس کا بہ می نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جس شخص پر قرض ہے چونکہ قرض خواہ اس کو قرضہ سپرد کرنے پر قادر ہے اس لئے اس کے واسطے قرضہ کا ہبہ کرنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے ؟ 
جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جس پر قرضہ نہ ہو اس کے واسطے قرضہ کا ہبہ کرنا اس وقت نا جائز ہے جبکہ واہب ( ہبہ کرنے والا ) اس کو قبضہ کی اجازت نہ دے لیکن جب مدیون کے علاوہ کو قرضہ ہبہ کر دیا اور قبضہ کی اجازت دیدی تو یہ استحسانا جائز ہے اور یہاں مسئلہ ہبہ میں جب مکفول لا نے کفیل کے لیے قرضہ ہبہ کیا تو گویا مکفول لانے کفیل کو اس قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کی قدرت دیدی جو قرضہ مکفول عنہ واجب ہے اور جب مکفول لہ نے کفیل کو قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کی قدرت دیدی تو مکفول لیا کی طرف سے قبضہ کی اجازت بھی پائی گئی اور جب مکفول لڑ نے کفیل کو قبضہ کی اجازت دیدی تو ایسا ہو گیا گو یا مکفول لڑ نے کفالہ ختم کر کے کفیل کو قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل بنادیا پھر اس نے قرضہ پر قبضہ کیا پھر مکول لڑ نے اس کو ہبہ کیا تو اب مکفول لن کی طرف قرضہ کا مید اس شخص کے واسطے ہو گا جس پر قرضہ ہے (کفیل) اور یہ جائز ہے۔ کفالہ بامرہ کی صورت میں ادائیگی کدین کے بعد کفیل کے مکفول عنہ سے ما ضمن کے رجوع کا اختیار ہے ما اڈی کے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے ( اس کو جس طرح ہبہ اور میراث کی صورتوں پر قیاس کیا گیا ہے اسی طرح حوالہ کی صورت پر بھی قیاس کیا ہے اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ حامد ( قرضدار) نے اپنے قرض خواہ (شاہد ) کا قرضہ یعنی ایک ہزار درہم خالد کے حوالہ کیا درانحالیکہ خالد (محتال علیہ ) پر حامد یعنی قرضدار کا کوئی قرضہ بھی نہیں ہے پس محتال علیہ یعنی خالد نے شاہد یعنی قرض خواہ کو بجائے ایک ہزار کے بدل دراہم کے دینار دیدئے یا اور کوئی سامان دے دیا اور قرض خواہ نے بخوشی اس کو قبول کر لیا تو اب محتال علیہ یعنی خالد کو ماضمن یعنی ایک ہزار درہم رجوع کرنے
The author of al-Hidayah said: The meaning of the text's statement 'He recovers what he paid' is that if the surety pays the very thing he guaranteed, then he recovers from the principal debtor what he paid. But if he paid something other than what he guaranteed, then in that case the surety has no right to take back what he paid; rather, he can only take back the thing he guaranteed. For example, if the principal debtor owes bad dirhams, but the surety paid good dirhams, then the surety is permitted to take back bad dirhams from the principal debtor, and he is not permitted to take good dirhams. Or if the principal debtor owes good dirhams, but the surety gave bad dirhams to the principal creditor and the creditor turned a blind eye and accepted them, then the surety will recover good dirhams from the principal debtor. Or for example, if the principal debtor owes one thousand dirhams, and the surety paid two hundred dinars to the principal creditor and the creditor accepted them, then the surety will recover from the principal debtor what he guaranteed (ma daman), i.e., one thousand dirhams. And he will not have the right to take back what he paid (ma adda), i.e., the two hundred dinars. The proof for this is that the surety, by paying the principal debtor's debt, has become the owner of that debt, as if he purchased that property from the principal creditor. And when the surety becomes the owner of the debt that is established on the principal debtor, then the surety becomes the successor of the principal creditor. And the principal creditor can demand from the principal debtor that which is obligatory upon him. Similarly, the surety as the successor of the principal creditor will also have the right to demand the same thing that is established on the principal debtor, regardless of what he paid, just as if he had become the owner of it through gift or inheritance. For example, if the principal creditor gifted to the surety the debt that is on the principal debtor, then the surety becomes the owner of that debt and he has the right to take that same thing, not something else. Or if the principal creditor dies and the surety becomes his heir, then the surety becomes the owner of the debt, and he will recover from the principal debtor what he guaranteed (ma daman), i.e., the thing he was surety for. So just as in the case of gift and inheritance, the surety, being the owner of the debt, becomes the successor of the principal creditor and can take from the principal debtor that which was owed to the principal creditor and which the surety guaranteed, similarly, after the surety pays the debt on behalf of the principal debtor, he can take back that which he guaranteed. Objection: There is an objection here: that it is not valid for the principal creditor to make a gift of the debt to the surety, because a debt can only be gifted to the person who owes it (the debtor), not to someone else. And according to the correct opinion, due to suretyship, what becomes obligatory on the surety is the demand (mutalaba) not the debt itself, so the debt does not become obligatory on the surety. And when the debt has not become obligatory on the surety, then it is not valid for the principal creditor to gift the debt to the surety. The reason is that a gift is valid only for something that the giver is capable of handing over. If he is not capable, the gift is not valid. Now, since the creditor is capable of handing over the debt to the debtor (because the debtor can pay it), but the surety is not a debtor, so how can the gift be valid? Reply: The reply is that gifting a debt to someone who is not the debtor is impermissible only when the giver does not grant permission to take possession. But when the debt is gifted to someone other than the debtor and permission to take possession is given, then it is valid by istihsan. In this case of gift, when the principal creditor gifts the debt to the surety, it is as if the principal creditor gave the surety the power to take possession of the debt that is owed by the principal debtor. And when the principal creditor gave the surety the power to take possession, permission for possession is found. When the principal creditor gave permission to take possession, it is as if the principal creditor terminated the suretyship and appointed the surety as his agent to take possession of the debt. Then he took possession of the debt, and then the principal creditor gifted it to him. So now the debt is due from the principal debtor to the surety, and this is valid. In kafalah bi'amrih, after payment, the surety has the right to recover from the principal debtor what he guaranteed (ma daman), not what he paid (ma adda). Just as analogy was made to gift and inheritance, similarly analogy is made to the case of hawalah (transfer of debt). The example is: Hamid (the debtor) transferred his debt of one thousand dirhams owed to Shahid (the creditor) to Khalid (the transferee) while Khalid did not owe anything to Hamid. Then Khalid paid Shahid dinars or other goods instead of dirhams, and Shahid accepted. Then Khalid can recover from Hamid only the amount he guaranteed (ma daman) i.e., one thousand dirhams.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the matn's statement 'رجع بما أدی' from the Hidayah. The commentator clarifies that this means the surety recovers what he guaranteed, not necessarily what he physically paid if he paid something different. Examples illustrate: if the debtor owed bad dirhams and the surety paid good dirhams, he can only claim bad dirhams from the debtor. The proof is that by paying, the surety becomes the owner of the debt owed to the creditor, stepping into the creditor's shoes. He can then only claim what was originally owed, just as if he received the debt through gift or inheritance. An objection arises: is it valid to gift a debt to a non-debtor? The reply uses istihsan: if the creditor gives permission to take possession, the gift is valid, and here the creditor's act of gifting implies such permission. Thus the analogy holds. The passage also extends the analogy to hawalah (transfer of debt), where the transferee who pays something different can also only recover the guaranteed amount.

Key Terms
ما ضمن (ma daman): The specific thing (e.g., amount or quality) that the surety guaranteed to pay.
ما أدي (ma adda): The actual property or amount that the surety paid to the creditor, which may differ from the guaranteed thing.
قيام مقام (qiyam maqam): Standing in the place of another; legal succession to rights.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from a clear analogy for a stronger legal reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a surety pays the creditor in a different form than the debt (e.g., pays dinars for a dirham debt), what can he recover from the debtor?
A) The dinars he paid
B) The equivalent value in dirhams
C) The original dirham debt that he guaranteed
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The surety's payment transfers ownership of the debt to him, allowing recovery only of the original debt, not the substitute payment.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
Hiba of Debt to the Surety and the Role of Istihsan
Ruling on kafil becoming owner of debt through hiba or inheritance and subsequent right to demand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on hiba of a debt to a surety and apply the principle of istihsan to override qiyas in such cases.

Core Idea
Hiba of a debt to a non-debtor is valid by istihsan when the donor permits possession.

You have learned that the surety (kafil) can become owner of the debt through a gift from the creditor or through inheritance. But a natural objection arises: gifting a debt to someone who does not owe it is normally invalid because the donor cannot hand over possession. The Hanafi school uses istihsan—juristic preference—to permit this when the creditor grants permission to collect. This lesson walks through the objection and its resolution, showing how Hanafi legal reasoning works.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on kafil's ownership via hiba or inheritance
Identify that when the creditor gifts the debt to the surety, or the surety inherits it, the surety becomes the owner and can demand the exact debt from the principal debtor.
The surety steps into the creditor's shoes.
2
Recognize the qiyas-based objection
Understand why a strict analogy (qiyas) would declare this hiba invalid: hiba of a debt to a non-debtor is normally invalid because the donor cannot hand over possession; the surety is not the debtor, so the gift should be void.
The objection relies on the rule that hiba requires physical handover.
3
See how istihsan overrides the qiyas
The Hanafi response uses istihsan: when the creditor gives permission for the surety to take possession, the surety becomes able to collect through the principal debtor, making the hiba valid.
Istihsan allows a departure from qiyas for a stronger reason.
4
Analyze the agency analogy
The text explains that by granting permission, the creditor effectively makes the surety an agent to collect the debt, then gifts it after collection, so the debtor becomes the surety's debtor.
This resolves the handover problem.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi position
The operative ruling is that the hiba is valid with permission. This is the position relied upon in fatwa.
It illustrates the Hanafi method of balancing textual rules with practical needs.

قرضہ کامالک ہو گیا جو مکفول عنہ کے ذمہ میں ثابت ہے تو کفیل ، مکفول لہ کا قائم مقام ہوگا اور مکفول لۂ مکفول عنہ سے اس چیز کا مطالبہ کر سکتا ہے جو مکفول عنہ پر واجب ہے پس اسی طرح مکفول لہ کے قائم مقام یعنی کفیل کو بھی اسی چیز کے مطالبہ کا حق ہوگا جو ملفول علنیڈ پر ثابت ہے خواہ اس نے ادا کچھ بھی کیا ہو جیسے فیل ہبہ یا میراث کے ذریعہ اس کا مالک ہو گیا ہو بایں طور کہ مکفول اند نے کفیل کو وہ قرضہ ہبہ کر دیا ہو جو مکفول عنہ کے ذمہ میں ثابت ہے تو کفیل اس قرضہ کا مالک ہو جائے گا اور اس کو اسی کے لینے کا اختیار ہوگا دوسری چیز لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا یا مکفول لہ وفات پا جائے اور کفیل اسکا وارث ہو جائے تو کفیل قرضہ کا مالک ہو جائے گا اور و ہملٹول لہ کے قائم مقام ہو کر مکفول عنہ سے ما ضمن کا رجوع کرے گا یعنی اس چیز کا رجوع کرے گا جس کا وہ ضامن ہوا تھا پس جس طرح ہبہ اور میراث کی صورت میں کفیل قرضہ کا مالک ہونے کی وجہ سے مکفول لز کے قائم مقام ہو کہ مکفول عنہ سے اس چیز کو لے سکتا ہے جو مکفول عنہ پر مکفول لڑ کے لئے واجب تھی اور یہ اس کا ضامن ہوا تھا۔ اسی طرح کفیل مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے قرضہ ادا کرنے کے بعد ائی کو واپس لے سکتا ہے جس کا وہ ضامن ہوا تھا۔
اشکال یہاں ایک اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ کٹیل کے لئے مکفول لیا کی طرف سے قرضہ کو ہبہ کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ قرضہ کو اس شخص کے اسطے ہبہ کرنا تو جائز ہے جس پر قرضہ ہو اور جس پر قرضہ نہ ہو اس کے واسطے ہبہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور کفالہ کی وجہ سے کفیل پر صحیح قول کے مطابق چونکہ مطالبہ لازم ہوتا ہے نہ کہ دین اس لئے کفیل پر قرصہ لازم نہ ہو گا۔ اور جب کفیل پر قرضہ لازم نہیں ہوا تو کٹیل کے لئے مکفول لہ کی طرف سے قرضہ کا ہبہ کرنا بھی درست نہ ہوگا اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ ہبہ ایسی چیز کا صحیح ہوتا ہے جس کے سپرد کرنے پر واہب (بہ کرنے والا ) قادر ہو اور جس کے سپرد کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو اس کا بہ می نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جس شخص پر قرض ہے چونکہ قرض خواہ اس کو قرضہ سپرد کرنے پر قادر ہے اس لئے اس کے واسطے قرضہ کا ہبہ کرنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے ؟
جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جس پر قرضہ نہ ہو اس کے واسطے قرضہ کا ہبہ کرنا اس وقت نا جائز ہے جبکہ واہب ( ہبہ کرنے والا ) اس کو قبضہ کی اجازت نہ دے لیکن جب مدیون کے علاوہ کو قرضہ ہبہ کر دیا اور قبضہ کی اجازت دیدی تو یہ استحسانا جائز ہے اور یہاں مسئلہ ہبہ میں جب مکفول لا نے کفیل کے لیے قرضہ ہبہ کیا تو گویا مکفول لانے کفیل کو اس قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کی قدرت دیدی جو قرضہ مکفول عنہ واجب ہے اور جب مکفول لہ نے کفیل کو قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کی قدرت دیدی تو مکفول لیا کی طرف سے قبضہ کی اجازت بھی پائی گئی اور جب مکفول لڑ نے کفیل کو قبضہ کی اجازت دیدی تو ایسا ہو گیا گو یا مکفول لڑ نے کفالہ ختم کر کے کفیل کو قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل بنادیا پھر اس نے قرضہ پر قبضہ کیا پھر مکول لڑ نے اس کو ہبہ کیا تو اب مکفول لن کی طرف قرضہ کا مید اس شخص کے واسطے ہو گا جس پر قرضہ ہے (کفیل) اور یہ جائز ہے۔
The debt became the property of the one who is established as due from the principal debtor, so the surety will be the representative of the creditor, and the creditor can demand from the principal debtor that thing which is obligatory upon the principal debtor. Similarly, the surety who is the representative of the creditor will also have the right to demand that same thing which is established upon the principal debtor, even if he has paid something, like if he became owner through hiba or inheritance in such a way that the creditor gifted to the surety that debt which is established upon the principal debtor, then the surety becomes owner of that debt and will have the authority to take that same thing, not another thing. Or if the creditor dies and the surety becomes his heir, then the surety becomes owner of the debt and, as the representative of the creditor, will revert to the principal debtor for what he guaranteed, i.e., he will revert for that thing of which he was guarantor. Just as in the case of hiba and inheritance, the surety, due to being owner of the debt, becomes the representative of the creditor so that he can take from the principal debtor that thing which was obligatory upon the principal debtor for the creditor and of which he was guarantor. Similarly, the surety, after paying the debt on behalf of the principal debtor, can take back that which he guaranteed.
Objection: There is an objection here, and that is that for the surety, the creditor gifting the debt is not valid, because gifting a debt to the person on whom the debt is due is valid, but gifting it to one on whom the debt is not due is not valid. And due to suretyship, according to the correct opinion, demand becomes necessary not the debt, so the debt will not be necessary upon the surety. And when the debt is not necessary upon the surety, then for the surety, the creditor gifting the debt will also not be valid. The reason for this is that hiba is valid for a thing over which the donor has power to hand over, and for a thing over which he does not have power to hand over, hiba is not valid. So since the creditor has power to hand over the debt to the person on whom the debt is due, therefore gifting the debt to him is valid, but to the surety who does not owe it, it is not valid?
Answer: The answer is that gifting a debt to one on whom the debt is not due is invalid when the donor does not give permission for possession. But when he gifts the debt to someone other than the debtor and gives permission for possession, then it is valid by istihsan. And here in the matter of hiba, when the creditor gifted the debt to the surety, it is as if the creditor gave the surety power to take possession of that debt which is obligatory upon the principal debtor. And when the creditor gave the surety power to take possession of the debt, then permission for possession from the creditor is also obtained. And when the creditor gave the surety permission for possession, it is as if the creditor ended the suretyship and made the surety an agent to take possession of the debt, then he took possession of the debt, then the creditor gifted it to him. So now from the creditor, the debt becomes due for the person on whom the debt is (i.e., the surety), and this is valid.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on the surety's right to claim the debt after becoming its owner through hiba (gift) or inheritance. It first states that if the creditor (makful lah) transfers ownership of the debt to the surety (kafil) either by gifting it or through inheritance (if the surety inherits from the creditor), the surety steps into the creditor's shoes and can demand the exact debt from the principal debtor (makful 'anhu), not something else. Similarly, after the surety pays the debt, he can also revert to the principal for the exact amount he guaranteed (ma daman).
Then an objection is raised: gifting a debt to a non-debtor is usually invalid because the donor cannot hand over possession; the surety is not the debtor, so the hiba should be invalid. The response uses istihsan (juristic preference) to permit the hiba when the donor gives explicit permission for the donee to take possession. By granting permission, the creditor effectively makes the surety an agent to collect the debt from the principal and then gifts it, so the surety becomes the debtor's creditor. This analysis shows the Hanafi method of reconciling strict qiyas (analogy) with practical necessity through istihsan.

Key Terms
کفیل (kafil): The surety/guarantor who is liable for the debt of the principal debtor.
مکفول لہ (makful lah): The creditor who is owed the debt from the principal debtor.
مکفول عنہ (makful 'anhu): The principal debtor for whom the surety guarantees.
ہبہ (hiba): A gift; transfer of ownership without compensation.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrules qiyas for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is hiba of a debt to a non-debtor valid?
A) Always valid
B) Valid only if the donee is the debtor
C) Valid if the donor permits the donee to take possession
D) Never valid

Key Takeaway
Hiba of a debt to a surety is valid by istihsan when the creditor grants permission for possession, illustrating how Hanafi fiqh balances strict analogy with practical necessity.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
Kafil bi-Amrihi Only Reverts for Guaranteed Amount, Not What Was Actually Paid
Ruling with proof via qiyas and critical refinement distinguishing kafil from ma'mur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for kafil bi-amrihi regarding the surety's right to revert, and distinguish it from the case of ma'mur bi qada' al-dayn using the principle of ownership transfer.

Core Idea
The surety with command (kafil bi-amrihi) becomes owner of the debt upon payment and can only reclaim the guaranteed amount.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi contract law: what a surety can reclaim after paying off the principal's debt. The text clarifies that a kafil bi-amrihi is entitled only to the guaranteed amount (ma daman), not any extra he paid. This is based on the principle that paying a debt under obligation transfers ownership of the debt itself. The passage contrasts this with a voluntary agent (ma'mur) who does not become owner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific ruling for kafalah bi-amrihi? The surety can only reclaim the guaranteed amount (ma daman), not what he actually paid (ma adda).
This is the core rule.
2
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
The text uses qiyas to hawala (transfer of debt): just as the person to whom debt is transferred becomes owner of the debt and can only claim the original amount, so too the surety.
Also uses qiyas to hiba and inheritance, but hawala is detailed.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal reasoning)
Both in hawala and kafalah, the payer becomes owner of the debt upon payment and stands in the creditor's shoes. Therefore, the payer's right is limited to what the creditor could claim.
This is based on the principle of ownership transfer (milkiyyah).
4
Address the counter-argument (objection)
An objector equates the kafil with a ma'mur bi qada' al-dayn. Both act by command. But the response distinguishes: the ma'mur is not obligated; he pays voluntarily, so he does not become owner and can reclaim whatever he actually paid.
This highlights the difference between obligatory (wajib) and voluntary (tabarru') payment.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi position
Thus, the Hanafi position is that the surety's right is limited to the guaranteed amount. This is a mufta bihi ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.
A refinement from 'Inayah notes that even the ma'mur's right is conditional: he cannot reclaim more than ordered.

کفالہ بامرہ کی صورت میں ادائیگی کدین کے بعد کفیل کے مکفول عنہ سے ما ضمن کے رجوع کا اختیار ہے ما اڈی کے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے ( اس کو جس طرح ہبہ اور میراث کی صورتوں پر قیاس کیا گیا ہے اسی طرح حوالہ کی صورت پر بھی قیاس کیا ہے اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ حامد ( قرضدار) نے اپنے قرض خواہ (شاہد ) کا قرضہ یعنی ایک ہزار درہم خالد کے حوالہ کیا درانحالیکہ خالد (محتال علیہ ) پر حامد یعنی قرضدار کا کوئی قرضہ بھی نہیں ہے پس محتال علیہ یعنی خالد نے شاہد یعنی قرض خواہ کو بجائے ایک ہزار کے بدل دراہم کے دینار دیدئے یا اور کوئی سامان دے دیا اور قرض خواہ نے بخوشی اس کو قبول کر لیا تو اب محتال علیہ یعنی خالد کو ماضمن یعنی ایک ہزار درہم رجوع کرنے کا اختیار ہے ما ادی (جوادا کیا ) رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ محتال علیہ ادا کرنے سے دین کا مالک ہو گیا ہے اور جب محتال علیہ، دین کا مالک ہو گیا تو یہ متال لہیعنی قرض خواہ کے قائم مقام ہوگا اور چونکہ قرض خواہ کو اپنا قرض یعنی ایک ہزار درہم لینے کا اختیار تھا۔ لہذا اس کے قائم مقام یعنی محتال علیہ کو بھی ایک ہزار درہم لینے کا اختیار ہو گا۔ اسی طرح کفیل کو اپنے مکفول عنہ سے ماضمن کے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا اور ما ادمی کے رجوع کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ بخلاف المامورتے ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے قرضہ واپس لینے کا اختیار اسی وقت ہوتا ہے جبکہ کفیل نے مکفول عنہ کے حکم سے قرضہ ادا کیا ہو۔ اور اس وقت کفیل بامرہ اور مامور بقضاء الدین میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مامور بقضاء الدین بھی قرضدار کے حکم سے قرضہ ادا کرتا ہے اور کفیل با مرد بھی قرضدار یعنی مکفول عنہ کے حکم سے قرضہ ادا کرتا ہے اور مامور بقضاء الدین قرینہ ادا کرنے کے بعد قرضدار سے ماادی ( جو کچھ ادا کیا گیا ) کو واپس لینے کا مجاز ہے خواہ ما ادی وہ ہو جو قرضدار پر قرض تھا یا اس کے علاوہ ہو ۔ پس اسی طرح کفیل کو بھی ما ادی واپس لینے کا اختیار ہونا چاہیے تھا خواہ ما ادی وہی ہو جس کا ضامن ہوا تھا خواہ اس کے علاوہ ہو۔ حالانکہ آپ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر ماادی، ماضمن کے خلاف ہو تو کفیل ماضمن (جس کا کفیل ہوا تھا ) واپس لے سکتا ہے اس کو ما ادی واپس لینے کا اختیار نہیں ہوتا ؟
جواب .. اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مامور بقضاء الدین پر کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہے بلکہ اس نے اپنی خوشی سے بطور احسان یہ کام منظور کیا ہے تو مامور بقضاء الدین قرضہ ادا کرنے سے قرضہ کا مالک نہیں ہوگا اور جب مامور بقضاء الدین ، قرضہ کا مالک نہیں ہوا تو وہ طالب یعنی قرض خواہ کے قائم مقام بھی نہیں ہوا اور جب قرض خواہ کے قائم مقام نہیں ہوا تو جو قرضدار پر واجب تھا اس کو لینے کا مجاز بھی نہ ہوگا بلکہ جو کچھ اس نے ادا کیا ہے اس کو واپس لے سکتا ہے اور رہا کفیل با مرہ تو وہ کغالہ کی وجہ سے اپنے او پر مال قرض کا ادا کرنا لازم کرتا ہے اور جب کفیل پر مال قرض کا ادا کرنالازم ہے تو کفیل قرض ادا کرنے کے بعد اس قرض کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ اور قرض کا مالک ہو کر مکفول را یعنی قرض خواہ کے قائم مقام ہوگا پس جس طرح مکفول ایا کو اسی چیز کے مطالبہ کا حق ہے جو قرضدار یعنی مکفول عنہ کے ذمہ میں ثابت ہے۔ اسی طرح کفیل کو بھی مکفول عنہ سے اس چیز کے لینے کا اختیار ہے جو قرضدار یعنی مکفول عنہ پر واجب ہے اور کفیل اس کا ضامن ہوا ہے ما ادی و غیر ہ دوسری چیز لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ حاصل یہ کہ فیل بامرہ اور مامور بقضاء الدین میں بہت بڑا فرق ہے اور فرق کے ساتھ قیاس درست نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا کھیل بامرہ کو مامور بقضاءالدین پر قیاس کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب عنایہ کے لکھنے کے مطابق ہدایہ کی عبارت حيث يرجع بما ادی کے اطلاق میں تسامح ہے کیونکہ عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مامور بقضاء الدین ہر صورت میں مادی رجوع کرے گا حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ اگر مودی ( جو ادا کیا گیا ) مامور بہ کے مانند ہو یا اس سے کم تر ہو تب تو ما ادی رجوع کرے گا اور اگر مؤدی مامور بہ سے بڑھ کر ہو تو مامور بہ کو واپس لے گاما اونٹی واپس نہ لے گا مثلاً قرضدار پردرا ہم زیوف کا قرضہ ہے مگر مامور بقضاء الدین نے دراہم زیوف کی جگہ دراہم جیا د ادا کر دیئے تو وہ قرضدار سے دراہم زیوف واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ وصف جودت جو قرضہ سے زائد ایک چیز ہے اس کو ادا کرنے میں مامور بقضاء الدین متبرع ہے اور متبرع کو رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ درا ہم جیا د واپس نہیں لے سکتا صرف در اہم زیوف واپس لے سکتا ہے حالانکہ مادی
In the case of suretyship with command (kafalah bi-amrihi), after payment of the debt, the surety has the option to revert to the principal debtor for the guaranteed amount (ma daman), not for what he actually paid (ma adda). Just as this was analogized to the cases of hiba and inheritance, similarly it is analogized to the case of hawala (transfer of debt). Its scenario is: Hamid (debtor) transferred his debt of one thousand dirhams to Khalid (the person to whom debt is transferred) while Khalid is not owing anything to Hamid. Then Khalid gave the creditor (Shahid) dinars instead of dirhams, or some other goods, and the creditor willingly accepted. Now Khalid has the right to revert for the guaranteed amount (one thousand dirhams), not for what he actually paid. Because Khalid became owner of the debt by paying, and when he became owner, he becomes the representative of the creditor. And since the creditor had the right to take his debt (one thousand dirhams), therefore his representative Khalid also has the right to take one thousand dirhams. Similarly, the surety has the right to revert to his principal for the guaranteed amount, not for what he paid. This is contrary to the case of the one commanded (ma'mur). This is the answer to an implied question.
Question: The surety has the right to take back the debt from the principal only when he paid by the principal's command. At that time, there is no difference between the surety with command (kafil bi-amrihi) and the one commanded to pay the debt (ma'mur bi qada' al-dayn). Because the one commanded also pays the debt by the debtor's command, and the surety with command also pays by the debtor's command. And the one commanded, after paying, is authorized to take back from the debtor what he paid, whether that be the debt due or something else. So similarly, the surety should also have the right to take back what he paid, whether it be the guaranteed amount or something else. But you (the author) have said that if what he paid differs from the guaranteed amount, the surety can take back the guaranteed amount, not what he paid. Why?
Answer: The answer is that nothing is obligatory upon the one commanded; rather, he undertook this act voluntarily as a favor. So the one commanded does not become owner of the debt by paying it. And when he is not owner, he does not become the representative of the creditor. And when he is not the representative, he is not authorized to take what was owed to the creditor; rather, he can take back what he actually paid. As for the surety with command, he makes payment of the debt obligatory upon himself due to suretyship. And when payment is obligatory upon him, after paying he becomes owner of that debt. And by becoming owner, he becomes the representative of the creditor. So just as the creditor has the right to demand that very thing which is established upon the debtor, similarly the surety has the right to take from the principal that thing which was obligatory upon the debtor and which he guaranteed; he does not have the right to take what he actually paid or something else. The conclusion is that there is a great difference between the surety with command and the one commanded, and qiyas cannot be made when there is a difference. Therefore, analogizing the surety with command to the one commanded is incorrect.
According to the author of 'Inayah, the wording of Hidayah 'where yarji'u bima adda' (he reverts with what he paid) is ambiguous, because from the wording it appears that the one commanded will in all cases revert with what he paid, but that is not so. Rather, if what he paid is similar to or less than what was commanded, then he reverts with what he paid; but if what he paid exceeds what was commanded, then he takes back the commanded amount, not the excess. For example, the debtor owes dirhams of low quality, but the one commanded paid high-quality dirhams instead. Then he can take back low-quality dirhams from the debtor, because the quality of goodness is an extra thing beyond the debt; in paying it, the one commanded is a volunteer (mutabarri'), and a volunteer has no right to revert. So he cannot take back the high-quality dirhams; he can only take back the low-quality dirhams, even though the actual payment was
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling for kafalah bi-amrihi (suretyship with the principal's command). The core rule: after paying, the surety can only claim from the principal debtor the exact amount he guaranteed (ma daman), not any surplus he actually paid (ma adda). The text draws an analogy to hawala (transfer of debt): when a person discharges another's debt with a different commodity and the creditor accepts, the discharge becomes owner of the original debt and can only claim that. The passage then addresses a potential confusion: the difference between a surety with command (kafil bi-amrihi) and a mere agent commanded to pay a debt (ma'mur bi qada' al-dayn). An objector argues they are similar because both act by the debtor's command. The reply distinguishes: the agent is not bound to pay; he does it voluntarily, so he does not become owner of the debt and can reclaim exactly what he paid. The surety, however, has a binding obligation (due to suretyship), so he becomes owner of the debt upon payment and steps into the creditor's shoes, entitled only to what was owed—the guaranteed amount. A final note from 'Inayah refines the Hidayah's phrasing: the agent's right to reclaim what he paid is conditional—if he paid more than ordered, he can only claim the ordered amount; if less or equal, he can claim the actual payment. This highlights the Hanafi method of precise legal distinctions and the use of analogy (qiyas) and istihsan.

Key Terms
کفالہ بامرہ (kafalah bi-amrihi): Suretyship with the command of the principal debtor; the surety pays at the debtor's request.
مضمن (ma daman): The specific debt amount that the surety guaranteed.
ما ادی (ma adda): The amount or goods actually paid by the surety/agent.
مامور بقضاء الدین (ma'mur bi qada' al-dayn): A person commanded to pay off a debt; acts voluntarily without obligation.
حوالہ (hawala): Transfer of debt from one debtor to another with the creditor's consent.

C) The difference between what he paid and the guaranteed amount
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In kafalah bi-amrihi, the surety's right to reclaim is strictly limited to the guaranteed amount because he becomes owner of the debt and stands in the creditor's shoes.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
The Kafil's Right to Recover Only Madmin
Explains the general rule of kafil's recourse and the distinction from ma'mur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a kafil can only recover the guaranteed amount (madmin) from the principal debtor, and explain why the kafil bi-amrihi differs from the ma'mur bi qada al-dayn.

Core Idea
A kafil recovers only madmin; the kafil becomes owner of the debt, unlike a volunteer payer.

In this lesson, we examine the fundamental rule in Hanafi kafalah: the kafil (guarantor) who pays the debt by order of the principal debtor can only recover the specific amount for which he stood surety (madmin), not any other amount he may have paid. This rule is clarified by distinguishing the kafil bi-amrihi from the ma'mur bi qada al-dayn (a person ordered to repay). Understanding this distinction is key to correctly applying the principle of recourse.

Guided Path
1
State the General Rule
Identify the ruling: The kafil can recover from the makful 'anhu only the guaranteed amount (madmin), not any other amount paid (ma adi) that differs.
2
Understand the Objection
Consider the hypothetical objection: Since the ma'mur bi qada al-dayn can recover whatever he pays, why can't the kafil do the same? Both act by order of the debtor.
This objection is based on apparent analogy (qiyas).
3
Analyze the Hanafi Response
Examine the key distinction: The ma'mur pays voluntarily without legal obligation; he does not become owner of the debt. The kafil bi-amrihi, however, is legally obliged to pay due to his guarantee; after payment, he becomes owner and steps into the creditor's shoes.
The kafil's obligation (luzum) arises from the contract of kafalah.
4
Derive the Consequence
Because the kafil becomes owner, he can only recover what was originally owed (the debt itself, i.e., madmin), not an excess. The ma'mur, not being owner, can only take back his actual payment.
The difference in legal status (owner vs. non-owner) invalidates the analogy.

Book of Kafalah. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 9. He does not have the option to recover what was paid (ma adi). Because the assignee (muhtal alayh) becomes owner of the debt by paying, and when he becomes owner, he stands in the place of the creditor. Since the creditor had the right to take his debt of one thousand dirhams, so his substitute (the assignee) also has the right to take one thousand dirhams. Similarly, the kafil has the right to recover from his makful anhu the guaranteed amount (madmin), and not the amount paid (ma adi). Except the ma'mur. This is the answer to a presumed question. The question is: The kafil only has the right to take back the debt from the makful anhu when he paid by the order of the makful anhu. At that time, there is no difference between the kafil bi-amrihi and the ma'mur bi qada al-dayn. Because the ma'mur also pays by the order of the debtor, and the kafil bi-amrihi also pays by the order of the debtor (the makful anhu). The ma'mur bi qada al-dayn, after paying, is entitled to take back from the debtor what he paid (ma adi), whether that paid amount is the same as the debtor's debt or different. So similarly, the kafil should have had the right to take back ma adi, whether it is the same as that for which he was surety or different. Yet you have stated that if ma adi differs from madmin, the kafil can take back madmin (that for which he was surety), and he does not have the right to take back ma adi. The answer: The answer is that the ma'mur bi qada al-dayn is not obliged to pay anything; rather, he voluntarily accepted this task as a favor. So the ma'mur does not become owner of the debt by paying it. When he does not become owner, he does not stand in place of the creditor. When he does not stand in place, he is not entitled to take what was owed to the debtor, but he can only take back what he actually paid. As for the kafil bi-amrihi, he makes it obligatory upon himself to pay the debt due to the suretyship. When it is obligatory for the kafil to pay, then after paying, he becomes owner of the debt. After becoming owner, he stands in place of the creditor. So just as the creditor has the right to demand exactly what is established as a debt upon the debtor (the makful anhu), similarly the kafil has the right to take from the makful anhu exactly what was owed and for which he was surety. He does not have the right to take something else (ma adi other than madmin). The conclusion is that there is a great difference between the kafil bi-amrihi and the ma'mur bi qada al-dayn, and with a difference, analogy is not valid. Therefore, analogizing the kafil bi-amrihi to the ma'mur is incorrect. According to Sahib al-'Inayah, the Hidayah's expression 'where he recovers what he paid' is imprecise in its generality, because the expression suggests that the ma'mur recovers ma adi in all cases, but it is not so. Rather, if the paid amount (mu'addi) is like the commanded amount or less, then he recovers ma adi; but if the paid amount exceeds the commanded amount, he takes back the commanded amount and not the excess. For example, if the debtor owes bad dirhams (zuyuf), but the ma'mur pays good dirhams (jiyad) instead of the bad ones, then he can take back bad dirhams from the debtor. Because the quality of goodness (wasf al-jawdah) is an extra thing beyond the debt; in paying it, the ma'mur is a volunteer (mutabarri'), and a volunteer does not have the right of recourse. Therefore, he cannot take back the good dirhams, only the bad ones, even though what he paid was good dirhams, not bad. Thus, it is known that the Hidayah's expression 'where he recovers what he paid' is not correct absolutely. The author of Hidayah says: If the debt amount is one thousand dirhams, but the kafil made a reconciliation (sulh) with the creditor (makful lah) for five hundred dirhams, then in that case the kafil can recover from the makful anhu what he paid, i.e., five hundred dirhams, and he does not have the right to recover the guaranteed amount, i.e., one thousand dirhams. Because the meaning of reconciliation for five hundred dirhams is that the creditor has discharged the kafil for five hundred dirhams. Discharge is like the creditor cancelling five hundred dirhams of the debt. In that cancelled amount, the kafil does not have the right of recourse. Therefore, in the mentioned case of reconciliation, the kafil can take five hundred dirhams from the makful anhu, and it is as if the creditor discharged the kafil. So if the creditor discharges the kafil from the entire debt, then the kafil has absolutely no right of recourse against the makful anhu. And if he discharges him from a part, then the kafil can take from the makful anhu the amount he pays. Similarly, in the case of reconciliation, the kafil can take from the makful anhu only the amount he pays.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of kafalah (suretyship) regarding the kafil's right of recourse (ruju') against the principal debtor (makful 'anhu). It opens by stating the general rule that the kafil can only recover the specific amount for which he was surety (madmin), not any other amount he may have paid (ma adi) if it differs. The text then addresses a potential objection: why the distinction between a kafil bi-amrihi (guarantor by order of the debtor) and a ma'mur bi qada al-dayn (a person ordered to repay a debt)? The answer is that the ma'mur pays voluntarily without any legal obligation on him, so he does not become the owner of the debt; therefore, he can only recover what he actually paid. In contrast, the kafil bi-amrihi is legally obliged to pay due to his guarantee, so after payment, he becomes the owner of the debt and steps into the position of the creditor, allowing him to recover only the original debt, not any excess. The passage then refines this principle by criticizing the Hidayah's phrasing 'where he recovers what he paid' as too general, giving the example of paying better quality coins than owed. Finally, it discusses the effect of sulh (reconciliation) between the kafil and the creditor, where the kafil recovers only the amount he actually paid, not the full guaranteed amount, because the reconciliation effectively reduces the debt.

Key Terms
كفيل (kafil): The guarantor or surety who undertakes to pay the debt of another (makful 'anhu) to the creditor (makful lah).
مكفول عنه (makful 'anhu): The principal debtor on whose behalf the kafil pays the debt.
مضمن (madmin): The specific amount or obligation for which the kafil becomes surety; the guaranteed debt.
ما أدى (ma adi): The actual amount paid by the kafil to the creditor, which may be equal to, less than, or more than the guaranteed amount.
كفيل بالأمر (kafil bi-amrihi): A guarantor who pays by the order of the principal debtor, thus having legal right to recourse.
مأمور بقضاء الدين (ma'mur bi qada al-dayn): A person ordered to repay a debt, who pays voluntarily without being legally obligated, and thus does not become owner of the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi rule in this lesson, what does a kafil recover from the principal debtor if he pays exactly the guaranteed amount?
A) The guaranteed amount (madmin)
B) The amount paid (ma adi) regardless
C) Nothing
D) Twice the guaranteed amount

Key Takeaway
A kafil bi-amrihi recovers only the guaranteed amount (madmin), as he becomes owner of the debt, unlike a voluntary payer.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate

Effect of Sulh and Refinement on Kafil's Recourse
Refines the recourse rule: quality differences and sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the refined rule regarding quality differences in payment and explain how sulh affects the kafil's right of recourse.

Core Idea
Sulh reduces the debt; the kafil recovers only what he pays, not the original guaranteed amount.

This lesson builds on the general rule by examining two refinements. First, we address the imprecision in the Hidayah's phrasing that a ma'mur always recovers what he paid; we correct it with the example of paying better quality dirhams. Second, we explore the effect of sulh (reconciliation) between the kafil and the creditor, which reduces the kafil's recourse to the amount actually paid, not the original guaranteed amount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Imprecision in Hidayah
Recognize that the Hidayah's statement 'where he recovers what he paid' is too general. The ma'mur does not always recover ma adi if the paid amount exceeds the commanded amount.
This correction is from Sahib al-'Inayah.
2
Analyze the Quality Example
Work through the example: the debtor owes bad dirhams, but the ma'mur pays good dirhams. He can only recover the value of bad dirhams because the extra quality is a voluntary gift (tabarru').
The ma'mur is a volunteer for the excess; a volunteer has no right of recourse.
3
Understand the Sulh Scenario
Examine the case where the kafil settles with the creditor for less than the guaranteed amount (e.g., sulh for 500 on a 1000 debt). This discharge reduces the debt; the kafil recovers only what he actually paid.
Sulh is treated as partial discharge (ibra) by the creditor.
4
Apply the Principle to Full Discharge
If the creditor fully discharges the kafil, the kafil has no recourse at all because the debt is cancelled. If partial, recourse equals the paid amount.
This follows from the principle that the kafil steps into the creditor's shoes; if the creditor cancels the debt, there is nothing to recover.

اشرف البدایہ جلد 9
ما ادی (جوادا کیا) رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ محتال علیہ ادا کرنے سے دین کا مالک ہو گیا ہے اور جب محتال علیہ، دین کا مالک ہو گیا تو یہ متال لہ یعنی قرض خواہ کے قائم مقام ہوگا اور چونکہ قرض خواہ کو اپنا قرض یعنی ایک ہزار درہم لینے کا اختیار تھا۔ لہذا اس کے قائم مقام یعنی محتال علیہ کو بھی ایک ہزار درہم لینے کا اختیار ہو گا۔ اسی طرح کفیل کو اپنے مکفول عنہ سے ماضمن کے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا اور ما ادی کے رجوع کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ بخلاف المامور (یہ ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے)۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے قرضہ واپس لینے کا اختیار اسی وقت ہوتا ہے جبکہ کفیل نے مکفول عنہ کے حکم سے قرضہ ادا کیا ہو۔ اور اس وقت کفیل بامرہ اور مامور بقضاء الدین میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مامور بقضاء الدین بھی قرضدار کے حکم سے قرضہ ادا کرتا ہے اور کفیل بامرہ بھی قرضدار یعنی مکفول عنہ کے حکم سے قرضہ ادا کرتا ہے اور مامور بقضاء الدین قرضہ ادا کرنے کے بعد قرضدار سے ما ادی (جو کچھ ادا کیا گیا) کو واپس لینے کا مجاز ہے خواہ ما ادی وہ ہو جو قرضدار پر قرض تھا یا اس کے علاوہ ہو۔ پس اسی طرح کفیل کو بھی ما ادی واپس لینے کا اختیار ہونا چاہیے تھا خواہ ما ادی وہی ہو جس کا ضامن ہوا تھا خواہ اس کے علاوہ ہو۔ حالانکہ آپ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر ما ادی، ماضمن کے خلاف ہو تو کفیل ماضمن (جس کا کفیل ہوا تھا) واپس لے سکتا ہے اس کو ما ادی واپس لینے کا اختیار نہیں ہوتا؟ جواب... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مامور بقضاء الدین پر کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہے بلکہ اس نے اپنی خوشی سے بطور احسان یہ کام منظور کیا ہے تو مامور بقضاء الدین قرضہ ادا کرنے سے قرضہ کا مالک نہیں ہوگا اور جب مامور بقضاء الدین، قرضہ کا مالک نہیں ہوا تو وہ طالب یعنی قرض خواہ کے قائم مقام بھی نہیں ہوا اور جب قرض خواہ کے قائم مقام نہیں ہوا تو جو قرضدار پر واجب تھا اس کو لینے کا مجاز بھی نہ ہوگا بلکہ جو کچھ اس نے ادا کیا ہے اس کو واپس لے سکتا ہے اور رہا کفیل بامرہ تو وہ کفالہ کی وجہ سے اپنے اوپر مال قرض کا ادا کرنا لازم کرتا ہے اور جب کفیل پر مال قرض کا ادا کرنا لازم ہے تو کفیل قرض ادا کرنے کے بعد اس قرض کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ اور قرض کا مالک ہو کر مکفول لہ یعنی قرض خواہ کے قائم مقام ہوگا پس جس طرح مکفول لہ کو اسی چیز کے مطالبہ کا حق ہے جو قرضدار یعنی مکفول عنہ کے ذمہ میں ثابت ہے۔ اسی طرح کفیل کو بھی مکفول عنہ سے اس چیز کے لینے کا اختیار ہے جو قرضدار یعنی مکفول عنہ پر واجب ہے اور کفیل اس کا ضامن ہوا ہے، ما ادی و غیر ہ دوسری چیز لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ حاصل یہ کہ کفیل بامرہ اور مامور بقضاء الدین میں بہت بڑا فرق ہے اور فرق کے ساتھ قیاس درست نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا کفیل بامرہ کو مامور بقضاء الدین پر قیاس کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب عنایہ کے لکھنے کے مطابق ہدایہ کی عبارت "حيث يرجع بما ادی" کے اطلاق میں تسامح ہے کیونکہ عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مامور بقضاء الدین ہر صورت میں ما ادی رجوع کرے گا حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ اگر مؤدی (جو ادا کیا گیا) مامور بہ کے مانند ہو یا اس سے کم تر ہو تب تو ما ادی رجوع کرے گا اور اگر مؤدی مامور بہ سے بڑھ کر ہو تو مامور بہ کو واپس لے گا ما ادی واپس نہ لے گا۔ مثلاً قرضدار پر دراہم زیوف کا قرضہ ہے مگر مامور بقضاء الدین نے دراہم زیوف کی جگہ دراہم جیاد ادا کر دیئے تو وہ قرضدار سے دراہم زیوف واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ وصف جودت جو قرضہ سے زائد ایک چیز ہے اس کو ادا کرنے میں مامور بقضاء الدین متبرع ہے اور متبرع کو رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ دراہم جیاد واپس نہیں لے سکتا صرف دراہم زیوف واپس لے سکتا ہے حالانکہ ما ادی دراہم جیاد میں نہ کہ دراہم زیوف۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ ہدایہ کی عبارت "حيث يرجع بما ادی" علی الاطلاق صحیح نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر قرضہ کی رقم ایک ہزار درہم ہو مگر کفیل نے مکفول لہ سے پانچ سو درہم پر صلح کر لی ہو تو اس صورت میں کفیل مکفول عنہ سے ما ادی یعنی پانچ سو درہم واپس لے سکتا ہے ما ضمن یعنی ایک ہزار درہم واپس لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا کیونکہ پانچ سو درہم پر صلح کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مکفول لہ نے کفیل کو پانچ سو درہم سے بری کر دیا ہے اور بری کرنا ایسا ہے گویا مکفول لہ نے پانچ سو درہم کا قرضہ ساقط کر دیا ہے اور ساقط شدہ مقدار میں کفیل کو رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوتا لہذا مذکورہ صلح کی صورت میں کفیل مکفول عنہ سے پانچ سو درہم واپس لے سکتا ہے اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے مکفول لہ کفیل کو بری کر دے۔ پس اگر مکفول لہ کفیل کو پورے قرضہ سے بری کر دے تو کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کرنے کا بالکل اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر ایک جز سے بری کر دیا تو کفیل جس قدر ادا کرے گا اس قدر مکفول عنہ سے لے سکتا ہے اسی طرح صلح کی صورت میں کفیل جو مقدار ادا کرے گا مکفول عنہ سے اسی قدر لے سکتا ہے۔
Book of Kafalah. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 9. He does not have the option to recover what was paid (ma adi). Because the assignee (muhtal alayh) becomes owner of the debt by paying, and when he becomes owner, he stands in the place of the creditor. Since the creditor had the right to take his debt of one thousand dirhams, so his substitute (the assignee) also has the right to take one thousand dirhams. Similarly, the kafil has the right to recover from his makful anhu the guaranteed amount (madmin), and not the amount paid (ma adi). Except the ma'mur. This is the answer to a presumed question. The question is: The kafil only has the right to take back the debt from the makful anhu when he paid by the order of the makful anhu. At that time, there is no difference between the kafil bi-amrihi and the ma'mur bi qada al-dayn. Because the ma'mur also pays by the order of the debtor, and the kafil bi-amrihi also pays by the order of the debtor (the makful anhu). The ma'mur bi qada al-dayn, after paying, is entitled to take back from the debtor what he paid (ma adi), whether that paid amount is the same as the debtor's debt or different. So similarly, the kafil should have had the right to take back ma adi, whether it is the same as that for which he was surety or different. Yet you have stated that if ma adi differs from madmin, the kafil can take back madmin (that for which he was surety), and he does not have the right to take back ma adi. The answer: The answer is that the ma'mur bi qada al-dayn is not obliged to pay anything; rather, he voluntarily accepted this task as a favor. So the ma'mur does not become owner of the debt by paying it. When he does not become owner, he does not stand in place of the creditor. When he does not stand in place, he is not entitled to take what was owed to the debtor, but he can only take back what he actually paid. As for the kafil bi-amrihi, he makes it obligatory upon himself to pay the debt due to the suretyship. When it is obligatory for the kafil to pay, then after paying, he becomes owner of the debt. After becoming owner, he stands in place of the creditor. So just as the creditor has the right to demand exactly what is established as a debt upon the debtor (the makful anhu), similarly the kafil has the right to take from the makful anhu exactly what was owed and for which he was surety. He does not have the right to take something else (ma adi other than madmin). The conclusion is that there is a great difference between the kafil bi-amrihi and the ma'mur bi qada al-dayn, and with a difference, analogy is not valid. Therefore, analogizing the kafil bi-amrihi to the ma'mur is incorrect. According to Sahib al-'Inayah, the Hidayah's expression 'where he recovers what he paid' is imprecise in its generality, because the expression suggests that the ma'mur recovers ma adi in all cases, but it is not so. Rather, if the paid amount (mu'addi) is like the commanded amount or less, then he recovers ma adi; but if the paid amount exceeds the commanded amount, he takes back the commanded amount and not the excess. For example, if the debtor owes bad dirhams (zuyuf), but the ma'mur pays good dirhams (jiyad) instead of the bad ones, then he can take back bad dirhams from the debtor. Because the quality of goodness (wasf al-jawdah) is an extra thing beyond the debt; in paying it, the ma'mur is a volunteer (mutabarri'), and a volunteer does not have the right of recourse. Therefore, he cannot take back the good dirhams, only the bad ones, even though what he paid was good dirhams, not bad. Thus, it is known that the Hidayah's expression 'where he recovers what he paid' is not correct absolutely. The author of Hidayah says: If the debt amount is one thousand dirhams, but the kafil made a reconciliation (sulh) with the creditor (makful lah) for five hundred dirhams, then in that case the kafil can recover from the makful anhu what he paid, i.e., five hundred dirhams, and he does not have the right to recover the guaranteed amount, i.e., one thousand dirhams. Because the meaning of reconciliation for five hundred dirhams is that the creditor has discharged the kafil for five hundred dirhams. Discharge is like the creditor cancelling five hundred dirhams of the debt. In that cancelled amount, the kafil does not have the right of recourse. Therefore, in the mentioned case of reconciliation, the kafil can take five hundred dirhams from the makful anhu, and it is as if the creditor discharged the kafil. So if the creditor discharges the kafil from the entire debt, then the kafil has absolutely no right of recourse against the makful anhu. And if he discharges him from a part, then the kafil can take from the makful anhu the amount he pays. Similarly, in the case of reconciliation, the kafil can take from the makful anhu only the amount he pays.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of kafalah (suretyship) regarding the kafil's right of recourse (ruju') against the principal debtor (makful 'anhu). It opens by stating the general rule that the kafil can only recover the specific amount for which he was surety (madmin), not any other amount he may have paid (ma adi) if it differs. The text then addresses a potential objection: why the distinction between a kafil bi-amrihi (guarantor by order of the debtor) and a ma'mur bi qada al-dayn (a person ordered to repay a debt)? The answer is that the ma'mur pays voluntarily without any legal obligation on him, so he does not become the owner of the debt; therefore, he can only recover what he actually paid. In contrast, the kafil bi-amrihi is legally obliged to pay due to his guarantee, so after payment, he becomes the owner of the debt and steps into the position of the creditor, allowing him to recover only the original debt, not any excess. The passage then refines this principle by criticizing the Hidayah's phrasing 'where he recovers what he paid' as too general, giving the example of paying better quality coins than owed. Finally, it discusses the effect of sulh (reconciliation) between the kafil and the creditor, where the kafil recovers only the amount he actually paid, not the full guaranteed amount, because the reconciliation effectively reduces the debt.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A reconciliation or settlement between the kafil and the creditor, often for a lesser amount than the guaranteed debt.
متبرع (mutabarri'): A volunteer; one who pays extra voluntarily without legal obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, if a kafil pays 800 dirhams to the creditor as part of a sulh agreement on a 1000 dirham debt, how much can he recover from the principal debtor?
A) 800 dirhams
B) 1000 dirhams
C) 200 dirhams
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Sulh reduces the debt; the kafil recovers only what he pays, and full discharge eliminates recourse entirely.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
Kafil Cannot Demand Payment Before He Pays
States and proves that kafil cannot demand money from principal debtor before paying himself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a kafil's right to demand payment from the principal debtor before paying the creditor, apply the condition of ownership, and distinguish the case of a wakil bil-shira.

Core Idea
A kafil cannot demand payment before he pays — ownership of the debt is the key.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi suretyship law. While a surety (kafil) guarantees the debt, he does not gain the right to collect from the principal debtor (makful 'anhu) until he himself has paid the creditor. The underlying principle is ownership: the kafil must become the owner of the debt through payment before he can demand reimbursement. The text contrasts this with an agent for purchase (wakil bil-shira), who can demand the price from his principal before paying the seller, because a nominal exchange creates a different legal relationship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The kafil cannot demand money from the makful anhu before paying the creditor.
This is the core provision.
2
Extract the underlying legal cause
Ownership (milkiyya) of the debt is the cause (mu'jib) that gives the kafil the right of recourse (ruju').
Without ownership, the cause is absent.
3
Apply the cause to the ruling
Since the kafil does not own the debt before payment, the cause is absent, so he cannot demand.
Thus, payment is a condition for the right to demand.
4
Contrast with the wakil bil-shira
The wakil can demand before payment because a nominal exchange (mubadala hukmiyya) between agent and principal gives the wakil a notional ownership.
This exception proves the rule by highlighting the different legal relationship.
5
Consider the supplementary ruling on detainment
If the kafil is detained or imprisoned due to the debt, he may reciprocally detain/imprison the principal debtor as a proportional remedy.
This is a separate but related principle of reciprocity (mu'amala bi-mithli).
