کفیل مکفول عنہ سے قرضہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے مال کے مطالبہ کا حق نہیں رکھتا
قال وليس للكفيل أن يطالب المكفول عنه بالمال قبل أن يؤدى عنه لأنه لا يملكه قبل الأداء بخلاف الوكيل بالشراء حيث يرجع قبل الأداء لأنه انعقد بينهما مبادلة حكمية
ترجمہ: اور مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے قرضہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے مال کے مطالبہ کا اختیار نہیں ہے کیونکہ کفیل ادا کرنے سے پہلے قرضہ کا مالک نہیں ہوتا برخلاف وکیل بالشراء کے کیونکہ وہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے رجوع کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان مبادلہ حکمی منعقد ہوا ہے۔
تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب تک کفیل مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے قرضہ ادا نہ کرے اس وقت تک کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے مال کے مطالبہ کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ موجب للرجوع کفیل کا مالک ہونا ہے یعنی کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار اس وقت ہوتا ہے جب کفیل قرضہ کا مالک ہو جائے حالانکہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے کفیل قرضہ کا مالک نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جب ادا کرنے سے پہلے کفیل قرضہ کا مالک نہیں ہوا تو موجب للرجوع بھی نہیں پایا گیا اور جب رجوع کو واجب کرنے والی چیز یعنی کفیل کا مالک ہونا نہیں پایا گیا تو ادا کرنے سے پہلے کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے قرضہ کا مال لینے کا اختیار بھی نہ ہوگا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر کسی نے کسی کو کوئی چیز خریدنے کا وکیل کیا تو وکیل کو اختیار ہے کہ بائع ثمن ادا کرنے سے پہلے اپنے موکل سے ثمن کی رقم لے لے۔ کیونکہ وکیل اور مؤکل کے درمیان حکماً مبادلہ اور بیع ہوتی ہے پس وکیل، بائع کے مرتبہ میں اور مؤکل مشتری کے مرتبہ میں ہوگا۔ اور بائع کو مبیع سپرد کرنے سے پہلے چونکہ ثمن کے مطالبہ کا حق ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے وکیل کو بھی اپنے مؤکل سے ثمن کے مطالبہ کا حق ہو گا۔ خواہ وکیل نے اپنے بائع کو ثمن ادا کیا ہو یا ثمن ادا نہ کیا ہو۔
مال کے سلسلے میں کفیل کو پکڑا گیا تو وہ مکفول عنہ کو پکڑے
قال فإن لوزم بالمال كان له أن يلازم المكفول عنه حتى يخلصه وكذا اذا حبس كان له أن يحبسه لأنه لحقه ما لحقه من جهته فيعامله بمثله
The kafil does not have the right to demand the money from the makful anhu before he pays it from him. He said: It is not for the kafil to demand the makful anhu for the money before he pays on his behalf, because he does not own it before payment, contrary to the agent for purchase, who can demand before payment because a nominal exchange has been contracted between them. Translation: Before paying the debt on behalf of the makful anhu, the kafil does not have the right to demand the money from the makful anhu, because the kafil does not become owner of the debt before paying it, unlike the agent for purchase, who can demand before payment because a nominal exchange has been contracted between the agent and the principal. Commentary: The issue is that as long as the kafil does not pay the debt on behalf of the makful anhu, he does not have the right to demand the money from the makful anhu. The proof is that the cause for recourse (mu'jib li al-ruju') is the kafil's ownership, i.e., the kafil gets the right to recourse against the makful anhu when he becomes owner of the debt, but he does not own it before payment. So when before payment the kafil has not become owner, the cause for recourse is not present, and thus before payment the kafil does not have the right to take the money from the makful anhu. Contrary to this, if someone appoints an agent to buy something, the agent has the right to take the price from his principal before paying the seller, because between the agent and the principal there is a nominal exchange and sale. Hence the agent is in the position of the seller and the principal in the position of the buyer. Just as the seller has the right to demand the price before delivering the sold item, so the agent has the right to demand the price from his principal, whether the agent has paid the price to the seller or not. In matters of property, if the kafil is detained, he may detain the makful anhu. He said: If he is confined for the money, he may confine the makful anhu until he releases him, and similarly if he is imprisoned, he may imprison him, because he has suffered what he suffered due to him, so he treats him similarly.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents a distinct ruling from the Hidayah: the kafil cannot demand the debt money from the principal debtor (makful 'anhu) before he himself pays it to the creditor. The reasoning is that the kafil does not become the owner of the debt until he pays it; ownership is the essential condition (mu'jib) that gives him the right of recourse. The text contrasts this with the case of an agent for purchase (wakil bil-shira), who can demand the price from his principal before paying the seller because a nominal exchange (mubadala hukmiyya) exists between them, placing the agent in the position of a seller who can demand the price before delivery. The passage ends with a supplementary ruling: if the kafil is detained or imprisoned due to the debt, he can detain or imprison the principal debtor in reciprocity (mu'amala bi-mithlihi), as a form of proportional remedy.

Key Terms
مطالبة (mutalaba): The kafil's demand for payment from the principal debtor before the kafil has paid the creditor; such demand is legally ineffective.
اداء (ada'): Payment by the kafil of the debt to the creditor, which triggers ownership and the right of recourse.
وكيل بالشراء (wakil bil-shira): An agent appointed to purchase something; he can demand the price from his principal before paying the seller due to the nominal exchange created by the agency contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A kafil has not yet paid the creditor. Can he demand the debt amount from the principal debtor?
A) Yes, because he is the surety
B) No, because he does not own the debt before paying
C) Yes, by analogy to an agent for purchase
D) Only if the principal debtor agrees

Key Takeaway
A kafil cannot demand payment from the principal debtor before paying the creditor, because ownership of the debt is the necessary cause for recourse.

Guarantor's Right to Reclaim After Settlement
Explanation of guarantor's recourse limit after sulh with creditor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a guarantor's recourse after settlement is limited to the amount actually paid, distinguishing between ma ada and ma damina.

Core Idea
After settlement, the guarantor reclaims only what he paid, not what he guaranteed.

This lesson explains a critical distinction in Hanafi kafalah: when a guarantor settles with the creditor for a reduced amount, his right to reclaim from the principal debtor is limited to that reduced payment. The settlement acts as a discharge (ibra), cancelling the forgiven portion. Many mistakenly think the guarantor can always demand the full guaranteed amount. We will unpack the ruling from Ashraf al-Bidaya, its rationale, and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is the guarantor's recourse against the principal debtor after paying the creditor under a settlement. The ruling: the guarantor can only reclaim the amount he actually paid (ma ada), not the full guaranteed amount (ma damina).
This is a clear Hanafi position based on the concept of ibra.
2
Understand the Legal Basis
The settlement (sulh) for a reduced amount legally equals the creditor discharging the guarantor from that part of the debt. Discharge cancels the debt as if it were never owed. Hence, the guarantor has no right to pass on the cancelled amount to the debtor.
The analogy: just as full discharge ends recourse, partial discharge limits it.
3
Distinguish Key Terms
Ma ada (what is paid) vs. ma damina (what is guaranteed). The guarantor's recourse is tied to his actual outlay, not the original guarantee. This prevents the guarantor from profiting by settling at a discount.
Memorize the Arabic phrases: ما أدی (ma ada) and ما ضمن (ma damina).
4
Apply to Variations
If the guarantor is discharged from the entire debt (full ibra), he has no recourse. If discharged from a part, he only reclaims the part he pays. The same logic applies to settlement.
The ruling is consistent: no recourse for the waived portion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكفاله۔ اشرف البدایہ جلد - قم دراہم جیاد میں نہ کہ دراہم زیوف پس معلوم ہوا کہ ہدایہ کی عبارت پر جع بما ادی علی الاطلاق صحیح نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر قرضہ کی رقم ایک ہزار درہم ہو مگر کفیل نے مکفول لہ سے پانچ سو درہم پر صلح کر لی ہو تو اس صورت میں کفیل مکفول عنہ سے ما ادی یعنی پانچ سو درہم واپس لے سکتا ہے ما ضمن یعنی ایک ہزار درہم واپس لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا کیونکہ پانچ سو درہم پر صلح کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مکفول لہ نے کفیل کو پانچ سو درہم سے بری کر دیا ہے اور بری کرنا ایسا ہے گویا مکفول لہ نے پانچ سو درہم کا قرضہ ساقط کر دیا ہے اور ساقط شدہ مقدار میں کفیل کو رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوتا لہذا مذکورہ صلح کی صورت میں کفیل مکفول عنہ سے پانچ سو درہم واپس لے سکتا ہے اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے مکفول لہ کفیل کو بری کر دے۔ پس اگر مکفول لہ نے کفیل کو پورے قرضہ سے بری کر دے تو کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کرنے کا بالکل اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر ایک جز سے بری کر دیا تو کفیل جس قدر ادا کرے گا اس قدر مکفول عنہ سے لے سکتا ہے اسی طرح صلح کی صورت میں کفیل جو مقدار ادا کرے گا مکفول عنہ سے اسی قدر لے سکتا ہے۔ کفیل مکفول عنہ سے قرضہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے مال کے مطالبہ کا حق نہیں رکھتا
Book of Kafalah. Ashraf al-Bidaya Volume 9. (Regarding) good dirhams, not bad dirhams. So it became known that the text of al-Hidayah regarding 'jama' bi ma adda' is not correct in absolute terms. The author of al-Hidayah states: If the debt amount is one thousand dirhams, but the guarantor made a settlement with the creditor for five hundred dirhams, then in this case the guarantor can take back from the principal debtor what he paid, i.e., five hundred dirhams; he does not have the right to take back what he guaranteed, i.e., one thousand dirhams. Because the meaning of settlement for five hundred dirhams is that the creditor discharged the guarantor from five hundred dirhams, and discharging is such that it is as if the creditor cancelled five hundred dirhams of the debt. In the amount cancelled, the guarantor does not have the right to recourse. Therefore, in the mentioned case of settlement, the guarantor can take back five hundred dirhams from the principal debtor. And this is like the creditor discharging the guarantor. So if the creditor discharges the guarantor from the entire debt, then the guarantor has no right to recourse against the principal debtor at all. And if he discharges him from a part, then the guarantor can take from the principal debtor to the extent he pays. Similarly, in the case of settlement, the guarantor can take from the principal debtor the amount he pays. The guarantor does not have the right to demand money from the principal debtor before paying the debt.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya explains a key ruling in Hanafi kafalah: when a guarantor (kafil) settles with the creditor (makful lahu) for less than the full debt, his right of recourse against the principal debtor (makful 'anhu) is limited to the amount he actually paid (ma ada), not the amount he guaranteed (ma damina). The settlement effectively operates as a discharge (ibra) from the creditor, canceling that portion of the debt. Since the discharged amount is considered forgiven, the guarantor cannot reclaim it from the principal debtor. This is analogous to the creditor directly forgiving part of the debt. The passage also notes the general principle that the guarantor cannot demand payment from the principal debtor before paying the creditor himself.

Key Terms
کفیل (kafil): The guarantor who undertakes to pay the debt of another.
مکفول عنہ (makful 'anhu): The principal debtor for whom the guarantee is given.
مکفول لہ (makful lahu): The creditor to whom the debt is owed.
صلح (sulh): A settlement or compromise agreement, often for a reduced amount.
ما أدی (ma ada): What the guarantor actually paid.
ما ضمن (ma damina): What the guarantor guaranteed (the original debt amount).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a guarantor (kafil) settles with the creditor for 500 dirhams on a 1000 dirham debt, how much can he reclaim from the principal debtor?
A) 1000 dirhams
B) 500 dirhams
C) Nothing
D) It depends on the debtor's consent

Key Takeaway
When a guarantor settles with the creditor for less than the debt, his recourse against the debtor is limited to the amount he actually paid, because the settlement acts as a discharge of the waived portion.

Guarantor Cannot Demand Payment Before Paying
Arabic matn with Urdu commentary on guarantor's recourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a guarantor may demand reimbursement from the principal debtor and explain the legal reasoning (dalil aqli) that distinguishes kafalah from wakalah.

Core Idea
A guarantor must pay first to own the debt before seeking recourse.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from Hanafi fiqh on guaranty (kafalah). The guarantor cannot demand payment from the principal debtor before actually paying the creditor, because he does not yet own the debt. The text contrasts this with an agent for purchase (wakil bi al-shira) who can demand the price beforehand due to a notional exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action the text is ruling on (the guarantor demanding money before paying) and what the hukm is (not permissible, haram).
2
Locate the cause (mu'ajjib)
Identify the legal cause that makes recourse obligatory: ownership of the debt. Note that ownership only occurs after payment.
Mu'ajjib li al-ruju' = ownership
3
Analyze the contrast with wakalah
Compare the guarantor with an agent for purchase. The agent can demand the price before paying because a notional exchange (mubadala hukmiyya) creates a seller-buyer relationship, giving the agent the right to demand the price.
This contrast highlights the absence of any exchange in kafalah
4
Understand the qiyas reasoning
The text uses a qiyas (analogy) to clarify the ruling, but the core proof is the absence of ownership. The guarantee contract does not transfer ownership of the debt; it only creates a secondary obligation.
Dalil aqli: ownership is a prerequisite for recourse
5
State the final ruling
Conclude that the guarantor may only demand reimbursement after paying the creditor. Any demand before payment is invalid and the guarantor cannot compel the debtor.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وليس للكفيل أن يطالب المكفول عنه بالمال قبل أن يؤدى عنه لأنه لا يملكه قبل الأداء بخلاف لوكيل بالشراء حيث يرجع قبل الأداء لأنه أنعقد بينهما مبادلة حكمية
ترجمہ اور مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے قرضہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے مال کے مطالبہ کا اختیار نہیں ہے کیونکہ کفیل ادا کرنے سے پہلے قرضہ کا مالک نہیں ہوتا بر خلاف وکیل بالشراء کے کیونکہ وہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے رجوع کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ وکیل اور موکل کے درمیان مبادلہ حکمی منعقد ہوا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب تک کفیل مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے قرضہ ادا نہ کرے اس وقت تک کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے مال کے مطالبہ کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ موجب للرجوع کفیل کا مالک ہونا ہے یعنی کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار اس وقت ہوتا ہے جب کفیل قرضہ کا مالک ہو جائے حالانکہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے کفیل قرضہ کا مالک نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جب ادا کرنے سے پہلے کفیل قرضہ کا مالک نہیں ہوا تو موجب للرجوع بھی نہیں پایا گیا اور جب رجوع کو واجب کرنے والی چیز یعنی کفیل کا مالک ہونا نہیں پایا گیا تو ادا کرنے سے پہلے کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے قرضہ کا مال لینے کا اختیار بھی نہ ہوگا اس کے برخلاف اگر کسی نے کسی کو کوئی چیز خریدنے کا وکیل کیا تو وکیل کو اختیار ہے کہ بائع ثمن ادا کرنے سے پہلے اپنے موکل سے ثمن کی رقم لے لے۔ کیونکہ وکیل اور مؤکل کے درمیان حکما مبادلہ اور بیع ہوتی ہے پس وکیل، بائع کے مرتبہ میں اور مؤکل مشتری کے مرتبہ میں ہوگا۔ اور بائع کو مبیع سپرد کرنے سے پہلے چونکہ ثمن کے مطالبہ کا حق ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے وکیل کو بھی اپنے مؤکل سے ثمن کے مطالبہ کا حق ہو گا۔ خواہ وکیل نے اپنے بائع کو ثمن ادا کیا ہو یا ثمن ادا نہ کیا ہو۔
He said: The guarantor does not have the right to demand money from the principal debtor before he pays on his behalf, because he does not own it before payment, unlike an agent for purchase who can demand before payment because a notional exchange is concluded between them. Translation: And before paying the debt on behalf of the principal debtor, the guarantor does not have the right to demand money from the principal debtor, because the guarantor is not the owner of the debt before payment, unlike an agent for purchase, because he can demand before payment since a notional exchange is concluded between the agent and the principal. Explanation: The issue is that as long as the guarantor does not pay the debt on behalf of the principal debtor, he does not have the right to demand money from the principal debtor. The proof is that the cause for recourse is the guarantor's ownership, i.e., the guarantor has the right to recourse when he becomes owner of the debt, but before payment the guarantor is not the owner. So when before payment the guarantor is not the owner, the cause for recourse is not found. And when the thing that makes recourse obligatory, i.e., the guarantor's ownership, is not found, then before payment the guarantor does not have the right to take the debt money from the principal debtor. In contrast, if someone appoints an agent to buy something, the agent can demand the price from his principal before paying the seller, because a notional exchange and sale is concluded between agent and principal. Thus the agent is like the seller and the principal like the buyer. And since the seller has the right to demand the price before delivering the sold item, so the agent also has the right to demand the price from his principal, whether the agent has paid the price to the seller or not.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling of Hanafi fiqh: the guarantor cannot demand reimbursement from the principal debtor until he has actually paid the creditor. The reasoning is that the guarantor does not 'own' the debt before payment; ownership is the cause (mu'ajjib) for recourse. Contrast is made with an agent for purchase (wakil bi al-shira), who can demand the price from his principal before paying, because the agency contract creates a notional exchange between them, placing the agent in the position of seller and the principal as buyer.

Key Terms
موجب للرجوع (mu'ajjib li al-ruju'): The cause that makes recourse obligatory; here, ownership of the debt.
وکیل بالشراء (wakil bi al-shira): An agent appointed to purchase something.
مبادلہ حکمی (mubadala hukmiyya): A notional or legal exchange, as between agent and principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the contract prohibits it
B) Because he does not own the debt until he pays
C) Because the debtor is not liable until after payment
D) Because the creditor must consent first

Key Takeaway
A guarantor must first pay the creditor to own the debt before he can seek recourse from the principal debtor.

The Guarantor's Right to Pursue the Principal Debtor: A Madhhab Dispute
Arabic matn and debate on guarantor's right to imprison debtor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the guarantor's right to pursue the principal debtor, identify its condition (kafala bi amrihi), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The guarantor may imprison the debtor because the debtor caused the hardship.

When a guarantor (kafil) is pursued or imprisoned by the creditor for a debt, a natural question arises: can the guarantor in turn pursue or imprison the principal debtor (makful 'anhu)? This passage presents the Hanafi view—that reciprocal treatment is justified—and contrasts it with the more apparent Shafi'i opinion denying such a right. Understanding the legal reasoning and condition for this right deepens our grasp of guaranty (kafalah) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the guarantor may pursue and even have the principal debtor imprisoned if the guarantee was at the debtor's request.
The text explicitly uses 'kaana lahu' (he has the right).
2
Identify the key condition
Note the condition mentioned in the commentary: the guarantee must be 'biamrihi' (at the debtor's request). Without this, the right does not arise.
This is a shart for the permissibility.
3
Present the opposing school's view
State Imam al-Shafi'i's more apparent opinion: the guarantor cannot imprison the debtor before paying because he has no established right over the debtor prior to payment.
This is labelled as 'azhar' (more apparent) by the author.
4
Analyze the proofs and determine the practical consequence
The Hanafi proof is based on equity: the debtor caused the hardship, so it is his duty to relieve the guarantor. The Shafi'i proof denies any right before payment. The practical difference (thamarah) is that under Hanafi law the guarantor can seek imprisonment, whereas under the Shafi'i view he cannot.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فإن لوزم بالمال كان له أن يلازم المكفول عنه حتى يخلصه وكذا اذا حبس كان له أن يحبسه لأنه لحقه ما لحقه من جهته فيعامله بمثله
ترجمہ پس اگر مال کے سلسلہ میں کفیل کو لازم پکڑا گیا تو کفیل کے لئے جائز ہے کہ وہ مکفول عنہ کو لازم پکڑے یہاں تک کہ مکفول عنہ اس کو چھٹکارا دلائے۔ اور اسی طرح اگر کفیل قید کیا گیا تو اس کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ مکفول عنہ کو قید کرادے کیونکہ کفیل کو جو کچھ پریشانی لاحق ہوئی وہ مکفول عنہ کی وجہ سے لاحق ہوئی ہے پس مکفول عنہ کے ساتھ ایسا ہی معاملہ کر سکتا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مکفول لہ اپنا قرضہ وصول کرنے کے لئے کفیل کا دامن گیر ہو گیا یعنی ہر وقت کفیل کے پیچھے پڑا رہتا ہے تو کفیل کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ مکفول عنہ کا دامن گیر ہو یعنی کفیل، مکفول عنہ کا پیچھا کرے یہاں تک کہ مکفول عنہ کفیل کا دامن چھڑا دے یعنی مکفول عنہ ہی نے کفیل کو اس مصیبت میں مبتلا کیا ہے لہذا اس مصیبت سے نجات دلانا بھی مکفول عنہ ہی پر واجب ہوگا اور اگر مکفول لہ نے اپنے قرضہ کی وجہ سے کفیل کو قید کرادیا تو کفیل کو بھی اختیار ہے کہ وہ مکفول عنہ کو قید کرادے۔ بشرطیکہ کفالہ بامرہ ہو۔ یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے اور اس کے قائل امام مالک اور امام احمد ہیں امام شافعی کا قول اظہر یہ ہے کہ کفیل کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ وہ مکفول عنہ کو قید کرادے۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل. ہے کہ قرضہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے کفیل کا مکفول عنہ پر کوئی حق واجب نہیں ہے تو کفیل کے لئے مکفول عنہ کو قید کرانے کا حق بھی نہ ہوگا۔
ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ کفیل کو جو کچھ پریشانی لاحق ہوئی ہے وہ مکفول عنہ کی وجہ سے لاحق ہوئی۔ اس لئے مکفول عنہ پر واجب ہے کہ وہ کفیل کو چھٹکارا دلائے یعنی مکفول لہ کا قرضہ ادا کر دے۔ اور اگر مکفول عنہ کفیل کو چھٹکارانہ دلا سکا تو کفیل کو مکفول عنہ کے ساتھ وہی معاملہ کرنے کا اختیار ہو گا جو معاملہ مکفول لہ کفیل کے ساتھ کرے گا۔
He said: If (the guarantor) is pursued for the money, he has the right to pursue the principal debtor until he frees him. Similarly, if he is imprisoned, he has the right to have him imprisoned, because what befalls him is due to the principal debtor, so he can treat him similarly. Translation: So if the guarantor is pursued for the money, it is permissible for the guarantor to pursue the principal debtor until the principal debtor frees him. And similarly, if the guarantor is imprisoned, he has the option to have the principal debtor imprisoned, because the hardship that befell the guarantor is due to the principal debtor, so he can treat him accordingly. Explanation: The issue is that if the creditor harasses the guarantor to collect the debt, i.e., constantly follows him, then the guarantor has the right to harass the principal debtor, i.e., the guarantor follows the principal debtor until the principal debtor releases the guarantor, meaning the principal debtor should free the guarantor from this trouble. And if the creditor had the guarantor imprisoned due to the debt, then the guarantor also has the right to have the principal debtor imprisoned, provided that the guarantee was at his request (kafala bi amrihi). This is one saying of Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad also hold it. The more apparent saying of Imam Shafi'i is that the guarantor does not have this right to have the principal debtor imprisoned. Imam Shafi'i's proof: Before paying the debt, the guarantor has no established right over the principal debtor, so he has no right to have him imprisoned. Our response: The hardship that befell the guarantor is due to the principal debtor. Therefore, it is obligatory on the principal debtor to free the guarantor, i.e., pay the debt to the creditor. And if the principal debtor does not free him, then the guarantor has the right to treat the principal debtor as the creditor treated him.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage addresses the guarantor's right to take recourse against the principal debtor when the creditor pressures or imprisons him. According to the Hanafi school (and one view of Imam Shafi'i, also held by Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad), the guarantor may similarly pursue or have the principal debtor imprisoned, provided the guarantee was at the debtor's request (kafala bi amrihi). The reason is that the hardship is caused by the debtor's failure to pay. The opposing view (the more apparent Shafi'i opinion) argues that since the guarantor has no established claim before payment, he cannot take such measures. The Hanafi response emphasizes that the debtor's obligation to relieve the guarantor justifies reciprocal treatment.

Key Terms
لازم پکڑنا (lazim pakarna): To pursue or harass persistently (in context of debt collection).
کفالہ بامرہ (kafala bi amrihi): Guarantee given at the request of the principal debtor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi fiqh, what condition must be met for the guarantor to have the principal debtor imprisoned when the creditor imprisons the guarantor?
A) The debtor must consent after imprisonment
B) The guarantee must be at the debtor's request (kafala bi amrihi)
C) The debt must be over 1000 dirhams
D) The creditor must approve

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the guarantor to pursue or imprison the principal debtor only when the guarantee was made at the debtor's request, based on the principle that the debtor caused the hardship.

Effect of Discharging Principal Debtor vs. Guarantor in Kafalah
Arabic matn and commentary on discharge of debtor vs. guarantor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of discharging the principal debtor versus the guarantor, and explain the underlying principle that the guarantor is a dependent (tabi').

Core Idea
Discharging the principal debtor automatically frees the guarantor, but discharging the guarantor does not affect the principal debtor's liability.

This lesson examines a fundamental rule in Hanafi kafalah: the guarantor's liability is accessory to the principal debtor's. We will see how the creditor's action toward one affects the other, and why the distinction lies in the nature of the guarantee contract as a joining of liability for demand (damm al-dhimma ila al-dhimma fi al-mutalaba).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two distinct cases: (1) the creditor discharges the principal debtor or receives payment from him, and (2) the creditor discharges only the guarantor. Note the difference in outcomes.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For scenario 1, the guarantor is also discharged. For scenario 2, the principal debtor remains liable. Write these clearly.
3
Find the legal reason (ta'lil)
The text explains: 'because the debt is upon the principal in the correct view' and 'the guarantor is a dependent'. The creditor's discharge of the principal eliminates the debt, which necessarily ends the accessory obligation. Discharging the accessory does not affect the principal.
Key concept: the guarantor is tabi' (dependent).
4
Connect to the definition of kafalah
Kafalah is defined as 'joining one liability to another in terms of demand' (ضم الذمتہ الی الذمتہ فی المطالبہ). The guarantor's liability is only for demand, not for the debt itself. When the principal's debt is gone, the purpose of the guarantee ceases.
This definition limits the guarantor's role.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
If a different school treats the guarantor as a primary obligor (as in some other views), the ruling would differ. The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi.
Some other schools may consider the guarantor's obligation independent, but the Hanafi school relies on this reasoning.

Source Text

ترجمہ جب مکفول لہ نے مکفول عنہ کو بری کر دیا یا مکفول لہ نے اس سے اپنا حق وصول کرلیا تو کفیل بری ہو گیا کیونکہ اصیل کا بری ہونا کفیل کے بری ہونے کو واجب کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ صحیح قول کے مطابق قرضہ تو اصیل پر ہے اور اگر مکفول لہ نے کفیل کو بری کیا تو اس سے اصیل بری نہ ہوگا کیونکہ کفیل تابع ہے اور اس لئے کہ کفیل پر صرف مطالبہ ہے اور بغیر کفیل کے مطالبہ کے اصیل پر قرضہ ہونا جائز ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مکفول لہ نے مکفول عنہ کو بری کر دیا یا مکفول عنہ سے اپنا دین وصول کر لیا تو کفیل بھی بری ہو جائے گا کیونکہ مکفول عنہ کو بری کرنا، اصیل کو بری کرنا ہے اس لئے کہ اصل دین اس پر ہوتا ہے اور اصیل کو بری کرنا مستلزم ہے کفیل کے بری کرنے کو۔ اس لئے اصیل یعنی مکفول عنہ کے بری ہونے سے کفیل بھی بری ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر مکفول لہ نے کفیل کو بری کیا تو اس سے اصیل بری نہ ہوگا کیونکہ دین تو اصیل پر واجب ہوتا ہے کفیل پر واجب نہیں ہوتا کفیل پر تو فقط مطالبہ واجب ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب مکفول لہ کے بری کر دینے کی وجہ سے مکفول عنہ سے دین ساقط ہو گیا تو مکفول عنہ پر دین کا مطالبہ بھی باقی نہ رہے گا اور جب مکفول عنہ پر دین کا مطالبہ باقی نہ رہا تو کفالہ کے معنی ضم الذمتہ الی الذمتہ فی المطالبہ نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے کفیل پر بھی مطالبہ باقی نہ رہے گا
And if the creditor discharges the principal debtor or receives (payment) from him, the guarantor is discharged, because the discharge of the principal necessitates the discharge of the guarantor, since the debt is upon the principal in the correct view. And if he discharges the guarantor, the principal is not discharged from it, because the guarantor is a dependent and there is no demand upon him, and the debt remaining upon the principal without him is permissible. Translation: When the creditor discharges the principal debtor or receives his right from him, the guarantor is discharged, because the discharge of the principal makes the discharge of the guarantor obligatory, since according to the correct view the debt is on the principal. And if the creditor discharges the guarantor, the principal is not discharged from it, because the guarantor is a dependent and upon him there is only the demand, and it is permissible for the debt to remain on the principal without the guarantor. Explanation: The issue is that if the creditor discharges the principal debtor or receives his debt from him, then the guarantor is also discharged. Because discharging the principal debtor is discharging the principal (asil), and the original debt is upon him, and discharging the principal necessitates discharging the guarantor. Therefore, with the discharge of the principal (i.e., the principal debtor), the guarantor is also discharged. And if the creditor discharges the guarantor, the principal is not discharged from it, because the debt is obligatory on the principal, not on the guarantor; on the guarantor only the demand is obligatory. So when the debt falls from the principal debtor due to the creditor's discharge, then demand upon the principal debtor also does not remain. And when demand does not remain on the principal debtor, then due to the meaning of kafala (joining of liability in demand) not being found, the demand on the guarantor also does not remain.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage establishes a key distinction in Hanafi kafalah: the guarantor (kafil) is a follower (tabi') of the principal debtor (asil). Thus, if the creditor discharges the principal debtor or receives payment from him, the guarantor is automatically discharged. However, the reverse is not true: if the creditor discharges only the guarantor, the principal debtor remains liable. The reason is that the debt is fundamentally owed by the principal debtor; the guarantor's obligation is merely accessory (the joining of liability for demand, ضم الذمة إلى الذمة في المطالبة). Once the principal's debt is discharged, the purpose of the guarantee ceases, but discharging the guarantor does not affect the principal's obligation.

Key Terms
اصیل (asil): The principal debtor (makful 'anhu) who originally owes the debt.
تبع (taba'): Dependent or accessory; the guarantor is a dependent of the principal debtor.
ضم الذمتہ الی الذمتہ فی المطالبہ (damm al-dhimma ila al-dhimma fi al-mutalaba): Joining one liability to another in terms of demand; the essence of kafalah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The guarantor remains liable until specifically released.
B) The guarantor is automatically discharged.
C) The guarantor becomes jointly liable with the debtor.
D) The guarantor's liability is reduced by half.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi kafalah, discharging the principal debtor automatically frees the guarantor, but discharging the guarantor does not affect the principal's liability because the guarantor is a dependent and the debt is primarily on the principal.

The Surety's Right to Pursue the Principal Debtor (Al-Mukhtalaf Fih)
States Hanafi ruling and defends it against Shafi'i opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the surety's recourse against the debtor, identify the condition (kafala bi amrihi), and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
The surety may pursue the debtor only when the debtor caused the suretyship—causation creates obligation.

This passage presents a classical dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i school on whether a surety can proactively demand reimbursement from the principal debtor before paying the creditor. The Hanafi school, relying on the principle of causation, grants the surety the right to pursue the debtor if the suretyship was at the debtor's request. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing the type of suretyship and the basis of the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The surety is being pursued or imprisoned by the creditor. The passage describes two situations: the creditor 'holds the surety's collar' (constant pursuit) or has the surety imprisoned.
This sets the context for the surety's need for recourse.
2
Note the condition
The Hanafi ruling applies only when the suretyship is 'bi amrihi' (with the debtor's command). The passage explicitly states this condition.
Without this condition, the surety has no proactive right.
3
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
The hardship suffered by the surety is caused by the debtor's failure to pay his debt. Therefore, the debtor is obligated to relieve the surety's hardship.
This is a causal argument (dalil aqli) – the debtor's action (requesting suretyship and not paying) is the cause.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that before payment, the surety has no established right against the debtor, so no right to imprison exists. The Hanafi rebuttal emphasizes the causal link.
The dispute hinges on whether causation alone creates a legal obligation.

Source Text

امام شافعی کی دلیل . ی ہے کہ قرضہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے کھیل کا مکفول عنہ پر کوئی حق واجب نہیں ہے تو کفیل کے لئے مکفول عنہ کو قید کرانے کا حق بھی نہ ہوگا۔

So if in the matter of wealth the surety is held liable, then it is permissible for the surety to hold the principal debtor liable until the principal debtor secures his release. Similarly, if the surety is imprisoned, he has the option to have the principal debtor imprisoned, because whatever hardship befell the surety befell due to the principal debtor. Thus he can deal with the principal debtor in such a manner.
Commentary: The issue is that if the creditor holds the surety's collar to collect his debt, i.e., constantly pursues the surety, then the surety has the option to hold the principal debtor's collar, i.e., pursue the principal debtor until the principal debtor releases the surety. Because it was the principal debtor who involved the surety in this trouble; thus it is obligatory upon the principal debtor to deliver the surety from this trouble. And if the creditor had the surety imprisoned due to his debt, then the surety also has the option to have the principal debtor imprisoned, provided the suretyship is with his command. This is one view of Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad hold it. The more apparent view of Imam Shafi'i is that the surety does not have this option to have the principal debtor imprisoned.
Imam Shafi'i's evidence: Before the debt is paid, the surety has no right that is obligatory upon the principal debtor, so the surety would also have no right to have the principal debtor imprisoned.
Our response: Whatever hardship befell the surety befell due to the principal debtor. Therefore, it is obligatory upon the principal debtor to release the surety, i.e., pay off the creditor's debt. And if the principal debtor cannot release the surety, then the surety has the option to deal with the principal debtor as the creditor deals with the surety.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the surety's right to seek recourse against the principal debtor. The Hanafi position, which is explicitly supported by the author, states that if the surety is pursued or imprisoned by the creditor, the surety has the right to pursue or imprison the principal debtor, provided the suretyship was with the debtor's command (kafala bi amrihi). The reasoning is that the surety's hardship arises from the debtor's failure to pay; thus the debtor must indemnify the surety. Imam Shafi'i's opposing view, also held by Malik and Ahmad, is that the surety has no such right because prior to payment, the surety has no claim against the debtor. The Hanafi rebuttal reiterates the causal link: the surety's predicament is directly caused by the debtor, so the debtor is obligated to relieve the surety. This is a classical example of istihsan (equity) overriding strict qiyas, although the text does not use the term explicitly. The dispute is practical: under Hanafi law, a surety can proactively recover from the debtor without waiting for the creditor's action.

Key Terms
كفالہ بامرہ (kafala bi amrihi): Suretyship that occurs at the command and request of the principal debtor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only when the suretyship was with the debtor's command (kafala bi amrihi)
C) Only after paying the debt
D) Only if the debtor agrees

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants the surety recourse against the debtor only when the debtor requested the suretyship, based on the principle that the cause of hardship must relieve it.

Release of Principal Debtor and Its Effect on the Surety
Ruling and proof on release of principal and its effect on surety

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of releasing the principal debtor on the surety, and explain the proof based on the accessory nature of suretyship.

Core Idea
Releasing the principal debtor releases the surety; releasing the surety does not release the principal — the debt is on the principal, not the surety.

This passage establishes a key asymmetry in Hanafi suretyship law: the creditor's release of the principal debtor automatically discharges the surety, but releasing the surety leaves the principal debtor's liability untouched. The reasoning hinges on the nature of the surety's obligation as accessory (tabi') to the principal debt. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of kafalah and avoiding confusion with hawala (transfer of debt).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Asymmetrical Ruling
The passage states two related but opposite rulings: (1) if the creditor releases the principal debtor, the surety is released; (2) if the creditor releases the surety, the principal debtor is not released. State both clearly.
The asymmetry is the key point.
2
Understand the Proof: Debt is on Principal
The proof given: the debt is fundamentally upon the principal debtor (asil). The surety's obligation is only to guarantee the demand (ضم الذمة في المطالبة). Therefore, when the principal is released, the foundation of the surety's obligation disappears. The surety is a follower (tabi').
Hanafi: surety does not bear the debt, only the demand.
3
Apply the Proof to the Two Scenarios
Scenario A: Release principal → debt extinguished → surety's accessory obligation also extinguished. Scenario B: Release surety → only the demand on surety is gone; the principal debt remains. The surety's release does not affect the principal because the surety is a follower, not the principal.
The surety's obligation is derivative, so it can be removed without affecting the principal.
4
Address the Objection about Condition of Release
The text anticipates an objection: if at the start of the contract the creditor stipulates that the principal is released (i.e., the surety becomes primarily liable), then releasing the principal would not release the surety. The answer: such a stipulation transforms the contract from kafalah into hawalah (transfer of debt). In pure kafalah, the principal's release frees the surety.
Distinguishes kafalah from hawalah based on the nature of liability.
5
Distinguish from Other Schools (Optional Context)
This asymmetric ruling is a distinct Hanafi position. Some other schools may hold that releasing the surety also releases the principal because the surety's liability is primary. Recognizing this difference helps in understanding madhhab-specific reasoning.
Cross-madhhab awareness strengthens analysis.

بدونه جائز جب مکفول لہ نے مکفول عنہ کو بری کر دیا یا مکفول لہ نے اس سے اپنا حق وصول کرلیا تو کفیل بری ہو گیا کیونکہ اصیل کابری ہونا کفیل کے بری ہونے کو واجب کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ صحیح قول کے مطابق قرضہ تو واجب ہوتا ہے کفیل پر واجب نہیں ہوتا کھیل پر تو فقط مطالبہ واجب ہوتا ہے، پس جب مکفول لا کے بری کر دینے کی وجہ سے مکفول عنہ سے دین ساقط ہو گیا تو مکفول عنہ پر دین کا مطالبہ بھی باقی نہ رہے گا اور جب مکفول عنہ پر دین کا مطالبہ باقی نہ رہا تو کفالہ کے معنی ضم الذمتۃ الی الذمتہ فی المطالبہ نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے کفیل پر بھی مطالبہ باقی نہ رہے گا اس جگہ ایک اعتراض ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر ابتدائے کفالہ میں براءۃ اصیل کو شرط قرار دیدیا گیا تو یہاں برکت اصیل موجود ہے لیکن یہ برأت کفیل کوستلزم نہیں ہے پس اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ براءة اصیل، براء ت کفیل کو مستلزم نہیں ہوتا۔ اس کا جواب پہلے گزر چکا کہ اگر ابتدائے کفالہ میں برکت اصیل کی شرط لگادی گئی تو یہ کفالہ نہ ہوگا بلکہ حوالہ ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ کفالہ بشرط برات اصیل کفالہ ہوتا ہے۔ اور اگر مکفول لڑ نے کفیل کو بری کیا تو اصیل یعنی مغول عنہ قرضہ سے بری نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کفیل مکفول عنہ کا تابع ہے اور مکفول عنہ تابع نہیں ہے پس اگر کفیل کو بری کرنے سے اصیل کو بری کر دیا جائے تو اصیل کا اپنے تابع کا تابع ہونا لازم آئے گا حالانکہ یہ قلب موضوع ہے اس لئے کہا گیا کہ کفیل کو بری کرنے سے اصیل بری نہ ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفیل پر صرف مطالبہ واجب ہوتا ہے اصل قرضہ واجہ نہیں ہوتا اور اصیل پر قرضہ کا باقی رہنا اس وقت بھی جائز ہے جبکہ کفیل ہی نہ ہو۔ جیسے کفالہ سے پہلے اصیل پر قرضہ موجود تھا یا نفیل مر گیا تو اصیل سے قرضہ ساقط نہیں ہوتا۔ پس اسی طرح اصیل پر اس وقت بھی قرضہ باقی رہے گا جبکہ کفیل کو مطالبہ سے بری کر دیا گیا ہو ۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ تفصیل کے بری ہونے سے اصیل یعنی مغول عند دین سے بری نہ ہوگا۔
If the creditor releases the principal debtor or receives (the debt) from him, the surety becomes released.
And if the creditor releases the principal debtor or receives full payment from him, the surety is released, because the release of the principal obligates the release of the surety, since the debt is upon the principal in the correct view. And if he releases the surety, the principal is not released from it, because the surety is a follower, and only the right to demand is upon him, and the continuation of the debt upon the principal without the surety is permissible. When the creditor releases the principal debtor or receives his right from him, the surety becomes released because the release of the principal necessitates the release of the surety, since according to the correct view, the debt is upon the principal. And if the creditor releases the surety, the principal is not released, because the surety is a follower and because only the right to demand is upon the surety, and the debt remaining upon the principal without the surety is permissible.
Commentary: The issue is that if the creditor releases the principal debtor or receives his debt from the principal debtor, the surety is also released because releasing the principal debtor is releasing the principal. The original debt is upon him, and releasing the principal necessitates releasing the surety. So with the release of the principal (i.e., the principal debtor), the surety is also released. And if the creditor releases the surety, it does not necessitate releasing the principal. According to the correct view, the debt is obligatory upon the principal, not upon the surety. Only the right to demand is obligatory upon the surety. So when the debt falls from the principal debtor due to the creditor's release, the right to demand the debt from the principal debtor also does not remain. And when the right to demand does not remain upon the principal debtor, due to the meaning of kafala (joining of liability in demand) not being found, the right to demand also does not remain upon the surety. Here there is an objection: If at the beginning of the kafala, the release of the principal is made a condition, then here the release of the principal exists, but it does not necessitate the release of the surety. So from this it is learned that the release of the principal does not necessitate the release of the surety. The answer to this has already passed: if at the beginning of the kafala the condition of release of the principal is placed, then this would not be kafala, but rather hawala (transfer of debt). Because kafala with the condition of release of the principal is not kafala. And if the creditor releases the surety, the principal (i.e., the principal debtor) is not released from the debt. Because the surety is the follower of the principal debtor, and the principal debtor is not a follower. So if releasing the surety were to release the principal, then the principal would become a follower of his follower, which is an inversion of the subject. Therefore, it is said that releasing the surety does not release the principal. The second evidence: Only the right to demand is obligatory upon the surety, not the original debt. And the continuation of the debt upon the principal is permissible even when there is no surety. Just as before the kafala, the debt existed upon the principal, or if the surety dies, the debt does not fall from the principal. Similarly, the debt will remain upon the principal even when the surety has been released from the right to demand. So it is established that the principal (i.e., the principal debtor) is not released from the debt by the release of the surety.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof on the effect of release (ibra) in suretyship. It establishes a clear asymmetry: if the creditor releases the principal debtor, the surety is automatically released; but if the creditor releases only the surety, the principal debtor remains liable. The proof is based on the principle that the debt is fundamentally upon the principal, and the surety is merely a guarantor of demand (ضم الذمة في المطالبة). The surety's obligation is accessory; thus discharging the principal removes the foundation of the surety's liability. However, discharging the surety does not affect the principal's debt because the surety is a follower (tabi') and not the primary obligor. The text also addresses a potential objection: if at the inception of the contract the creditor stipulates that the principal is released (i.e., the surety becomes the primary debtor), that transforms the contract into hawala (transfer of debt), not kafala. This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi theory of suretyship. The second proof reinforces that the principal's liability is independent of the surety's existence; therefore, releasing the surety does not affect the principal.

Key Terms
أصيل (asil): The principal debtor (makful 'anhu) who is primarily liable for the debt.
تبع (tabi'): Follower; the surety is a follower of the principal debtor in the sense that his obligation is accessory.
إبراء (ibra): Legal release or discharge from a debt or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the creditor releases only the surety, what happens to the principal debtor's liability?
A) The principal debtor is also released
B) The principal debtor remains liable
C) The principal debtor becomes a surety for the surety
D) The debt is extinguished

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi suretyship, the release of the principal debtor discharges the surety, but the release of the surety does not affect the principal's liability.

Effect of Postponement (Ta'khir) on Surety: The Analogy to Ibra
Ruling on effect of creditor's postponement in kafalah, with qiyas to ibra.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of postponement in suretyship and explain why postponement from the principal extends to the surety but not vice versa, using the analogy to permanent release (ibra).

Core Idea
Postponement from the principal debtor automatically postpones the surety's liability, but not vice versa—like ibra.

In Hanafi law, suretyship (kafalah) attaches the surety's liability to the principal debtor's obligation. A key question arises: when the creditor grants a postponement, who benefits? This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah establishes the rule using a qiyas (analogy) to permanent release (ibra). The distinction hinges on the nature of ta'khir as a temporary waiver of the right to demand. Understanding this rule is vital for ensuring that the surety's liability is not unfairly extended beyond what the creditor intended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage contrasts two cases: postponement from the principal debtor, and postponement from the surety. Note the different outcomes: in the first case, the surety also gets postponement; in the second, the principal is unaffected.
2
Recognize the underlying principle
The rule is derived by analogy to ibra (permanent release). In ibra, releasing the principal releases the surety, but releasing the surety does not release the principal. Recognize this asymmetry as the basis.
3
Apply the analogy to ta'khir
Just as ibra permanently removes the right to demand, ta'khir temporarily removes it. Apply the same asymmetry: temporary release of principal = temporary release of surety; temporary release of surety ≠ temporary release of principal.
The qiyas is valid because the effective cause (illa) is the same: waiver of the right to demand.
4
Distinguish the term-in-contract case
The passage notes an exception: if the suretyship contract itself includes a term (e.g., 'I guarantee this debt payable in one month'), then the term applies to both parties because it was part of the original obligation. This differs from a later postponement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مکفول لہ نے مکفول عنہ سے قرض مؤخر کر دیا تو کفیل سے بھی مؤخر ہو جائے گا
وكذا اذا أخر الطالب عن الأصيل فهو تاخير عن الكفيل ولو أخر عن الكفيل لم يكن تاخيرا عن الذى عليه الأصل لأن التأخير ابراء موقت فيعتبر بالأبراء المؤبد بخلاف ما اذا كفّل بالمال الحال مؤجلا إلى شهر فإنه يتاجل عن الأصيل لأنه لاحق له الا الدين حال وجود الكفالة فصار الأجل داخلاً فيه أما لههنا فبخلافه
ترجمہ اور اسی طرح اگر مکفول لڑنے مکفول عنہ سے قرضہ کو مؤخر کر دیا تو یہ کفیل سے مؤخر ہوگا۔ اور اگر کفیل سے مؤخر کیا تو یہ اس سے مؤخر کرنا نہیں ہوگا ۔ جس پر اصل دین ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مؤخر کرنا ایک وقت معین تک بری کرنا ہوتا ہے تو دائمی طور پر بری کرنے پر قیاس کیا جائیگا۔ برخلاف اس کے جب فی الحال واجب الاداء مال کا ایک ماہ کی میعاد تھہرا کر فیل ہوا۔ تو یہ اصیل سے بھی مؤجل ہو گا۔ کیونکہ کفالہ موجود ہونے کی حالت میں مکفول لا کا سوائے قرضہ کے کوئی حق نہیں ہے تو میعادای قرضہ میں داخل ہوگئی رہا یہاں تو اس کے خلاف ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مکول لا نے اصیل یعنی مکفول عنہ سے مطالبہ دین کو ایک وقت معینہ تک کے لئے مؤخر کیا تو یہ کنیل سے بھی مؤخر ہو جائے گا۔ چنانچہ میعاد مقررہ تک کفیل سے بھی مطالبہ کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر مکفول لڑ نے کفیل سے مطالبہ کو ایک وقت معینہ تک کے لئے مؤخر کر دیا تو یہ مشول عند سے موخر کرنا نہ ہوگا۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ مؤخر کرنا چونکہ ایک مدت تک کے لئے مطالبہ کو ساقط کرنا ہے اس لئے یہ ایک وقت معین تک کے لئے بری کرنا ہوا۔ حاصل یہ کہ ایک مدت تک کے لئے مطالبہ کو مؤخر کرنا چونکہ ابراء مؤقت ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو ابراء مؤبد ( دائمی طور سے بری کرنے ) پر قیاس کیا جائے گا۔ اور ابراء مؤبد کی صورت میں چونکہ مکفول عنہ کو بری کرنے سے کفیل بری ہو جاتا ہے اور کفیل کو بری کرنے سے مکفول عنہ بری نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے اس طرح ابراء موقت میں بھی مکفول عنہ کو پری کرنے سے کھیل بری ہو جائیگا۔ مگر کفیل کو بری کرنے سے ملقول عنہ برگی نہ ہوگا۔
If the creditor postpones the debt from the principal debtor, then it is also postponed from the surety.
Similarly, if the creditor postpones from the principal, it is a postponement from the surety. And if he postpones from the surety, it is not a postponement from the one upon whom is the original debt, because postponement is a temporary release, so it is analogized to permanent release. Contrary to the case where one becomes surety for a present due wealth with a one-month term, then it is deferred from the principal, because the creditor has no right except the debt at the time of the existence of the kafala, so the term became included in it. But here it is opposite.
Translation: Similarly, if the creditor postponed the debt from the principal debtor, then it will be postponed from the surety. And if he postponed from the surety, then it will not be a postponement from the one upon whom is the original debt. Because postponement is a release for a fixed time, so it is analogized to permanent release. Contrary to the case where he became surety for a present due property with a one-month term, then it is deferred from the principal, because at the time of the kafala the creditor has no right except the debt, so the term entered into it. But here it is opposite.
Commentary on the scenario: If the creditor postponed the demand for the debt from the principal (i.e., the principal debtor) for a specific time, then it will also be postponed from the surety. Accordingly, until the fixed time, the creditor will have no right to demand from the surety. And if the creditor postponed the demand from the surety for a specific time, then it will not be a postponement from the principal debtor.
The evidence: Because postponement is the removal of the right to demand for a period, therefore it is a release for a fixed time. The conclusion: Since postponing the demand for a period is a temporary release (ibra mu'aqqat), it will be analogized to permanent release (ibra mu'abbad). And in the case of permanent release, when the principal debtor is released, the surety is released; and when the surety is released, the principal debtor is not released. Similarly, in temporary release, when the principal debtor is released (i.e., postponed), the surety is released (i.e., postponed), but when the surety is released, the principal debtor is not released.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on the effect of postponement (ta'khir) in suretyship. The rule mirrors that of release (ibra): postponement granted to the principal debtor also postpones the surety's liability, but postponement granted to the surety does not extend to the principal debtor. The proof is via qiyas: temporary release (ta'khir) is analogized to permanent release (ibra), because both involve suspending the right to demand. The text distinguishes this from a case where the suretyship itself is contracted with a term (e.g., 'I guarantee this present debt but payable in one month'). In that case, the term applies to both the principal and the surety, because the contract itself included the deferment. But in the scenario of subsequent postponement after the contract, the same rule as ibra applies. This is an important nuance: the timing of the deferment matters. The Hanafi position ensures that the surety's liability is directly tied to the principal's; any indulgence given to the principal automatically benefits the surety, but the surety cannot independently grant indulgence to the principal.

Key Terms
ابراء مؤقت (ibra mu'aqqat): Temporary release; postponement of the right to demand for a fixed period.
تأخير (ta'khir): Postponement; deferring the time of payment or demand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the creditor grants a one-month postponement to the surety, what effect does it have on the principal debtor?
A) The principal debtor also gets a one-month postponement
B) The principal debtor's obligation is unaffected
C) The principal debtor becomes liable immediately
D) The suretyship is terminated

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, postponement (ta'khir) in suretyship mirrors the rules of permanent release (ibra): postponement from the principal extends to the surety, but postponement from the surety does not affect the principal.

Kafalah — Surety

Discharging the Principal Discharges the Surety
Ruling on the effect of ibra' between asil and kafil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on the effect of discharging the principal (asil) or surety (kafil) in a kafalah contract and apply the principle of subsidiarity (taba'iyya) to explain why discharging the surety does not discharge the principal.

Core Idea
Discharging the principal debtor discharges the surety; discharging the surety does not discharge the principal.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a critical distinction in kafalah: the relationship between the principal debtor (asil) and the surety (kafil). The asil is primary, the kafil is subsidiary. This legal relationship determines the effect of discharge (ibra'). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the law of suretyship and avoiding confusion between kafalah and hawalah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties in kafalah
Recognize the asil (principal debtor) and kafil (surety). The kafil guarantees the debt of the asil to the creditor.
The asil bears primary liability; the kafil is secondary.
2
Understand the objection presented
The objection claims that if discharge of the asil is a condition at inception, then the asil is discharged but the kafil is not, suggesting that discharge of asil does not necessarily discharge kafil.
The answer distinguishes kafalah from hawalah (transfer of debt).
3
Analyze the first proof: subsidiarity
The kafil is a subsidiary (tabi') of the asil. Discharging the subsidiary does not affect the principal. Reversing this would make the asil a subsidiary of its own subsidiary, which is logically invalid.
4
Analyze the second proof: nature of obligation
The kafil owes only the demand (mutalaba), not the debt itself. The debt remains on the asil even if the kafil dies or is discharged. Thus, discharging the kafil's demand does not remove the debt from the asil.
5
Conclude the ruling
Based on these proofs, the Hanafi ruling is established: discharging the asil discharges the kafil, but discharging the kafil does not discharge the asil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتراض ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر ابتدائے کفالہ میں براءۃ اصیل کو شرط قرار دیدیا گیا تو یہاں برکت اصیل موجود ہے لیکن یہ برأت کفیل کوستلزم نہیں ہے پس اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ براءة اصیل، براء ت کفیل کو مستلزم نہیں ہوتا۔ اس کا جواب پہلے گزر چکا کہ اگر ابتدائے کفالہ میں برکت اصیل کی شرط لگادی گئی تو یہ کفالہ نہ ہوگا بلکہ حوالہ ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ کفالہ بشرط برات اصیل کفالہ ہوتا ہے۔ اور اگر مکفول لڑ نے کفیل کو بری کیا تو اصیل یعنی مغول عنہ قرضہ سے بری نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کفیل مکفول عنہ کا تابع ہے اور مکفول عنہ تابع نہیں ہے پس اگر کفیل کو بری کرنے سے اصیل کو بری کر دیا جائے تو اصیل کا اپنے تابع کا تابع ہونا لازم آئے گا حالانکہ یہ قلب موضوع ہے اس لئے کہا گیا کہ کفیل کو بری کرنے سے اصیل بری نہ ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفیل پر صرف مطالبہ واجب ہوتا ہے اصل قرضہ واجہ نہیں ہوتا اور اصیل پر قرضہ کا باقی رہنا اس وقت بھی جائز ہے جبکہ کفیل ہی نہ ہو۔ جیسے کفالہ سے پہلے اصیل پر قرضہ موجود تھا یا نفیل مر گیا تو اصیل سے قرضہ ساقط نہیں ہوتا۔ پس اسی طرح اصیل پر اس وقت بھی قرضہ باقی رہے گا جبکہ کفیل کو مطالبہ سے بری کر دیا گیا ہو ۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ تفصیل کے بری ہونے سے اصیل یعنی مغول عند دین سے بری نہ ہوگا۔
Objection is that if at the inception of kafalah, the discharge (ibra) of the principal (asil) was made a condition, then here the discharge of the asil is present, but this does not necessitate the discharge of the surety (kafil). So it is learned from this that discharge of the asil does not necessitate discharge of the kafil. Its answer has already passed that if at the inception of kafalah the condition of discharge of the asil is placed, then this is not kafalah but rather becomes hawalah. Because kafalah with the condition of discharge of the asil is kafalah. And if the creditor (mukful lahu) discharges the kafil, then the asil (the one on whose behalf the debt is owed) will not be discharged from the debt. Because the kafil is a subsidiary (tabi') of the asil, and the asil is not a subsidiary. So if discharging the kafil were to also discharge the asil, then it would necessitate that the asil becomes a subsidiary of its subsidiary, and this reverses the intended order. Therefore it is said that discharging the kafil does not discharge the asil. The second proof is that only the right to demand payment becomes obligatory on the kafil, not the actual debt, and it is permissible for the debt to remain on the asil even if there is no kafil. Just as before kafalah the debt existed on the asil, or if the kafil dies, the debt is not removed from the asil. So likewise, the debt will remain on the asil even when the kafil has been discharged from the demand. So it is established that the disengagement of the kafil does not discharge the asil, i.e., the one on whose behalf the debt is owed.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the effect of discharge (ibra') in a kafalah contract. The author addresses an objection: if the creditor discharges the principal debtor (asil), the surety (kafil) is also discharged because the kafil is a subsidiary. But if the creditor discharges only the kafil, the asil is not discharged. The proof is twofold: (1) the kafil is a subsidiary; making the asil a subsidiary of its subsidiary would reverse the legal order; (2) the kafil owes only the demand (mutalaba), not the debt itself, so discharging the demand does not affect the debt on the asil. This is a standard Hanafi ruling based on istihsan and the principle of taba'iyya (subsidiarity).

Key Terms
ibra' (ibra'): Legal discharge or release from a debt or obligation, whether permanent or temporary.
kafil (kafil): The surety who guarantees the debt or obligation of another (asil).
asil (asil): The principal debtor or the person on whose behalf the kafalah is made.
tabi' (tabi'): Subsidiary, dependent, or secondary; the legal principle that the subsidiary follows the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the creditor discharges the surety (kafil) without discharging the principal debtor (asil), does the asil become free from the debt?
A) Yes, because the surety is the one demanding payment.
B) No, because the kafil is only a subsidiary and discharging the subsidiary does not discharge the principal.
C) Yes, because the debt is considered satisfied.
D) No, but only if the surety agrees.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi kafalah, discharging the subsidiary (kafil) does not discharge the principal (asil); discharging the principal discharges the subsidiary.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
Deferment of Demand from Principal Defers from Surety
Ruling on ta'khir with qiyas to ibra' mu'abbad and defense of the analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deferment in kafalah and apply the analogy (qiyas) between temporary discharge (ibra' mu'aqqat) and permanent discharge (ibra' mu'abbad).

Core Idea
Deferring demand from the principal automatically defers from the surety, but not vice versa, based on analogy to permanent discharge.

This lesson examines the effect of deferment (ta'khir) of demand in the contract of suretyship (kafalah). The Hanafi school distinguishes between deferring from the principal (asil) and from the surety (kafil). Using the tool of qiyas, it draws an analogy to permanent discharge (ibra' mu'abbad) to derive the ruling, and then defends this analogy against a potential objection.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the two limbs: deferment from the principal defers from the surety; deferment from the surety does not defer from the principal.
2
Identify the proof: qiyas
Recognize that ta'khir (temporary discharge) is analogized to ibra' mu'abbad (permanent discharge) because both involve dropping the demand (isqat al-mutalaba).
3
Break down the qiyas
Identify the elements: asl = ibra' mu'abbad, far' = ta'khir, illa = dropping the demand. Confirm that the ruling on the asl (discharging asil discharges kafil, but not vice versa) applies to the far'.
4
Address the objection
Consider the objection that ibra' mu'abbad and ta'khir differ in rejectability. Then analyze the Hanafi response: qiyas does not require full identity; unity in the effective cause is sufficient.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical consequence: if the creditor defers from the surety, the creditor can still demand from the principal immediately. Know that this is the mufta bihi position.

And likewise, if the creditor defers (the debt) from the principal (asil), it is a deferment from the surety (kafil). And if he defers from the kafil, it is not a deferment from the one upon whom is the original debt. Because deferment is a temporary discharge (ibra' mu'aqqat), so it is considered analogous to permanent discharge (ibra' mu'abbad). Contrary to when one becomes surety for an immediately due debt with a deferment of one month, then it is deferred from the asil because he has no right except the debt at the time of kafalah, so the term enters into it. But here it is otherwise. Translation: And similarly, if the creditor deferred the debt from the asil, then it is deferred from the kafil. And if he deferred from the kafil, it is not a deferment from he upon whom is the original debt. Because deferment is freeing for a specified time, so it is analogized to permanent freeing. Contrary to when the surety is for an immediately due wealth (debt) with a term of one month, then it becomes deferred from the asil because at the time of kafalah there is no right but the debt, so the term enters into it. Here it is the opposite. Explanation: The case is that if the creditor deferred the demand of the debt from the asil for a specified time, then it is also deferred from the kafil. So until the appointed term, the creditor has no right to demand from the kafil. And if the creditor deferred the demand from the kafil for a specified time, it is not a deferment from the asil. The proof is that deferral, since it is a dropping of the demand for a period, is a temporary discharge. So it is analogized to permanent discharge. In case of permanent discharge, discharging the asil discharges the kafil, but discharging the kafil does not discharge the asil. So likewise, in temporary discharge, discharging the asil will discharge the kafil, but discharging the kafil will not discharge the asil. Question: Here a question arises: there is a great difference between permanent discharge (ibra' mu'abbad) and temporary discharge (ibra' mu'aqqat) regarding the kafil, because if the kafil rejects permanent discharge, it is not rejected; rather the discharge is established and the demand is dropped from the kafil. But temporary discharge, if the kafil rejects it, it is rejected, and the demand to pay the guaranteed amount remains obligatory on him. So with such a difference, how is it correct to analogize temporary discharge to permanent discharge? Answer: Its answer is that for analogy (qiyas) it is not a condition that there be complete unity and equality in all respects between the analogized (muqayas) and the analogized-upon (muqayas 'alayh). Rather, it is sufficient that unity and equality be present in one aspect. And such unity exists here, in that in permanent discharge the demand is dropped, and in temporary discharge the demand is also dropped. So the dropping of demand is found in both. Even though in permanent discharge it is dropped permanently, and in temporary discharge it is dropped for a specified time, when unity exists in this aspect, there is no harm in analogizing temporary discharge to permanent discharge. As for why permanent discharge is not rejected by the kafil's rejection, and temporary discharge is rejected, the reason is that permanent discharge is pure dropping (isqat) regarding the kafil; it contains no element of ownership (tamlik), and isqat does not require acceptance. Therefore, permanent discharge is not rejected even if the kafil rejects it. Temporary discharge is merely a deferment of demand; it is not of the category of isqat. And whatever is not from the category of isqat is rejected by rejection. Therefore, temporary discharge is rejected by rejection.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the effect of deferment (ta'khir) of demand in kafalah, along with a detailed qiyas discussion. The ruling states: if the creditor defers the demand from the principal debtor (asil), it also defers from the surety (kafil); but if he defers from the kafil, it does not defer from the asil. This is established by analogy to permanent discharge (ibra' mu'abbad). A question arises: permanent discharge is an isqat (dropping) that does not require acceptance, so it cannot be rejected; temporary discharge is not an isqat, so it can be rejected by the kafil. The answer is that qiyas does not require complete identity in all aspects; it is sufficient that both share the same effective cause ('illa) of dropping the demand. The difference in rejectability is due to the nature of isqat vs. ta'khir, but the underlying commonality supports the ruling.

Key Terms
ta'khir (ta'khir): Deferment of the demand for payment for a specified period; a temporary discharge.
ibra' mu'abbad (ibra' mu'abbad): Permanent discharge from a debt or obligation; an isqat (dropping) that does not require acceptance.
ibra' mu'aqqat (ibra' mu'aqqat): Temporary discharge, such as deferment of demand; not a pure isqat and is subject to rejection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence if the creditor defers demand from the surety only?
A) The principal is also deferred for the same period.
B) The principal is not deferred and can be demanded immediately.
C) The surety is discharged forever.
D) The surety's debt is forgiven.

Key Takeaway
Deferment from the principal automatically includes the surety, but deferment from the surety does not affect the principal, based on analogy to the rule of permanent discharge.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
6 min
Surety for a Current Debt with a Term: Exception
Exception when kafalah includes a term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a term included in the original kafalah contract and a later deferment, and apply the Hanafi ruling on deferred demand.

Core Idea
When the surety contract includes a payment term, the term becomes part of the debt, deferring it for both principal and surety.

In the previous lesson, we learned that if the creditor defers the demand from the surety after the contract, the principal debtor remains immediately liable. However, an exception arises when the surety contract itself includes a term. This lesson examines that exception and the legal reasoning behind it, demonstrating how the term attaches to the original debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First, recall the standard rule: if the creditor delays demanding payment from the surety after the contract, the principal debtor is still immediately liable. Now consider the exception: if the surety contract from the start includes a term (e.g., one month) for an otherwise immediate debt.
The key is timing: before or after the contract.
2
Locate the key difference
In the exception, the term is part of the contract itself. The surety attributed the term to the debt, not just to his own liability. In the standard case, the deferment is a separate act after the contract.
The term in the contract modifies the underlying debt obligation.
3
Trace the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
At the moment of kafalah, the creditor's only right is the debt itself (not the right to demand from the surety, which hasn't yet arisen). Therefore, when the surety stipulates a term, it attaches to the debt, which is owed by the principal. Hence the term applies to both.
The Hanafi principle: the term becomes part of the debt, not an independent arrangement.
4
Apply to a concrete example
Example: Hamid owes Khalid 100 dinars due immediately. Wasef becomes surety with a one-month term. The creditor cannot demand payment from either Hamid or Wasef before the month ends.
Contrast with: if Wasef had become surety without a term, and later Khalid grants him a delay, Hamid remains immediately liable.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The established Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) is that the term in the contract is binding on both the surety and the principal debtor. This is the relied-upon view for fatwa.
Some schools may differ, but the Hanafi school is consistent on this distinction.

Source Text

Contrary to when he becomes surety for an immediately due wealth (debt) with a term of one month, then it is deferred from the asil because he has no right except the debt at the time of kafalah, so the term enters into it. But here it is the opposite. Translation: Contrary to when the surety is for an immediately due debt with a term of one month, then it becomes deferred from the asil because at the time of kafalah the creditor has no right but the debt, so the term enters into the debt. Here it is the opposite. 'Contrary to when he becomes surety...' is an answer to an implied question. The implied question is: You said that if the demand is deferred from the kafil, it is not deferred from the asil. But this is false because if someone becomes surety for a debt that is immediately due but he accepts the suretyship with a one-month term, for example, Khalid has one hundred dinars immediately due from Hamid, and Wasef [or 'Abd] becomes surety with a one-month term, then in this case just as the demand is deferred from the kafil, similarly it is deferred from the asil (the person on whose behalf the debt is owed). So it is proven that if the demand is deferred from the kafil, it is also deferred from the asil. The answer: The answer is that in this case, at the time of the existence of the kafalah, the creditor has no right except the debt, because the right to demand that arises from the kafalah is not yet established. So the term enters into the original debt, because the surety attributed the term to the debt itself. Thus the debt became deferred. And since the debt is established on the liability of the asil, when the original debt is deferred, this term is established for both the asil and the kafil. As for the issue in the text (matn), there the kafalah existed first, then after that the creditor deferred from the kafil that right to demand which he had obtained due to the kafalah. This does not necessitate the deferment of the original debt. And when the deferment of the original debt is not necessitated, the creditor can still demand from the asil immediately. And from the kafil, since the demand has been deferred, he has no right to demand immediately.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage clarifies an exception to the previous rule: if the surety contract itself includes a term (ajal) for a debt that is otherwise immediately due, then that term applies to both the principal debtor (asil) and the surety (kafil). The reason is that the term becomes part of the debt itself because the surety's guarantee is from the start conditional upon the term. This is different from the earlier case where the creditor unilaterally defers from the kafil after the contract. In that case, the original debt remains immediately due from the asil. The explanation uses an example: if the creditor has a debt of 100 dinars due immediately from Hamid, and someone becomes surety with a one-month term, the term applies to both; the creditor cannot demand from either before one month. But if the surety contract was without term, and later the creditor defers from the surety, the asil remains liable immediately.

Key Terms
ajal (ajal): The agreed-upon term or period for payment of a debt, which enters into the debt itself.
mal hal (mal hal): Wealth or debt that is immediately due and payable (mutualajj), as opposed to deferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a surety contract for an immediately due debt includes a one-month term, when can the creditor demand payment from the principal debtor?
A) Immediately, because the debt was originally due.
B) After one month, because the term applies to both surety and principal.
C) Only from the surety, not from the principal.
D) At any time, regardless of the term.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a term included in the original kafalah contract extends to the principal debtor's obligation, deferring it equally.
