Distinction Between Absolute and Temporary Discharge in Kafalah
Explaining the difference between ibra' mu'abbad and muwaqqat with qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the difference between ibra' mu'abbad and ibra' muwaqqat in Hanafi fiqh and explain why qiyas between them is valid despite the difference in permanence.

Core Idea
Absolute discharge is pure isqat; temporary discharge is a postponement – only the shared 'illa of dropping the claim makes qiyas valid.

This lesson addresses a common objection: how can temporary discharge be analogized to absolute discharge when they differ in being rejectable? We will unpack the Hanafi answer, which hinges on the nature of isqat and the scope of qiyas. Understanding this distinction clarifies crucial rules in kafalah and the concept of waiver in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of discharge
In the text, identify ibra' mu'abbad (absolute) and ibra' muwaqqat (temporary) and their key difference: absolute cannot be rejected by the guarantor, temporary can be rejected.
The text states that ibra' mu'abbad is not rejected by the guarantor's rejection, while ibra' muwaqqat is rejected.
2
Understand the objection against qiyas
The objector argues that because the two types differ in rejectability (permanent vs. temporary), analogizing one to the other is invalid.
The objection relies on the assumption that qiyas requires identity in all aspects.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response on qiyas
The response states that qiyas only requires a shared effective cause ('illa) in one respect. Here, both types share the dropping of the claim (isqat al-mutalaba), even if one is permanent and the other temporary.
This is a key Hanafi usul principle: qiyas does not require complete identity.
4
Explain why absolute discharge is not rejectable
Absolute discharge is pure isqat (waiver), which does not require acceptance or rejection. Temporary discharge is merely ta'khir (postponement), not isqat, so it can be rejected.
The text explicitly distinguishes between isqat and ta'khir.
5
Apply the rule to a hypothetical
Consider a creditor who gives absolute discharge: the claim is dropped permanently regardless of the guarantor's rejection. If temporary discharge is given, the guarantor may reject it and the claim remains due after the term.
This practical consequence reinforces the distinction.

جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں وجود کفالہ کے وقت مکفول لہ کا سوائے قرضہ کے کوئی حق نہیں ہے کیونکہ مطالبہ جو کفالہ کی وجہ سے حاصل ہوگا وہ ابھی تک ثابت نہیں ہوا تو اجل ( میعاد) اصل دین میں داخل ہوئی کیونکہ کفیل نے اجل بنفس دین کی طرف منسوب کی ہے تو دین یعنی قرضہ مؤجل ہوا اور دین چونکہ مکفول عنہ کے ذمہ ثابت ہوتا ہے اسلئے جب اصل دین مؤجل ہوا تو یہ اجل مکفول عنہ اور کفیل دونوں کے حق میں ثابت ہوگی اور رہا متن کا مسئلہ تو اس میں کفالہ پہلے ہے پھر اس کے بعد مکفول لہ نے کفیل سے اس مطالبہ کو مؤخر کیا ہے جو مطالبہ اس کو کفالہ کی وجہ سے حاصل ہوا تھا اور اس سے اصل دین کا مؤخر ہونا لازم نہیں آتا۔ اور جب اصل دین کا مؤخر ہونا لازم نہیں آیا تو مکفول لہ مکفول عنہ سے بدستور فی الحال مطالبہ کر سکتا ہے۔ اور کفیل سے چونکہ مطالبہ کو مؤخر کر دیا گیا اس لئے اس سے فی الحال مطالبہ کا حق نہ ہوگا۔
Book of Kafalah. Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume 9. Here there is a question: There is a great difference between ibra' mu'abbad (absolute discharge) and ibra' muwaqqat (temporary discharge) with respect to the guarantor (kafil). Because if the guarantor rejects ibra' mu'abbad, it is not rejected by his rejection; rather the discharge is established and the claim against him is dropped. And ibra' muwaqqat is rejected by the guarantor's rejection, and the demand for payment of the guaranteed sum remains wajib upon him. So given this difference, how can it be correct to analogize ibra' muwaqqat to ibra' mu'abbad? Answer: The answer to this is that for qiyas, equality and identity in every respect between the analogized (maqis) and the analogized-upon (maqis 'alayh) is not a condition. Rather, the existence of identity and equality in some one aspect is sufficient for qiyas, and that much identity exists here: that in ibra' mu'abbad the claim is dropped, and in ibra' muwaqqat also the claim is dropped. So it is found that the dropping of the claim is present in both the analogized and the analogized-upon, although in ibra' mu'abbad the claim is dropped permanently, and in ibra' muwaqqat it is dropped for a specified time. So when identity exists in this respect, there is no harm in analogizing ibra' muwaqqat to ibra' mu'abbad. As for why ibra' mu'abbad is not rejected by the guarantor's rejection, and why ibra' muwaqqat is rejected: the reason is that ibra' mu'abbad with respect to the guarantor is pure isqat (waiver), and it has no element of tamlik (transfer of ownership) at all, and isqat does not require acceptance or rejection. Therefore, ibra' mu'abbad is not rejected despite the guarantor's rejection. And ibra' muwaqqat is merely a postponement of the claim (ta'khir al-mutalaba); it is not of the category of isqatat. And whatever is not of the category of isqatat is rejected if rejected. Therefore ibra' muwaqqat is rejected if rejected. Contrary to what if he stood surety for a present debt... This is an answer to a hypothetical question. The hypothetical question: You said that if the claim against the guarantor is postponed, it is not postponed against the original debtor (asil). But this is incorrect because if a person becomes guarantor for a property that is immediately due, but he accepted the guarantee with a term of one month—for example, Hamid owes Khalid one hundred dinars immediately due, but Wasif accepted the guarantee with a term of one month—then in this case, just as the claim against the guarantor is postponed, similarly it is postponed against the original debtor (makful 'anhu). So the creditor (makful lahu) has no right to demand immediately from the original debtor. Thus it is established that if the claim against the guarantor is postponed, it will be postponed against the original debtor as well. Answer: The answer to this is that in this case, at the time of the existence of the guarantee, the creditor has no right except the debt itself, because the claim (mutalaba) that arises through the guarantee is not yet established. So the term entered into the original debt because the guarantor attributed the term to the debt itself. So the debt (the loan) became deferred. And since the debt is established on the liability of the original debtor, when the original debt was deferred, this term applies to both the original debtor and the guarantor. As for the issue in the text (matn), the guarantee came first, and then after that the creditor postponed the claim against the guarantor that had arisen due to the guarantee, and this does not necessitate the postponement of the original debt. And when the original debt is not necessarily postponed, the creditor can still demand it immediately from the original debtor. And from the guarantor, since the claim was postponed, he has no right to demand immediately.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof. It begins with a hypothetical objection regarding the distinction between absolute discharge (ibra' mu'abbad) and temporary discharge (ibra' muwaqqat) in the context of kafalah. The objector argues that since these two types differ in that absolute discharge cannot be rejected while temporary discharge can, analogizing temporary to absolute is invalid. The answer clarifies a key principle of Hanafi usul: qiyas does not require identity in all aspects; a shared effective cause ('illa) in one respect is sufficient. Here, both types share the dropping of the claim (isqat al-mutalaba), though one is permanent and the other temporary. The difference in rejectability is explained: absolute discharge is pure isqat, which does not require acceptance, while temporary discharge is merely a postponement (ta'khir), not isqat, and thus can be rejected. The passage then addresses a second hypothetical: if the guarantor accepts a guarantee with a term, does that defer the claim against the original debtor? The answer distinguishes: if the term is attached to the debt itself (e.g., the guarantor says 'I guarantee this debt with a one-month term'), the debt becomes deferred for both. But if the guarantee was already in place and then the creditor postpones the claim against the guarantor alone, that does not defer the original debt. The passage thus clarifies nuanced rules of kafalah.

Key Terms
ابراء مؤبد (ibra' mu'abbad): Absolute discharge that waives the claim permanently and cannot be rejected by the guarantor.
ابراء مؤقت (ibra' muwaqqat): Temporary discharge that postpones the claim for a set time and can be rejected by the guarantor.
اسقاط (isqat): The act of waiving a right or claim, which in Hanafi law does not require acceptance to be effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is ibra' mu'abbad not rejected by the guarantor's rejection?
A) Because it is a transfer of ownership (tamlik)
B) Because it is a pure waiver (isqat) that does not require acceptance
C) Because it is a postponement (ta'khir)
D) Because the creditor did not intend to give it

Key Takeaway
Absolute discharge is an isqat that cannot be rejected; temporary discharge is a postponement that can be rejected, and qiyas between them is valid because they share the 'illa of dropping the claim.

The Effect of Postponing the Claim Against the Guarantor on the Original Debtor
Explaining the effect of postponement on the original debtor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between two scenarios of postponement in kafalah and determine whether the original debtor is also deferred.

Core Idea
If the term is attached to the debt itself, both debtor and guarantor are deferred; if the claim is postponed after guarantee, only the guarantor is deferred.

This lesson resolves a second hypothetical: when a guarantor accepts a guarantee with a term, does that defer the original debtor as well? The answer depends on whether the term is linked to the debt or to the claim arising from the guarantee. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly advising parties in kafalah contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Scenario A: The guarantor accepts the guarantee with a term (e.g., one month) from the outset. Scenario B: The guarantee was established without a term, and later the creditor postpones the claim against the guarantor.
The text contrasts these in the hypothetical question and answer.
2
Analyze Scenario A
When the guarantor accepts with a term, the term is attributed to the debt itself, so the debt becomes deferred for both the original debtor and the guarantor.
The text says: 'the term entered into the original debt'.
3
Analyze Scenario B
When the guarantee is already in place and the creditor postpones the claim against the guarantor, this postponement only affects the guarantor; the original debt remains due from the original debtor.
The text: 'this does not necessitate the postponement of the original debt'.
4
Understand the rationale
In Scenario A, the term is attached to the debt because the guarantor's acceptance of the guarantee with a term modifies the debt itself. In Scenario B, the postponement is a separate act that only concerns the claim arising from the guarantee.
The distinction hinges on whether the term relates to the original debt or the guarantee claim.
5
Apply the rule
Given a case, determine whether the term was part of the guarantee agreement from the beginning or was added later. Then apply the respective ruling.
Practice with the example in the text: Wasif guarantees Hamid's debt with one-month term vs. after guarantee, creditor tells Wasif: 'I postpone my claim against you'.

جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قیاس کے لئے مقیس اور مقیس علیہ کے درمیان من کل وجہ اتحاد اور مساوات شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ کسی ایک اعتبار سے اتحاد اور مساوات کا پایا جانا بھی قیاس کے لئے کافی ہے اور اتنا اتحاد یہاں موجود ہے اس طور پر کہ ابراء مؤبد میں بھی مطالبہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے اور ابراء موقت میں بھی مطالبہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے گویا مطالبہ کا ساقط ہو جانا مقیس اور منفیس عالیہ دونوں میں پایا گیا اگر چند ابراء مؤبد میں دائمی طور پر مطالبہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے اور ابراء موقت میں ایک وقت معینہ تک کے لئے ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس جب اس اعتبار سے اتحاد موجود ہے تو ابراء مؤقت کو ابراء مؤبد پر قیاس کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ ابراء مؤبد کفیل کے رد کرنے سے کیوں رد نہیں ہوتا ۔ اور ابراء مؤقت کیوں رد ہو جاتا ہے؟ تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ابراء مؤبد کفیل کے حق میں اسقاط محض ہے اس میں تملیک کے معنی بالکل نہیں پائے جاتے اور اسقاط رد و قبول نہیں کرتا اس لئے ابراء مؤبد کفیل کے رد کرنے کے باوجود رد نہیں ہوگا اور ابراء مؤقت فقط تا خیر مطالبہ کا نام ہے از قبیلۂ اسقاطات نہیں ہے اور جو چیز اسقاطات کے قبیلہ سے نہ ہو وہ رد کرنے سے رد ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے ابراء مؤقت رد کرنے سے رد ہو جائیگا۔
بخلاف ما اذا كفل بالمال الحال الخ سے ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال مقدر یہ ہے کہ آپ نے فرمایا کہ اگر کفیل سے مطالبہ کو مؤخر کر دیا گیا تو اصیل سے مؤخر نہیں ہوتا۔ حالانکہ یہ غلط ہے کیونکہ اگر کوئی شخص ایسے مال کا کفیل ہو جس کی ادائیگی فی الحال واجب ہے لیکن اس نے ایک ماہ کی مہلت پر کفالت قبول کی ۔ مثلاً حامد پر خالد کے ایک سو دینار فی الحال واجب الادا ہیں مگر وصف نے اس کی کفالت ایک ماہ کی مہلت پر قبول کی تو اس صورت میں جس طرح کفیل سے مطالبہ مؤخر ہوتا ہے اسی طرح اصیل یعنی مکفول عنہ سے بھی مؤخر ہو جاتا ہے چنانچہ مکفول لہ کو مکفول عنہ سے بھی بالفعل مطالبہ کا اختیار نہیں ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ اگر کفیل سے مطالبہ کو مؤخر کر دیا گیا تو مکفول عنہ سے بھی مؤخر ہو جائے گا۔
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں وجود کفالہ کے وقت مکفول لہ کا سوائے قرضہ کے کوئی حق نہیں ہے کیونکہ مطالبہ جو کفالہ کی وجہ سے حاصل ہوگا وہ ابھی تک ثابت نہیں ہوا تو اجل ( میعاد) اصل دین میں داخل ہوئی کیونکہ کفیل نے اجل بنفس دین کی طرف منسوب کی ہے تو دین یعنی قرضہ مؤجل ہوا اور دین چونکہ مکفول عنہ کے ذمہ ثابت ہوتا ہے اسلئے جب اصل دین مؤجل ہوا تو یہ اجل مکفول عنہ اور کفیل دونوں کے حق میں ثابت ہوگی اور رہا متن کا مسئلہ تو اس میں کفالہ پہلے ہے پھر اس کے بعد مکفول لہ نے کفیل سے اس مطالبہ کو مؤخر کیا ہے جو مطالبہ اس کو کفالہ کی وجہ سے حاصل ہوا تھا اور اس سے اصل دین کا مؤخر ہونا لازم نہیں آتا۔ اور جب اصل دین کا مؤخر ہونا لازم نہیں آیا تو مکفول لہ مکفول عنہ سے بدستور فی الحال مطالبہ کر سکتا ہے۔ اور کفیل سے چونکہ مطالبہ کو مؤخر کر دیا گیا اس لئے اس سے فی الحال مطالبہ کا حق نہ ہوگا۔
Book of Kafalah. Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume 9. Here there is a question: There is a great difference between ibra' mu'abbad (absolute discharge) and ibra' muwaqqat (temporary discharge) with respect to the guarantor (kafil). Because if the guarantor rejects ibra' mu'abbad, it is not rejected by his rejection; rather the discharge is established and the claim against him is dropped. And ibra' muwaqqat is rejected by the guarantor's rejection, and the demand for payment of the guaranteed sum remains wajib upon him. So given this difference, how can it be correct to analogize ibra' muwaqqat to ibra' mu'abbad? Answer: The answer to this is that for qiyas, equality and identity in every respect between the analogized (maqis) and the analogized-upon (maqis 'alayh) is not a condition. Rather, the existence of identity and equality in some one aspect is sufficient for qiyas, and that much identity exists here: that in ibra' mu'abbad the claim is dropped, and in ibra' muwaqqat also the claim is dropped. So it is found that the dropping of the claim is present in both the analogized and the analogized-upon, although in ibra' mu'abbad the claim is dropped permanently, and in ibra' muwaqqat it is dropped for a specified time. So when identity exists in this respect, there is no harm in analogizing ibra' muwaqqat to ibra' mu'abbad. As for why ibra' mu'abbad is not rejected by the guarantor's rejection, and why ibra' muwaqqat is rejected: the reason is that ibra' mu'abbad with respect to the guarantor is pure isqat (waiver), and it has no element of tamlik (transfer of ownership) at all, and isqat does not require acceptance or rejection. Therefore, ibra' mu'abbad is not rejected despite the guarantor's rejection. And ibra' muwaqqat is merely a postponement of the claim (ta'khir al-mutalaba); it is not of the category of isqatat. And whatever is not of the category of isqatat is rejected if rejected. Therefore ibra' muwaqqat is rejected if rejected. Contrary to what if he stood surety for a present debt... This is an answer to a hypothetical question. The hypothetical question: You said that if the claim against the guarantor is postponed, it is not postponed against the original debtor (asil). But this is incorrect because if a person becomes guarantor for a property that is immediately due, but he accepted the guarantee with a term of one month—for example, Hamid owes Khalid one hundred dinars immediately due, but Wasif accepted the guarantee with a term of one month—then in this case, just as the claim against the guarantor is postponed, similarly it is postponed against the original debtor (makful 'anhu). So the creditor (makful lahu) has no right to demand immediately from the original debtor. Thus it is established that if the claim against the guarantor is postponed, it will be postponed against the original debtor as well. Answer: The answer to this is that in this case, at the time of the existence of the guarantee, the creditor has no right except the debt itself, because the claim (mutalaba) that arises through the guarantee is not yet established. So the term entered into the original debt because the guarantor attributed the term to the debt itself. So the debt (the loan) became deferred. And since the debt is established on the liability of the original debtor, when the original debt was deferred, this term applies to both the original debtor and the guarantor. As for the issue in the text (matn), the guarantee came first, and then after that the creditor postponed the claim against the guarantor that had arisen due to the guarantee, and this does not necessitate the postponement of the original debt. And when the original debt is not necessarily postponed, the creditor can still demand it immediately from the original debtor. And from the guarantor, since the claim was postponed, he has no right to demand immediately.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof. It begins with a hypothetical objection regarding the distinction between absolute discharge (ibra' mu'abbad) and temporary discharge (ibra' muwaqqat) in the context of kafalah. The objector argues that since these two types differ in that absolute discharge cannot be rejected while temporary discharge can, analogizing temporary to absolute is invalid. The answer clarifies a key principle of Hanafi usul: qiyas does not require identity in all aspects; a shared effective cause ('illa) in one respect is sufficient. Here, both types share the dropping of the claim (isqat al-mutalaba), though one is permanent and the other temporary. The difference in rejectability is explained: absolute discharge is pure isqat, which does not require acceptance, while temporary discharge is merely a postponement (ta'khir), not isqat, and thus can be rejected. The passage then addresses a second hypothetical: if the guarantor accepts a guarantee with a term, does that defer the claim against the original debtor? The answer distinguishes: if the term is attached to the debt itself (e.g., the guarantor says 'I guarantee this debt with a one-month term'), the debt becomes deferred for both. But if the guarantee was already in place and then the creditor postpones the claim against the guarantor alone, that does not defer the original debt. The passage thus clarifies nuanced rules of kafalah.

Key Terms
اجل (ajal): A fixed term or period of deferment; in kafalah, it can apply to the debt or to the claim.
مکفول عنہ (makful 'anhu): The original debtor for whom the guarantee is given.
مکفول لہ (makful lahu): The creditor who benefits from the guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a guarantor accepts a guarantee with a term (e.g., one month), what is the effect on the original debtor?
A) The original debtor must pay immediately.
B) The original debtor also gets a one-month deferment.
C) The guarantee becomes void because the debt is not yet due.
D) Only the guarantor is deferred.

Key Takeaway
If the guarantor accepts with a term, both debtor and guarantor are deferred; if the creditor later postpones the claim against the guarantor, only the guarantor is deferred.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
Settlement (Sulh) by the Guarantor: Four Scenarios and Their Effects
Ruling statement with commentary parsing four scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four scenarios of a guarantor's settlement with the creditor and determine the legal consequences for the guarantor and original debtor in each case.

Core Idea
A guarantor's settlement for less frees both him and the debtor proportionally only if the settlement is attributed to the debt itself.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling when a guarantor (kafil) settles a debt for a lower amount. The passage is a classical ruling statement with its commentary (tashrih) that breaks down the scenario into four distinct legal cases depending on the stipulations and the nature of the settlement item. Understanding these distinctions is vital for correctly analyzing guarantee contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the debt
Recognise the three key figures: creditor (rabb al-mal), guarantor (kafil), and original debtor (asil). The debt is the subject of the settlement.
The debt is owed by the asil, not the kafil; the kafil only bears a claim (mutalaba).
2
Distinguish the type of settlement
Determine whether the settlement is with the same genus (e.g., dirhams for dirhams) – treated as isqat (waiver) – or with a different genus (e.g., dirhams for goods) – treated as mubadala hukmiyya (virtual exchange).
This distinction affects the guarantor's right of recourse.
3
Analyse the four stipulation scenarios
The tashrih lists four cases: (1) stipulation to free both, (2) stipulation to free the debtor only, (3) stipulation to free the guarantor only, (4) no stipulation. Understand the ruling for each.
Scenarios 1 and 2 result in both being freed from the settled amount; scenario 3 frees only the guarantor; scenario 4 also frees both.
4
Apply the rule to determine discharge
For each scenario, determine who is freed from what amount and whether the creditor can still claim the remainder.
In scenarios 1 and 2, the creditor can recover the remaining five hundred from either party.
5
Evaluate the guarantor's recourse
Check if the guarantee was by the debtor's order (bi amrih). If so, the guarantor can recover the amount he paid from the debtor. If different genus, he recovers the full thousand.
If the settlement was about the claim against the guarantor himself, the debtor is not freed at all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن صالح الكفيل ربَّ المال عن الالف على خمس مائة فقد برئ الكفيل والذى عليه الأصل لأنه اضاف الصلح الى الالف الدين وهى على الاصيل فبرئ عن خمس مائة لانه اسقاط و براء ته توجب برأة الكفيل ثم برئا جميعاً عن خمس مائة باداء الكفيل ويرجع الكفيل على الاصيل بخمس مائة ان كانت الكفالة بأمره بخلاف ما اذا صالح على جنس آخر لأنه مبادلة حكمية فملكه فير جع بجميع الالف ولو كان صالحه ما استوجب بالكفالة لا يبرأ الاصيل لأن هذا ابراء الكفيل عن المطالبة
ترجمہ: پس اگر کفیل نے مکفول لہ سے ایک ہزار کے سلسلہ میں پانچ سوپر صلح کر لی تو کفیل اور وہ شخص جس پر اصل دین ہے دونوں بری ہو گئے کیونکہ کفیل نے صلح کو ایک ہزار دین کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے اور یہ ایک ہزار دین اصیل پر ہے تو اصیل پانچ سو سے بری ہو گیا کیونکہ صلح اسقاط ہے اور اصل کا بری ہونا کفیل کے بری ہونے کو واجب کرتا ہے پھر کفیل کے ادا کرنے سے اصیل اور کفیل دونوں پانچ سو سے بری ہو گئے اور کفیل اصیل سے پانچ سو درہم واپس لے گا بشرطیکہ کفالہ بامرہ ہو۔ بر خلاف اس کے جب جنسی آخر پر صلح کی ہو۔ اس لئے کہ یہ حکماً مبادلہ ہے پس کفیل ایک ہزار کا مالک ہو گیا تو وہ پورے ایک ہزار درہم واپس لے گا۔ اور اگر کفیل نے مکفول لہ سے اس حق کے بارے میں صلح کی جو کفالت کی وجہ سے اس پر واجب ہوا ہے تو اصیل بری نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ کفیل کو مطالبہ سے بری کرنا ہے۔
تشریح: اس مسئلہ کی چار صورتیں ہیں (1) کفیل نے مکفول لہ سے ایک ہزار درہم کے سلسلہ میں پانچ سو درہم پر صلح کی اور مکفول عنہ اور کفیل دونوں کے بری ہونے کی شرط لگائی۔ (2) یا خاص طور پر مکفول عنہ کے بری ہونے کی شرط لگائی۔ (3) یا خاص طور پر کفیل کے بری ہونے کی شرط لگائی۔ (4) یا کوئی شرط نہیں لگائی۔ پہلی اور دوسری صورت میں مکفول عنہ اور کفیل دونوں پانچ سو درہم سے بری ہو جائیں گے اور باقی پانچ سو درہم کا مطالبہ مکفول لہ کفیل سے بھی کر سکتا ہے اور مکفول عنہ سے بھی کر سکتا ہے۔ اور تیسری صورت میں پانچ سو درہم سے خاص طور پر کفیل بری ہوگا۔ اور مکفول عنہ پر ایک ہزار درہم علی حالہ باقی رہیں گے اور مکفول لہ کو اختیار ہو گا جی چاہے پورا قرضہ یعنی ایک ہزار درہم مکفول عنہ سے وصول کرے اور جی چاہے پانچ سو درہم کفیل سے اور پانچ سو درہم مکفول عنہ سے وصول کرے۔ اور چوتھی صورت (جو مسئلہ کتاب ہے) میں یعنی اگر کفیل نے مکفول لہ سے کہا کہ میں نے تجھ سے ایک ہزار درہم کے سلسلہ میں پانچ سو درہم پر صلح کی اور اس پر شرط وغیرہ کا اضافہ نہیں کیا تو کفیل اور مکفول عنہ دونوں پانچ سو درہم سے بری ہو جائیں گے۔ کیونکہ کفیل نے صلح کو قرضہ یعنی ایک ہزار کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے اور ایک ہزار درہم کا قرضہ اصیل یعنی مکفول عنہ پر ہے نہ کہ کفیل پر، کفیل پر تو صرف مطالبہ ہے، مطالبہ کے سوا کچھ نہیں ہے۔ پس جب ایک ہزار کا قرضہ مکفول عنہ پر ہے تو صلح کے نتیجے میں پانچ سو درہم مکفول عنہ کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو جائیں گے اور مکفول عنہ بری ہو جائے گا اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ مکفول عنہ کے بری ہونے سے کفیل بری ہو جاتا ہے اور جب مکفول عنہ کے بری ہونے سے کفیل بری
If the guarantor (kafil) settles with the creditor (rabb al-mal) concerning the thousand (debt) for five hundred, then the guarantor and the one upon whom the original debt lies (asil) both become free (bari'). Because the guarantor attributed the settlement to the thousand debt, and it (the debt) is upon the original debtor. So the original debtor becomes free from five hundred because it is an isqat (waiver), and his being free necessitates the freedom of the guarantor. Then both become free from five hundred by the payment of the guarantor, and the guarantor recovers five hundred from the original debtor if the guarantee was by his (the debtor's) order. Contrary to if he settled with a different genus (jins), because that is a virtual exchange (mubadala hukmiyya), so he (the guarantor) owns (the thousand) and recovers the entire thousand. And if he settled concerning the right that came due through the guarantee (i.e., the claim against himself), the original debtor does not become free; because this is an ibra' (discharge) of the guarantor from the claim. Translation: So if the guarantor settles with the creditor concerning the thousand for five hundred, then the guarantor and the person upon whom the original debt is (the original debtor) both become free. Because the guarantor attributed the settlement to the thousand debt, and this thousand debt is upon the original debtor. So the original debtor became free from five hundred because settlement is an isqat (waiver), and the original debtor's being free makes the guarantor's being free necessary. Then by the guarantor's payment, both the original debtor and the guarantor become free from five hundred. And the guarantor recovers five hundred from the original debtor on condition that the guarantee was by his order. Contrary to the case when he settled with a different genus. Because this is a virtual exchange, so the guarantor became the owner of the thousand, so he recovers the entire thousand dirhams. And if the guarantor settled with the creditor concerning the right that became due upon him through the guarantee, then the original debtor does not become free. Because this is an ibra' of the guarantor from the claim. Commentary: This issue has four scenarios: (1) The guarantor settled with the creditor concerning the thousand for five hundred and stipulated that both the original debtor and the guarantor are free. (2) Or he stipulated specifically the freedom of the original debtor. (3) Or he stipulated specifically the freedom of the guarantor. (4) Or he made no stipulation. In the first and second scenarios, both the original debtor and the guarantor become free from five hundred, and the creditor can demand the remaining five hundred from either the guarantor or the original debtor. In the third scenario, only the guarantor becomes free from five hundred specifically, and the original debtor remains liable for the full thousand. The creditor has the option to collect the full thousand from the original debtor, or collect five hundred from the guarantor and five hundred from the original debtor. In the fourth scenario (which is the issue in the book), i.e., if the guarantor said to the creditor, 'I settled with you concerning the thousand for five hundred' and did not add any condition, then both the guarantor and the original debtor become free from five hundred. Because the guarantor attributed the settlement to the debt of a thousand, and the debt of a thousand is upon the original debtor, not upon the guarantor; upon the guarantor is only the claim (mutalaba), nothing else. So when the debt of a thousand is upon the original debtor, as a result of the settlement, five hundred dirhams are dropped from the liability of the original debtor, and the original debtor becomes free. And it has passed before that when the original debtor becomes free, the guarantor becomes free. And when the original debtor's becoming free causes the guarantor to become free.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of the book on kafalah, followed by a tashrih (commentary) that parses the ruling into four scenarios. The core ruling: if a guarantor settles the debt of one thousand for five hundred, both the guarantor and the original debtor are discharged from the five hundred, and the guarantor can recover that amount from the debtor if the guarantee was at the debtor's request. However, if the settlement is with a different type of item (different genus), it is considered a virtual exchange, so the guarantor becomes owner of the entire debt and can recover the full thousand from the debtor. If the settlement is about the claim that arose from the guarantee itself (i.e., the creditor discharges the guarantor from the claim), then only the guarantor is freed; the debtor remains liable. The tashrih then breaks down the settlement into four possible stipulations: (1) stipulating freeing both, (2) stipulating freeing the debtor only, (3) stipulating freeing the guarantor only, (4) no stipulation. The ruling is explained for each case. In the first two, both are freed for the settled amount. In the third, only the guarantor is freed; the debtor remains liable for the full debt. In the fourth (without stipulation), both are freed because the settlement is attributed to the debt itself, which is on the debtor, so the debtor's discharge automatically discharges the guarantor.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A settlement or compromise between the guarantor and creditor concerning the debt, often for a lesser amount.
مبادلة حكمية (mubadala hukmiyya): A virtual exchange where the guarantor becomes owner of the debt in exchange for the settlement item, allowing full recourse.
إسقاط (isqat): A waiver or dropping of a right, here applied to the settlement that reduces the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the guarantor settles the debt of 1000 dirhams for 500 dirhams of a different type (jins) without any stipulation, what is the result?
A) Both guarantor and debtor are freed from 500, and guarantor recovers 500 from debtor.
B) The guarantor becomes owner of the 1000 and can recover the full amount from the debtor (if authorized).
C) Only the guarantor is freed; debtor owes full 1000.
D) The settlement is invalid because it is usury.

Key Takeaway
The effect of a guarantor's settlement on the debtor depends critically on whether the settlement is attributed to the debt itself (same genus) or is an exchange (different genus), and on any express stipulations.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
10 min
Guarantor's Compromise on Debt: Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on guarantor's compromise for reduced amount and its effect on both parties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between compromise on the same genus (isqat) and a different genus (mubadala hukmiyya), and evaluate the opposing view of the three imams.

Core Idea
When a guarantor compromises with a different genus, Hanafis treat it as a virtual exchange, entitling full recovery of the debt amount.

In suretyship, a guarantor may settle a debt with the creditor for a reduced amount or for a different item. The Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction: a compromise on the same currency is a dropping (isqat) of part of the debt, while a compromise on a different genus is a virtual exchange (mubadala hukmiyya). This distinction has major consequences for the guarantor's right to recover from the principal debtor. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling, its underlying logic, and the contrary view of Imam Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on compromise with same genus
When the guarantor compromises a 1000-dirham debt for 500 dirhams (same currency), the compromise is an isqat: 500 is dropped. Both guarantor and principal are discharged from that 500. The remaining 500 can be claimed from either.
The discharge of the principal automatically discharges the guarantor (bara'ah).
2
Analyze the nature of compromise with different genus
If the guarantor compromises for a different genus (e.g., cloth), the Hanafi school treats it as a virtual exchange (mubadala hukmiyya): the guarantor becomes owner of the full debt amount (1000) and can recover the entire 1000 from the principal (if authorized).
This is because the guarantor's liability is not a debt but a claim; the exchange gives full ownership.
3
Identify the opposing school positions
Imam Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad hold that the compromise is a sale; the guarantor cannot profit, so he recovers only the lesser of the debt and the value of the item given.
Their view is based on the principle that the guarantor should not gain from the transaction.
4
Follow the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the compromise is not a pure sale but includes an element of isqat; thus, ownership transfers fully, making the full debt recoverable.
The virtual exchange (mubadala hukmiyya) is a Hanafi legal construct that preserves the original debt amount.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Hanafi law, the guarantor gets full recovery regardless of the item's value; under the majority view, recovery is capped at the lower of debt and item value.
This difference can significantly affect the guarantor's financial outcome.

Book of Suretyship. 12. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Volume 9. If the guarantor makes a compromise with the creditor regarding a thousand for five hundred, then the guarantor and the one upon whom the debt is originally owed are both discharged. For he attributed the compromise to the thousand, which is a debt upon the principal, so the principal is discharged from five hundred because it is a dropping (isqat), and his discharge necessitates the discharge of the guarantor. Then both are discharged from five hundred by the payment of the guarantor, and the guarantor recovers five hundred from the principal if the suretyship was with his permission, unlike the case if he compromised for a different genus, because it is a virtual exchange, so he becomes owner and recovers the entire thousand. If he compromised regarding what became due through the suretyship, the principal is not discharged, because this is an acquittance of the guarantor from the claim. Translation: So if the guarantor made a compromise with the creditor regarding a thousand for five hundred, then the guarantor and the person upon whom the original debt is due are both discharged. Because the guarantor attributed the compromise to the thousand, which is a debt upon the principal, so the principal is discharged from five hundred because the compromise is a dropping, and the discharge of the principal necessitates the discharge of the guarantor. Then after the guarantor pays, both are discharged from five hundred, and the guarantor recovers five hundred dirhams from the principal provided the suretyship was with his permission, contrary to the case when he compromised for a different genus, because it is a virtual exchange, so the guarantor becomes owner of the thousand and recovers the entire thousand dirhams. And if the guarantor made a compromise with the creditor regarding the right that became due upon him because of the suretyship, the principal is not discharged, because this is an acquittance of the guarantor from the claim. Explanation: There are four scenarios for this issue: (1) The guarantor made a compromise with the creditor for five hundred dirhams regarding a thousand dirhams and stipulated the discharge of both the principal debtor and the guarantor. (2) Or he stipulated specifically the discharge of the principal debtor. (3) Or he stipulated specifically the discharge of the guarantor. (4) Or he did not stipulate any condition. In the first and second scenarios, both the principal debtor and the guarantor are discharged from five hundred dirhams, and the creditor may demand the remaining five hundred from either the guarantor or the principal debtor. In the third scenario, only the guarantor is discharged from five hundred dirhams, and the principal debtor remains liable for the full thousand dirhams; the creditor has the option to claim the full thousand from the principal debtor or to claim five hundred from the guarantor and five hundred from the principal debtor. In the fourth scenario (which is the ruling of the book), i.e., if the guarantor said to the creditor, 'I have made a compromise with you for five hundred dirhams regarding a thousand dirhams' and did not add any condition, then both the guarantor and the principal debtor are discharged from five hundred dirhams. Because the guarantor attributed the compromise to the debt of a thousand, and the debt of a thousand is upon the principal debtor, not upon the guarantor, for the guarantor only has the claim, nothing else. So when the debt of a thousand is upon the principal debtor, as a result of the compromise, five hundred dirhams are dropped from the principal debtor's liability, and the principal debtor is discharged. It has been previously mentioned that the discharge of the principal debtor brings about the discharge of the guarantor. So both are discharged from five hundred dirhams. As for the remaining five hundred, when the guarantor pays them, then both are discharged from that five hundred as well. However, if the suretyship was with the permission of the principal debtor, the guarantor has the option to recover the five hundred dirhams from the principal debtor. If the suretyship was without his permission, then he has no right of recourse. If the guarantor made a compromise with the creditor for a different genus besides the debt, for example, the guarantor compromised for a piece of cloth regarding a thousand dirhams and gave the piece of cloth, then the guarantor becomes the owner of a thousand dirhams. And when he becomes the owner of a thousand dirhams, he recovers a thousand dirhams from the principal debtor provided the suretyship was with his permission. According to the three imams, Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad, the guarantor recovers whichever is less between the debt and the value of the cloth. For example, if the value of the cloth is eight hundred rupees and the debt is a thousand rupees, then the guarantor recovers eight hundred rupees from the principal debtor. If the debt is a thousand rupees and the value of the cloth is twelve hundred rupees, then the guarantor has the option to recover a thousand rupees.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling on a guarantor making a compromise with the creditor for a reduced amount or for a different genus. The text begins by stating the ruling from the matn: if the guarantor compromises for a reduced amount (e.g., 500 of a 1000 debt), both the guarantor and the principal debtor are discharged from the reduced amount. The reasoning is that the compromise is an isqat (dropping) of the debt, and since the debt is originally on the principal, his discharge automatically discharges the guarantor. However, if the compromise is for a different genus (e.g., cloth), the Hanafi position is that it is a virtual exchange (mubadala hukmiyya), so the guarantor becomes owner of the full debt amount and can recover the entire 1000 from the principal (if authorized). The three other imams hold that the guarantor recovers only the lesser of the debt and the value of the cloth. The Urdu commentary then elaborates on four scenarios concerning the compromise on the same genus, explaining the effects based on conditions stipulated. The text provides a detailed analysis of each scenario, demonstrating the Hanafi juristic method of analyzing cases based on the nature of the transaction and the intention of the parties.

Key Terms
كفيل (kafeel): The guarantor or surety who undertakes liability for the debt of another.
مكفول عنه (mukful 'anhu): The principal debtor (the person on whom the original debt is owed).
مكفول له (mukful lahu): The creditor (the one to whom the debt is owed).
صلح (sulh): A compromise or settlement where one party accepts a reduced amount or different item to extinguish a claim.
إسقاط (isqat): Dropping or waiving a right; in this context, dropping part of the debt.
براءة (bara'ah): Discharge from liability; being free from a debt or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a guarantor compromises a 1000 dirham debt for 500 dirhams without any condition, what is the effect on the principal debtor?
A) The principal debtor is fully discharged from the entire 1000 dirhams.
B) The principal debtor remains liable for the full 1000 dirhams.
C) The principal debtor is discharged from 500 dirhams, and the remaining 500 may be claimed from either party.
D) The principal debtor is not affected until the guarantor actually pays.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats a guarantor's compromise as either isqat (same genus) or mubadala hukmiyya (different genus), with different consequences for the principal debtor's liability and the guarantor's right of recourse.

Kafalah — Surety

Guarantor's Compromise on Right of Demand
Ruling on compromise between guarantor and creditor regarding the right of demand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a guarantor's compromise regarding the right of demand and apply it to determine the liabilities of the creditor, guarantor, and principal debtor.

Core Idea
Releasing the guarantor from the claim rescinds the suretyship, not the debt.

A guarantor may negotiate with the creditor to be released from the suretyship, sometimes by paying a sum or even for free. This lesson clarifies that such a compromise does not affect the principal debtor's obligation. Instead, it is treated as a rescission (faskh) of the suretyship contract itself. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly allocating rights and liabilities in suretyship arrangements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Classification
What exactly is the act being ruled upon? It is the compromise (sulh) between the guarantor (kafil) and the creditor (makful lahu) regarding the creditor's right to demand payment from the guarantor. This is not a payment on behalf of the principal debtor but a separate transaction.
The compromise is on the right of claim (mutalaba), not the original debt (dayn).
2
Determine the Legal Effect on the Guarantor
The compromise results in the rescission (faskh) of the suretyship contract. Therefore, the creditor's right to demand from the guarantor is dropped, and the guarantor is released from his obligation as surety.
Faskh ends the contract, as opposed to isqat (dropping a right) which would eliminate the underlying right.
3
Determine the Legal Effect on the Principal Debtor
Since the compromise is on the guarantor's obligation only, the principal debtor's liability remains unchanged. The debt (dayn) and the creditor's right to demand payment from the principal debtor continue in full force.
The principal debtor is not benefited by the guarantor's separate compromise.
4
Analyze the Recovery Rights of the Guarantor
If the guarantor paid something for the compromise (e.g., 100 dirhams), he can recover that amount from the principal debtor only if the suretyship was with the principal's permission (bi-amrih). If the compromise was for free, the guarantor cannot recover anything.
The guarantor's recovery depends on authorization; without it, he bears the cost.
5
Apply the Ruling to the Numerical Example
If the debt is 1000 dirhams and the guarantor pays 100 dirhams to be released, the principal debtor still owes 1000 dirhams, but the creditor can only claim 900 dirhams from the principal (since he already received 100 from the guarantor? Actually, the creditor keeps the 100 as compensation for releasing the guarantor, so the principal still owes the full 1000? The passage says: the creditor will claim 900 from the principal, implying the 100 reduces the debt? Wait: It says 'the creditor will claim nine hundred dirhams from the principal debtor.' This suggests that the creditor's total recovery is capped at the original debt, so if he received 100 from the guarantor, he can only claim 900 from the principal. That is a nuanced point: the payment by the guarantor is treated as reducing the creditor's overall claim? But the text says the principal debtor remains liable for the full debt (1000), yet the creditor claims 900? Let's reconcile: The passage states: 'the original debt and the claim against the principal debtor are not dropped.' But then says: 'the creditor will claim nine hundred dirhams from the principal debtor' because the guarantor's payment is not on account of the debt but for his own release. So the debt remains 1000, but the creditor has already received 100 from the guarantor, so his net claim is reduced to 900? That seems contradictory to 'not dropped'. Actually, the passage means the principal debtor still owes 1000 dirhams, but the creditor's ability to collect from the principal is reduced because he already collected 100 from the guarantor. The principal debtor's obligation to pay 1000 remains, but the creditor's demand is now 900 because he must account for the 100 received. This is a subtle point: the debt is not extinguished, but the creditor's claim is reduced by the amount he already received. The passage says: 'the creditor will claim nine hundred dirhams from the principal debtor.' So the principal debtor pays 900, and the total payment to the creditor is 1000 (100 from guarantor + 900 from principal). The principal's debt of 1000 is satisfied by paying 900 directly and the 100 the creditor already took from the guarantor. So the principal benefits indirectly because the guarantor's payment reduces the creditor's claim. But the text says the principal is not discharged; it means the principal remains obligated to pay the remaining balance. The key is that the principal's liability is not reduced by the compromise itself, but the creditor's collection is reduced by the amount he already received. This needs careful explanation in the commentary.
Important nuance: The principal's debt is not reduced, but the creditor's demand is reduced by the amount received from the guarantor. The principal must pay the balance.

اور اگر کفیل نے مکفول لہ سے اس حق کے بارے میں صلح کی جو حق کفالہ کی وجہ سے مکفول لہ کا کفیل پر واجب ہوا تھا مثلاً کفیل نے مکفول لہ کو ایک سو درہم دے کر درخواست کی کہ مجھے کفالت سے بری کر دے یا مفت درخواست کی تو اس سے مکفول عنہ بری نہ ہوگا بلکہ مکفول عنہ کے ذمہ قرضہ اور مطالبہ بدستور باقی رہیں گے کیونکہ کفیل کو مطالبہ سے بری کرنا فسخ کفالہ ہے نہ کہ اصل دین کو ساقط کرنا پس جب یہ فسخ کفالہ ہے اور اصل دین کو ساقط کرنا نہیں ہے تو کفالہ کی وجہ سے کفیل پر جو مطالبہ واجب ہوا تھا وہ ساقط ہو جائے گا مگر مکفول عنہ سے اصل دین اور اس کا مطالبہ ساقط نہ ہو گا ہاں! اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ اگر کفیل نے ایک سو درہم پر صلح کی ہے تو وہ ایک سو درہم مکفول عنہ سے واپس لے گا بشرطیکہ کفالہ بامرہ ہو اور مکفول لہ مکفول عنہ سے نو سو دراہم کا مطالبہ کرے گا۔ اور اگر کفیل نے مفت صلح کی ہے تو اس صورت میں کفیل مکفول عنہ سے کچھ رجوع نہ کرے گا اور مکفول لہ کو مکفول عنہ سے پورے ایک ہزار دراہم لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔
And if the guarantor made a compromise with the creditor regarding the right that became due upon the guarantor because of the suretyship—for example, the guarantor gave the creditor one hundred dirhams and requested that he release him from the suretyship, or he requested it for free—then the principal debtor is not discharged from this. Rather, the debt and the claim against the principal debtor remain as they were, because releasing the guarantor from the claim is a rescission of the suretyship (faskh al-kafala), not a dropping of the original debt. So when this is a rescission of the suretyship and not a dropping of the original debt, then the claim that was due upon the guarantor due to the suretyship is dropped, but the original debt and the claim against the principal debtor are not dropped. However, it is essential that if the guarantor compromised for one hundred dirhams, he recovers that one hundred dirhams from the principal debtor provided the suretyship was with his permission, and the creditor will claim nine hundred dirhams from the principal debtor. If the guarantor compromised for free, then in that case the guarantor does not recover anything from the principal debtor, and the creditor has the right to take the full one thousand dirhams from the principal debtor.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on a specific scenario: when the guarantor makes a compromise with the creditor regarding the right of demand that the creditor has against the guarantor due to the suretyship itself (i.e., the creditor's right to claim from the guarantor). This is different from compromising on the original debt. The text explains that such a compromise is a rescission (faskh) of the suretyship contract, not a discharge of the principal debtor's liability. Therefore, the principal debtor remains liable for the full debt. However, if the guarantor paid something for the compromise, he can recover that amount from the principal debtor (if authorized). If the compromise was for free, the guarantor cannot recover anything. The key distinction is between the debt itself and the right to claim from the guarantor. The Hanafi school treats the suretyship as a separate obligation of demand, and its removal does not affect the original debt.

Key Terms
فسخ الكفالة (faskh al-kafala): Rescission or termination of the suretyship contract, which releases the guarantor from the claim but does not affect the principal debt.
مطالبة (mutalaba): The right of the creditor to demand payment from the guarantor; this right is separate from the actual debt.
حق (haqq): In this context, the right of claim that the creditor has against the guarantor due to the suretyship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a guarantor pays the creditor 100 dirhams to be released from the suretyship (without the principal's knowledge), what happens to the principal debtor's liability?
A) The principal debtor is discharged from 100 dirhams.
B) The principal debtor remains liable for the full debt, and the guarantor recovers 100 dirhams from him if authorized.
C) The principal debtor remains liable for the full debt, and the guarantor recovers nothing (if compromise was for free) or recovers the amount paid if authorized.
D) The principal debtor is fully discharged because the suretyship is terminated.

Key Takeaway
A guarantor's compromise with the creditor on the right of demand rescinds the suretyship but does not affect the principal debtor's obligation; any payment by the guarantor reduces the creditor's claim against the principal but does not extinguish the debt.

Creditor's Statement of Release: Implication for Guarantor's Recourse
Ruling on the legal implication of a creditor's statement of release to a guarantor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the creditor's statement of release to the guarantor and explain the logical inference (qiyas) behind treating it as an admission of payment.

Core Idea
A creditor's statement of release to a guarantor implies payment, granting the guarantor recourse against the principal debtor.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a creditor directly tells a guarantor that the guarantor has been released from the debt, this statement has legal consequences beyond mere discharge. The creditor's admission is interpreted as acknowledgment that payment occurred, because a gratuitous discharge from the creditor to the guarantor (who is not the direct debtor) is not the norm. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this ruling and its practical effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The creditor tells the guarantor, who guaranteed at the principal debtor's request, 'You have obtained release from me regarding the wealth.' The ruling: the guarantor has the right to recover that amount from the principal debtor.
The guarantor's right of recourse depends on this statement.
2
Analyze the key term: bara'at (release)
Bara'at can occur through payment or through gratuitous discharge (ibra'). In this context, the release is from the creditor to the guarantor, not to the principal debtor.
The passage emphasizes the direction: 'starts from the debtor and ends with the claimant'.
3
Understand the logical inference (qiyas)
A release that originates from the one who is sought (the creditor) and ends with the one seeking (the guarantor) cannot be without payment. Therefore, the statement must be based on actual payment by the guarantor.
This is the core of the dalil aqli: the release implies payment because a gratuitous discharge from creditor to guarantor is unlikely.
4
Recognize the legal effect: admission (iqrar) of payment
The creditor's statement is treated as an admission that the guarantor paid. This admission is binding, giving the guarantor the right to recover from the principal debtor.
No further proof of payment is required from the guarantor.
5
Note the significance and limits
This ruling applies only when the guarantor guaranteed at the order of the principal debtor. If the guarantee was voluntary, the recourse may differ. Also, if the creditor explicitly denies payment, the statement might be interpreted differently.
The passage focuses on the specific scenario of guarantee by order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مکفول لہ نے اس کفیل سے جو مکفول عنہ کے حکم سے مکفول لہ کے لیے کفیل ہوا تھا اس سے کہا کہ تو نے میری جانب سے برأت کر لی تو کفیل کو مکفول لہ سے مال لینے کا اختیار ہے جس کا وہ ضامن ہوا تھا
قال ومن قال لكفيل ضمن له مالا قد برئت إلى من المال رجع الكفيل على المكفول عنه معناه بما ضمن له بامره لأن البراة التي ابتداؤها من المطلوب وانتهاؤها إلى الطالب لا يكون إلا بالأيفاء فيكون هذا إقراراً بالأداء فيرجع
ترجمہ اور جس مکفول لہ نے کفیل سے جو مکفول لہ کے واسطے مال کا ضامن ہوا تھا یہ کہا کہ تو نے مال سے میری جانب برات کر لی تو کفیل مکفول عنہ سے مال واپس لے گا۔ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ جس مال کا اس کے حکم سے مکفول لہ کے واسطے ضامن ہوا تھا اس لئے کہ وہ برات جس کی ابتداء مکفول عنہ سے ہو اور اس کی انتہا مکفول لہ تک ہو تو وہ بغیر ادا کئے نہیں ہوگا۔ پس یہ ادا کرنے کا اقرار ہے تو کفیل اس کو مکفول عنہ سے واپس لے گا۔ تشریح ۔ اس جگہ فاضل مصنف نے مسلسل ایسے تین مسائل ذکر فرمائے ہیں جن کا تعلق ابراء (بری کرنے) کے ساتھ ہے پہلا مسئلہ یہ
The creditor said to the guarantor, who had become a guarantor for the creditor by the order of the principal debtor, 'You have obtained release from me regarding the wealth.' So the guarantor has the right to take the wealth from the principal debtor, i.e., the wealth for which he was a guarantor with his permission. Because the release (bara'at) that starts from the debtor (the one sought) and ends with the claimant cannot be except by payment, so this is an admission of payment, and he (the guarantor) may have recourse. Translation: And the creditor who said to the guarantor, who became a guarantor for the wealth for the creditor, 'You have obtained release from me regarding the wealth,' then the guarantor will take back the wealth from the principal debtor. The meaning is that it is the wealth for which he became a guarantor for the creditor with his order, because the bara'at that originates from the principal debtor and ends at the creditor cannot be without payment. So this is an admission of payment, and the guarantor will recover it from the principal debtor. Explanation: At this point, the author has mentioned three consecutive issues related to ibra' (discharge); the first issue is...
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling where the creditor tells the guarantor that he (the guarantor) has obtained release (bara'at) from the creditor concerning the debt. The text explains that this statement implies that the guarantor has actually paid the debt, because a release that originates from the debtor (meaning the statement is about the release from the creditor to the guarantor) must be based on payment. Therefore, this statement is treated as an admission by the creditor that the guarantor has paid. Consequently, the guarantor can have recourse against the principal debtor for the amount he guaranteed. The reasoning is that a discharge (bara'at) without payment is not valid in this context, so the creditor's statement is equivalent to acknowledging receipt of payment. The Urdu tashreeh notes that the author covers three consecutive issues related to ibra' (discharge), and this is the first one. The text provides a clear example of how Hanafi jurists use logical inference (dalil aqli) from the nature of transactions.

Key Terms
برأت (bara'at): Discharge or release from liability; in this context, the creditor's statement that the guarantor has been released from the debt.
إقرار (iqrar): Admission or acknowledgment; the creditor's statement is treated as an admission that payment was made.
أداء (ada'): Payment or fulfillment of the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The principal debtor is discharged from the debt.
C) The statement is treated as an admission that the guarantor paid, so he can recover from the principal debtor.
D) The guarantor must prove that he actually paid.

Key Takeaway
A creditor's statement of release to a guarantor implies payment, enabling the guarantor to seek recourse from the principal debtor.

Three Scenarios of Discharge in Kafalah and the Internal Hanafi Dispute
Three scenarios of discharge in kafalah and their effect on recourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three scenarios of discharge in kafalah and state the ruling on the surety's right of recourse for each, including the internal debate between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The wording of discharge determines recourse: 'paid' → recovery; 'waived' → no recovery; ambiguous → dispute.

In suretyship (kafalah), when the creditor discharges the surety, the question arises: can the surety recover the paid amount from the principal debtor? The answer depends on how the creditor worded the discharge. This lesson unpacks three classic scenarios from the Hanafi school, highlighting an internal dispute between the two leading students of Abu Hanifa: Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Scenarios
Listen to each wording the creditor uses: (1) 'you have been discharged from me in terms of the property' (implying payment), (2) 'I have discharged you' (pure waiver), (3) 'you are discharged' (ambiguous).
The translation aims to capture the nuance.
2
Determine the Legal Effect
For each scenario, decide whether the surety can recover from the debtor. Scenario 1: yes (acknowledgment of payment). Scenario 2: no (waiver).
The third scenario is disputed.
3
Analyze the Rationale
Understand the difference: 'payment acknowledgment' vs. 'pure waiver'. The creditor's words signal whether the debt was paid by the surety or simply forgiven.
The principle: 'al-ibra' min al-mal' is an acknowledgment; 'al-ibra' mujarrad' is a waiver.
4
Examine the Internal Hanafi Dispute
Focus on the third scenario ('bari'ta'). Imam Muhammad treats it as a waiver (no recourse). Imam Abu Yusuf treats it as an acknowledgment (recourse allowed). Understand each reasoning.
Imam Muhammad: take the lower probability (waiver). Imam Abu Yusuf: the phrase implies the discharge came from the surety.
5
Apply the Principle of Tarjih
Later Hanafi preference often sides with Imam Muhammad due to the maxim 'avoid recourse with doubt'. Note that the mufta bihi is not explicitly given here.
This shows the dynamism of the school.

Source Text

كتاب الكفاله

... [full clean text as per OCR, see below]
The Book of Kafalah: ... [full translation]
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses three scenarios in Kafalah where the creditor (makful lahu) discharges the surety (kafil). The key question is whether the surety can then recover from the principal debtor (makful 'anhu). The first scenario: the creditor says 'I have been discharged from you in terms of the property' (meaning the surety paid). Here the discharge is considered an acknowledgment of payment, so the surety recovers from the debtor. The second scenario: the creditor says 'I have discharged you' (without mentioning payment). This is a pure waiver, not an acknowledgment of payment, so the surety cannot recover. The third scenario: the creditor says 'You are discharged' (bare statement). Imam Muhammad equates it to the second scenario because it is ambiguous – it could be due to payment or waiver – and the lower probability (waiver) is taken, so the surety cannot recover. Imam Abu Yusuf equates it to the first scenario because the phrase implies the discharge originated from the surety (by payment). The text also notes that if the creditor is present, his explanation is sought as he is the one who made the ambiguous statement.

Key Terms
كفالة (kafalah): Suretyship: a contract where one person (kafil) guarantees the debt or presence of another (makful 'anhu) to a third party (makful lahu).
براءة (bara'ah): Discharge or release from a debt or obligation. Can be by payment or by waiver.
مكفول عنه (makful 'anhu): The principal debtor on whose behalf the surety guarantees.
مكفول له (makful lahu): The creditor to whom the guarantee is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The surety can recover because the debt is eliminated.
B) The surety cannot recover because it is a pure waiver.
C) The surety can recover only if the debtor consents.
D) The matter is disputed between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Key Takeaway
The surety's right of recourse depends on whether the creditor's discharge wording acknowledges payment or merely waives the debt; ambiguous wording leads to an internal Hanafi dispute.

The Meaning of 'Barat' in Kafalah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ambiguous discharge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the effect of the creditor's ambiguous statement 'barat' and identify the practical difference in recourse, as well as the rule when the creditor is present.

Core Idea
When a creditor says 'barat' (you are free), the school splits: Imam Muhammad sees release (no recourse), Imam Abu Yusuf sees payment (recourse allowed).

In suretyship (kafalah), the guarantor's liability may end either by paying the debt or by the creditor's release. But what if the creditor simply says 'barat' – a single ambiguous word? This passage from Al-Hidayah records an internal Hanafi disagreement between the two great students of Abu Hanifa: Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf. Their reasoning reveals the school's method for parsing ambiguous statements and the role of the creditor's own explanation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ambiguity
The creditor says 'barat' (you are free) without specifying whether it is because the guarantor paid (barā'ah bil-adā') or because the creditor released him (barā'ah bil-ibrā').
The word 'barat' is the third case among three cases discussed in the book of kafalah.
2
State the two positions
Imam Muhammad holds it is like release: guarantor freed, no recourse. Imam Abu Yusuf holds it is like payment: guarantor freed but with recourse to the principal debtor.
3
Follow each imam's dalil
Muhammad: two probabilities exist; the lower (release) is taken when in doubt, as in prayer rak'ah doubts. Abu Yusuf: the address 'ta' (you) attributes the freedom to the guarantor's act, which is payment, not the creditor's release.
Muhammad applies the principle of taking the lesser probability; Abu Yusuf uses linguistic implication of the verb form.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is whether the guarantor can claim reimbursement from the principal debtor after being discharged. Under Muhammad's view, no; under Abu Yusuf's, yes.
5
Apply the mashayikh's conditioning
If the creditor is present after uttering 'barat', his own explanation is sought and accepted. The dispute only applies when the creditor is absent.
This is a later addition by some mashayikh as reported in Al-Hidayah.

Source Text

اشرف البدایہ جلد-نم

كتاب الكفاله
مکفول لہ نے بری کر دیا اس میں ادائیگی کے بعد اور بغیر ادا ئیگی کے بری کرنا دونوں میں سے ادنی احتمال مراد ہو گا
ولو قال برنت قال محمد هو مثل الثانى لأنه يحتمل البرأة بالأداء اليه و إلا براء فيثبت الادنى اذ لا يرجع الكفيل بالشك وقال ابو يوسف هو مثل الأول لأنه أقر ببرأة إبتداؤها من المطلوب و أليه الإيفاء دون الابراء وقيل في جميع ما ذكرنا إذا كان الطالب حاضراً يرجع في البيان إليه لأنه هو المجمل
ترجمہ اور اگر مکفول لانے کہا کہ تو بری ہو گیا امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ یہ دوسرے مسئلہ کے مانند ہے اس لئے کہ اس کا بھی احتمال ہے کہ یہ براءت مكفول لہ کو ادا کرنے سے ہو اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ مکفول لڈ کے بری کرنے سے ہو۔ پس کم درجہ کی براءت ثابت ہو جائیگی کیونکہ شک کے ساتھ کفیل واپس نہیں لے سکتا ہے اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ یہ مسئلہ اول کے مانند ہے کیونکہ اس نے ایسی برائت کا اقرار کیا ہے جس کی ابتدا کفیل سے ہے اور کفیل کی جانب میں صرف ادا ہے نہ کہ بری کرنا اور کہا گیا کہ مذکورہ تمام صورتوں میں اگر مانول ایا موجود ہو تو ائل کے بیان کی جانب رجوع کیا جائے گا کیونکہ مجمل کرنے والا وہی ہے۔ تشریح مسائل ثلاثہ میں سے تیسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مکفول لانے کفیل سے کہا بسنت تو بری ہو گیا اور لفظ الی نہیں کہا تو اس میں اختلاف تے چنا نچہ امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ اس کا حکم مسئلہ ثانیہ یعنی ابر اتک کے مانند ہے یعنی جس طرح ابراتک کہنے کی صورت میں نفیل بری جاتا ہے اور اس کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح بونت کہنے کی صورت میں کفیل بری ہو جائے گا اور اس کو ما شوال عنہ سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ برات میں دو احتمال میں ایک یہ کہ مکفول لانے کفیل سے کہا کہ تو بری ہو گیا کیونکہ تو مال ادا کر چکا ہے۔ دوسرا احتمال یہ کہ تو بری ہو گیا کیونکہ میں تجھ کو بری کر چکا ہوں حاصل یہ کہ ایک احتمال برات بالا داء کا ہے اور ایک احتمال برات بالابر کا ہے پس ان دونوں میں سے برات بالا براء چونکہ اونی ہے اس لئے برات بالا براء ثابت ہو جائے گی کیونکہ جب ادنی اور اعلیٰ یا کم اور زائد کا احتمال ہو تو ادنی اور کم ثابت ہوتا ہے اعلیٰ اور زائد ثابت نہیں ہوتا جیسے اگر نمازی کو دوران نماز تعداد رکعات میں شبہ ہو جائے مثلاً یہ شبہ ہوا کہ دور کعتیں ہوئیں یا تین رکعات ہو ئیں تو حکم یہ ہے کہ وہ دو رکعت شمار کرے پس اسی طرح یہاں کم درجہ کی نداخت حاصل ہوگی یعنی یہ کہا جائے گا کہ کفیل ، مکفول لڈ کے بری کرنے سے بری ہوا ہے اور کفیل جب مکفول لا کے بری کرنے سے بری ہوا ہے تو اس کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کا اختیار نہیں ہوتا ۔ لہذا الفظ برنست کہنے کی صورت میں بھی کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس بات کا تو یقین ہے کہ انتظا ہر کت سے کفیل بری ہو گیا ہے خواہ مکھول لنڈ کے بری کرنے سے بری ہو ۔ خواہ مکسول لہ کو مال مکشول بہ ادا کرنے سے بری ہو لیکن مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کرنے میں شک ہے کیونکہ اگر ہرات بالا دا ء ہے تب نو کفیل کو رجوع کا اختیار ہے اور اگر برائت بالا براء ہے تو رجوع کا اختیار نہیں ہے پس جب کفیل کے رجوع کرنے میں شک ہو گیا تو شک کی وجہ ے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔

كتاب الكفاله
۱۷۴
اشرف البدایہ جلد - نم
حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اس کا حکم مسئلہ اولیٰ یعنی برنت التی کے مانند ہے یعنی جس طرح ہو نت الی کہنے کی صورت میں کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار ہوتا ہے اسی طرح صرف لفظ برات کہنے کی صورت میں بھی کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار حاصل ہوگا۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مکفول لڑ نے برکت کہ کر ایسی برات کا اقرار کیا ہے جس کی ابتدا کفیل سے ہے کیونکہ اس نے حرف خطاب یعنی تا ذکر کیا ہے پس برائت ایسے فعل سے ہوگی جو خاص طور پر کفیل کی طرف منسوب ہے اور کفیل کی طرف سے ادا کرنا ہوتا ہے نہ کہ بری کرنا یعنی ادا کرنا تو کفیل کے فعل سے ہوتا ہے لیکن بری کرنا اس کے فعل سے موجود نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جب یہ براءت کفیل کی طرف سے ہے اور کفیل کی طرف سے جو براءت حاصل ہوتی ہے وہ چونکہ ادا کرنے سے حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے یہ برأت بھی کفیل کے ادا کرنے سے حاصل ہوگی اور جو برکت کفیل کے ادا کرنے سے حاصل ہوتی ہو۔ اس میں چونکہ کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کا اختیار ہوتا ہے اس لئے لفظ ہر نت کہنے کی صورت میں بھی کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کا پورا پورا اختیار ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ مسائل ثلاثہ میں مذکورہ احکام اس وقت ہیں جبکہ مکفول لا مذکورہ الفاظ بول کر غائب ہو گیا ہو لیکن اگر مکفول لا موجود ہو تو تینوں مسئلوں میں اس کے بیان کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا یعنی اس سے دریافت کیا جائے گا کہ اس نے مال مکفول یہ پر قبضہ کیا ہے یا قبضہ نہیں کیا ہے کیونکہ کلام کے اندر مکفول لا ہی نے اجمال پیدا کیا ہے اور یہ قاعدہ ہے کہ کلام مجمل کی تفسیر اور بیان خود مجمل (اجمال کرنے والے) سے دریافت کی جاتی ہے پس مذکورہ مسائل میں بھی چونکہ ایک گونہ اجمل ہے اس لئے ان تینوں مسائل میں بھی مجمل یعنی مکفول لہ کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا بشرطیکہ مکفول لہ موجود ہو۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 9. Book of Kafalah. The creditor freed him; in this, whether after payment or without payment, the lesser probability is intended. And if he said 'barat' (you are free), Muhammad said: it is like the second case because it can be interpreted as being free from debt by payment [to him] or by release, so the lesser is established because the guarantor cannot recourse with doubt. Abu Yusuf said: it is like the first because he confessed a freedom whose origin is from the principal debtor, and to him is the payment, not the release. And it is said in all that we have mentioned: if the claimant is present, reference is made to his explanation because he is the one who made it ambiguous. Translation: And if the creditor said 'you are free', Imam Muhammad ruled that this is like the second case, because there is a probability that this freedom is from the creditor paying the debt and also that it is from the creditor releasing him. So the lesser degree of freedom is established because the guarantor cannot take back with doubt. And Abu Yusuf ruled that this is like the first case, because he admitted a freedom whose beginning is from the guarantor, and from the guarantor's side is only payment, not release. And it is said that in all the mentioned cases, if the claimant is present, reference is made to his explanation because he is the one who made it ambiguous. Explanation: Among the three cases, the third is that the creditor said to the guarantor 'basanta' (you have become free) and did not say the word 'ila' (to), so there is disagreement. Imam Muhammad ruled that its ruling is like the second case, i.e., the case of release; just as in saying 'abratuka' (I release you), the guarantor is freed and does not have recourse to the principal debtor, similarly in saying 'bunata' (you are free), the guarantor will be freed and will not have recourse to the principal debtor. The proof is that in the word 'barat' there are two probabilities: one that the creditor said to the guarantor 'you are free because you have paid the money', and the second that 'you are free because I have released you'. So there is one probability of freedom by payment and one of freedom by release. Between these two, the freedom by release is lower, so freedom by release is established because when there is probability of lower and higher or less and more, the lower and less is established, and the higher and more is not. For example, if a praying person doubts the number of rak'ahs, e.g., whether two rak'ahs or three, the ruling is that he counts two. So similarly here, the lower degree is obtained, i.e., it will be said that the guarantor was freed by the creditor's release, and when the guarantor is freed by the creditor's release, he does not have the option to recourse to the principal debtor. Therefore, in the case of saying 'barat', the guarantor will not have the option to recourse. A second proof is that it is certain that the guarantor has become free from the guarantee, whether he is freed by the creditor's release or by paying the guaranteed money to the creditor. But there is doubt regarding recourse to the principal debtor because if it is freedom by payment, then the guarantor has recourse, and if it is freedom by release, then there is no recourse. When there is doubt about the guarantor's recourse, then because of doubt, there is no option to recourse. On page 175: Kashf al-Hidayah Volume 9. Imam Abu Yusuf ruled that its ruling is like the first case, i.e., the case of 'barat ila' (freedom by payment to you). Just as in saying 'barta ila' (you are free to me), the guarantor has the option to recourse to the principal debtor, similarly in the case of saying only 'barat', the guarantor will have full recourse. His proof is that the creditor, by saying 'barat', admitted a freedom whose origin is from the guarantor because he used the address letter 'ta' (you). So the freedom will be from an act specific to the guarantor, and from the guarantor's side is payment, not release. Payment is from the guarantor's act, but release is not present from his act. So when this freedom is from the guarantor, and the freedom obtained from the guarantor is because of payment, therefore this freedom is also obtained from the guarantor's payment. And whichever freedom is obtained from the guarantor's payment, since the guarantor has recourse to the principal debtor, therefore in the case of saying 'barat', the guarantor will have full recourse. The author of Hidayah said that some mashayikh said that the rulings mentioned in the three cases are when the creditor, after uttering those words, became absent. But if the creditor is present, then in all three cases, reference is made to his explanation, i.e., he will be asked whether he received the guaranteed money or not, because the creditor himself created the ambiguity in the speech, and it is a rule that the interpretation and explanation of an ambiguous speech is sought from the one who made it ambiguous. So in the mentioned cases, since there is some ambiguity, in all three cases, reference is made to the one who made it ambiguous, i.e., the creditor, provided he is present.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the meaning of the creditor's statement 'barat' (you are free) to the guarantor. The dispute arises because the word is ambiguous: it could mean the guarantor is freed because he paid the debt (براءة بالأداء) or because the creditor released him (براءة بالإبراء). Imam Muhammad argues it is like the second case of the three mentioned earlier (the case of pure release, 'abratuka'), so the guarantor is freed and cannot recourse to the principal debtor. His reasoning: the word 'barat' has two probabilities—payment or release. Since the lower (release) is established when there is doubt (following the principle of taking the lesser probability, as in prayer doubts), and the guarantor cannot recourse with certainty, no recourse is allowed. Imam Abu Yusuf argues it is like the first case (the case of 'barat ila'), where the guarantor has recourse. His reasoning: the address 'barat' attributes the freedom to the guarantor's act (payment), not the creditor's release, so it implies payment, and thus recourse is allowed. The passage then adds a crucial note from the author of Al-Hidayah: if the creditor is present, his explanation is sought because he created the ambiguity. This ruling applies to all three cases. The passage thus clarifies how ambiguous language in suretyship is resolved: first by considering probabilities (in absence), and by the speaker's clarification (if present).

Key Terms
كفالة (kafālah): A contract of suretyship where the guarantor (kafil) undertakes to fulfill an obligation for the principal debtor (makful 'anhu) in favor of the creditor (makful lahu).
براءة (barā'ah): Freedom from the guarantee; can occur either by payment of the debt (barā'ah bil-adā') or by release (barā'ah bil-ibrā').
كفيل (kafīl): The guarantor who undertakes to pay the debt if the principal debtor defaults.
مكفول له (makfūl lahu): The creditor in whose favor the guarantee is made.
مكفول عنه (makfūl 'anhu): The principal debtor for whom the guarantee is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, if the creditor says 'barat' (you are free) to the guarantor, what is the ruling regarding the guarantor's right to recourse against the principal debtor?
A) The guarantor has full recourse because the release implies payment.
B) The guarantor has no recourse because the ambiguous statement establishes the lower probability (release).
C) The guarantor must ask the principal debtor for permission.
D) The guarantee becomes void automatically.

Key Takeaway
When a creditor's statement is ambiguous between payment and release, the Hanafi school holds two positions; but if the creditor is present, his own clarification overrides the debate.
