Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
Suspending Release from Kafalah on a Condition
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on suspending release from kafalah on a condition and explain the proof and ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Suspending release from kafalah is invalid because it contains tamlik, which cannot be conditioned.

In Hanafi fiqh, acts that transfer ownership (tamlik) cannot be suspended on future conditions. Release from kafalah involves such a transfer, making conditional release invalid. However, a minority view considers it pure dropping (isqat), thus valid. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is suspending the release of a guarantor (kafil) from liability on a future condition (e.g., 'if Zaid arrives'). The primary ruling is 'la yajuz' (not permissible), meaning it is invalid (batil).
The alternative transmission says it is valid (sahih).
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The primary proof is qiyas (analogy) to other releases and tamlikat. Since release from kafalah contains a meaning of tamlik, it resembles a transfer of ownership, which cannot be suspended.
The text says 'as in other releases' (sair al-bara'at).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The 'illa (effective cause) is the element of tamlik: the guarantor becomes owner of the right to demand (the creditor's claim). Tamlikat are invalid when suspended, so this release is also invalid.
The alternative view denies the tamlik element, calling it pure isqat.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
An alternative transmission (ruwiya) states it is valid because the guarantor is only liable for demand (mutalaba), not the debt, making release pure isqat like divorce.
The text supports this by noting that the guarantor's release is not nullified by rejection, unlike the principal debtor.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the first: not permissible. The text from Quduri is standard, and the alternative transmission is weaker.
Cross-madhhab: Shafi'i generally allows such suspensions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کفالت سے بری کرنے کو شرط کے ساتھ معلق کرنے کا حکم
قال ولا يجوز تعليق البرأة من الكفالة بالشرط لما فيه من معنى التمليك كما في سائر البراات و يروى انه يصح لأن عليه المطالبة دون الدين في الصحيح فكان اسقاطاً محضاً كالطلاق ولهذا لا يرتد الابراء عن الكفيل بالرد بخلاف ابراء الاصيل
ترجمہ اور کفالہ سے بری کرنے کو شرط پر معلق کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں مالک کرنے کے معنی ہیں جیسے دوسری براءتوں میں ہوتے ہیں اور روایت ہے کہ یہ صحیح ہے کیونکہ صحیح قول کے مطابق کفیل پر مطالبہ لازم ہے نہ کہ قرضہ تو یہ محض ساقط کرنا ہوگا جیسے طلاق ہے اور اسی وجہ سے کفیل کو بری کرنا اس کے رد کرنے سے رد نہ ہوگا بر خلاف اصیل کو بری کرنے کے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ کفالہ سے بری ہونے کو کسی شرط پر معلق کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً مکفول لڑ نے کہا اذا جاء غداً فانت برى من الكفالة اگر کل کا دن آ گیا تو تو کفالہ سے بری ہے یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفالہ سے بری ہونا استقاد محض نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں تملیک یعنی مالک کرنے کے معنی ہیں اس طور پر کہ کفالہ کی وجہ سے مکفول لہ کفیل سے مطالبہ کرنے کا مالک تھا لیکن جب کفیل کو بری کر دیا گیا تو گویا کفیل کو مطالبہ کا مالک کر دیا اور تملیکات یعنی مالک کرنے کو شرط پر معلق کرنا ، نا جائز ہے لہذا کفالہ سے بری ہونے کو بھی شرط پر معلق کرنا نا جائز ہوگا۔ جیسا ، وسری براتوں کو شرط پر معلق کرنا نا جائز ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے کہا کہ یہاں ایک اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر فیل بالمال نے مکفول لڑ سے یہ کہا کہ اگر میں کل آ ئندہ
The ruling on suspending release from kafalah on a condition. He said: It is not permissible to suspend the release from kafalah on a condition because it contains the meaning of transfer of ownership (tamlik) as in other releases. And it is transmitted that it is valid because upon the guarantor is the demand (of the creditor) and not the debt, according to the correct view, so it is a pure dropping (isqat) like divorce, and for this reason, the release of the guarantor is not nullified by rejection, unlike the release of the principal debtor. Translation: And suspending the release from kafalah on a condition is not permissible. Because there is the meaning of transferring ownership in it, as in other releases. And it is transmitted that it is valid because the correct view is that upon the guarantor is the demand (of the creditor) and not the debt, so it would be a pure dropping like divorce, and for this reason, the release of the guarantor is not nullified by rejection, unlike the release of the principal debtor. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri states that suspending release from kafalah on a condition is not permissible. For example, the creditor said: 'If tomorrow comes, then you are free from the kafalah' — this is not permissible. The proof is that being free from kafalah is not a pure dropping, but rather it contains the meaning of transfer of ownership, in the sense that because of kafalah, the creditor was the owner of the right to demand from the guarantor, but when the guarantor is released, it is as if the guarantor becomes the owner of the demand. And transferring ownership (tamlikat) is not permissible to suspend on a condition, therefore suspending release from kafalah on a condition is impermissible, just as it is impermissible to suspend other releases on a condition. Allamah Ibn al-Humam said that there is an objection here: that if the guarantor (kafil bil-mal) said to the creditor: 'If I come tomorrow...'
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on suspending the release from kafalah (suretyship) on a future condition (ta'liq). The main ruling, attributed to Sahib al-Quduri (a key Hanafi text), is that it is not permissible. The reason ('illa) is that release from kafalah involves an element of tamlik (transfer of ownership): the guarantor, by being released, gains ownership of the right to demand (i.e., the creditor's right to demand payment is transferred to the guarantor in a sense). Since tamlikat (transfers of ownership) cannot be suspended on conditions (e.g., selling a house contingent on an event is invalid), the release of the guarantor also cannot be suspended. However, a transmission (ruwiya) states it is valid because in the correct view, the guarantor is only liable for the demand (mutalaba) and not the debt itself. Thus, releasing him is a pure dropping (isqat mahd) of a right, similar to divorce (talaq) which is a pure relinquishment and valid when suspended. The passage also notes that unlike the release of a principal debtor (asil), the release of a guarantor is not nullified if the debtor rejects it—further evidence that it is a pure dropping. The commentary then begins to address an objection by Ibn al-Humam, but the text cuts off mid-sentence. The key point: the Hanafi school generally prohibits suspending the release of a guarantor on a condition due to the element of tamlik, though a minority view allows it, considering it pure isqat.

Key Terms
تعليق البرأة (ta'liq al-bara'ah): Suspending the release from a guarantee on the occurrence of a future condition.
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; here, the guarantor becomes owner of the right to demand (the creditor's claim), making the release more than a mere dropping.
إسقاط محض (isqat mahd): Pure dropping; a legal act that simply extinguishes a right without transferring ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the primary Hanafi position (Sahib al-Quduri), why is it not permissible to suspend the release from kafalah on a condition?
A) Because kafalah is a contract of guarantee that cannot be revoked.
B) Because it contains the meaning of transfer of ownership (tamlik), which cannot be suspended.
C) Because the creditor must be present at the time of release.
D) Because the guarantor must pay the debt first.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi primary view prohibits suspending release from kafalah on a condition because it involves tamlik, which cannot be conditional; an alternative view permits it as pure isqat, but the relied-upon position is the prohibition.

Effect of 'Bara'ah' in Kafalah on Kafil's Recourse
Ruling of Abu Yusuf on 'bara'ah' in kafalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Yusuf's position that saying 'bara'ah' in kafalah gives the kafil the right of recourse, and explain the dalil that discharge addressed to the kafil implies payment.

Core Idea
Discharge addressed to the kafil implies payment, entitling him to recourse.

In Hanafi fiqh, the word 'bara'ah' (discharge) in a kafalah contract can have significant implications for the kafil's right to seek reimbursement from the debtor. Imam Abu Yusuf presents a nuanced ruling that links the discharge to the kafil's act of payment, even if payment is not explicitly stated. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and the conditions under which it applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and Imam Abu Yusuf's ruling
The passage addresses whether the creditor saying 'bara'ah' to the kafil alone (without explicit mention of payment) grants the kafil the right of recourse against the debtor. Abu Yusuf rules that it does, equating it to the case of 'bara'ah al-'amma'.
The ruling is an expansion of a prior issue.
2
Analyze the dalil (proof) – the address 'ta'
The proof is that the creditor uses the second person 'ta' (you) in addressing the kafil. This attributes the discharge to an act specifically from the kafil, which is payment (ada'), not mere waiver (ibra').
The linguistic analysis of the address is key.
3
Understand the analogy with payment
Since the discharge is linked to the kafil's act, and the only act that can produce discharge from the kafil's side is payment, the 'bara'ah' must imply that payment occurred.
This is a qiyas (analogy) between two types of discharge.
4
Consider the refinement by Sahib al-Hidayah
The ruling applies when the creditor is absent. If present, his interpretation of his own ambiguous words is sought, and he is asked whether he received the property.
This condition affects the application of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اس کا حکم مسئلہ اولیٰ یعنی برنت التی کے مانند ہے یعنی جس طرح ہو نت الی کہنے کی صورت میں کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار ہوتا ہے اسی طرح صرف لفظ برات کہنے کی صورت میں بھی کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار حاصل ہوگا۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مکفول لڑ نے برکت کہ کر ایسی برات کا اقرار کیا ہے جس کی ابتدا کفیل سے ہے کیونکہ اس نے حرف خطاب یعنی تا ذکر کیا ہے پس برائت ایسے فعل سے ہوگی جو خاص طور پر کفیل کی طرف منسوب ہے اور کفیل کی طرف سے ادا کرنا ہوتا ہے نہ کہ بری کرنا یعنی ادا کرنا تو کفیل کے فعل سے ہوتا ہے لیکن بری کرنا اس کے فعل سے موجود نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جب یہ براءت کفیل کی طرف سے ہے اور کفیل کی طرف سے جو براءت حاصل ہوتی ہے وہ چونکہ ادا کرنے سے حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے یہ برأت بھی کفیل کے ادا کرنے سے حاصل ہوگی اور جو برکت کفیل کے ادا کرنے سے حاصل ہوتی ہو۔ اس میں چونکہ کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کا اختیار ہوتا ہے اس لئے لفظ ہر نت کہنے کی صورت میں بھی کفیل کو مکفول عنہ سے رجوع کا پورا پورا اختیار ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ مسائل ثلاثہ میں مذکورہ احکام اس وقت ہیں جبکہ مکفول لا مذکورہ الفاظ بول کر غائب ہو گیا ہو لیکن اگر مکفول لا موجود ہو تو تینوں مسئلوں میں اس کے بیان کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا یعنی اس سے دریافت کیا جائے گا کہ اس نے مال مکفول یہ پر قبضہ کیا ہے یا قبضہ نہیں کیا ہے کیونکہ کلام کے اندر مکفول لا ہی نے اجمال پیدا کیا ہے اور یہ قاعدہ ہے کہ کلام مجمل کی تفسیر اور بیان خود مجمل (اجمال کرنے والے) سے دریافت کی جاتی ہے پس مذکورہ مسائل میں بھی چونکہ ایک گونہ اجمال ہے اس لئے ان تینوں مسائل میں بھی مجمل یعنی مکفول لہ کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا بشرطیکہ مکفول لہ موجود ہو۔
Hadhrat Imam Abu Yusuf said that its ruling is like the first issue, i.e., like the word 'bara'ah' (discharge). Just as when one says 'bara'ah al-'amma' the kafil has the right to recourse against the makful 'anhu, similarly, when one says only the word 'bara'ah', the kafil will also have the right to recourse against the makful 'anhu. Its proof is that the makful lahu, by saying 'bara'ah', acknowledged a discharge whose origin is from the kafil, because he mentioned the letter of address (i.e., 'ta'). So the discharge will be from an act specifically attributed to the kafil, and from the kafil's side there is payment (ada'), not discharging (ibra'). That is, payment is from the kafil's act, but discharging is not present from his act. So when this discharge is from the kafil, and the discharge obtained from the kafil is obtained by payment, therefore this discharge will also be obtained by the kafil's payment. And when a discharge is obtained by the kafil's payment, the kafil has the right of recourse against the makful 'anhu. Therefore, even in the case of saying the mere word 'bara'ah', the kafil will have full right of recourse against the makful 'anhu. Sahib al-Hidayah said that some mashayikh stated that the mentioned rulings in the three issues apply when the makful lahu, after uttering those words, has become absent. But if the makful lahu is present, then in all three issues, recourse will be had to his explanation, i.e., he will be asked whether he has taken possession of the property or not, because the makful lahu himself created the ambiguity in the speech, and the rule is that the interpretation and explanation of ambiguous speech is sought from the one who created the ambiguity. Therefore, in these issues as well, since there is a kind of ambiguity, recourse will be had to the one who created the ambiguity, i.e., the makful lahu, provided he is present.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the effect of the word 'bara'ah' in kafalah. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that when the creditor (makful lahu) says 'bara'ah' (discharge) to the kafil, it implies that the kafil has fulfilled the debt, thus granting the kafil the right to seek reimbursement from the debtor (makful 'anhu). The reasoning (ta'lil) is that the discharge is attributed to the kafil's act of payment (ada'), not to the creditor's act of waiving (ibra'). This is because the creditor uses the second person 'ta' addressing the kafil. Therefore, the discharge is linked to the kafil's payment, which naturally gives him recourse. The passage also notes a refinement from Sahib al-Hidayah: these rulings apply when the creditor is absent; if he is present, his statement is taken as the interpretation of his ambiguous words, and he is asked whether he actually received the property.

Key Terms
برات (bara'ah): In this context, a verbal discharge from kafalah, implying the kafil has paid the debt.
مکفول عنہ (makful 'anhu): The principal debtor for whom the kafil guarantees.
مکفول لہ (makful lahu): The creditor in a kafalah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the word 'bara'ah' is a clear waiver of the debt.
B) Because the discharge is addressed to the kafil, implying his payment.
C) Because the creditor is absent.
D) Because the kafil has paid the debt directly.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a discharge (bara'ah) addressed to the kafil implies payment, granting the kafil the right to recover from the debtor, provided the creditor is absent.

Suspending Discharge from Kafalah on a Condition
Ruling and debate on whether discharge from kafalah can be conditional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on suspending discharge from kafalah and explain why the preferred view treats it as pure isqat (dropping of demand) that can be conditional.

Core Idea
Discharge from kafalah is pure isqat and can be conditional, like talaq.

This passage examines a specific legal question: can a creditor conditionally discharge a kafil (guarantor) from kafalah? Two intra-Hanafi views exist, one treating discharge as tamlik (transfer of ownership of the right to demand) and the other as isqat (dropping of demand). The preferred view, as outlined in al-Hidayah, adopts the isqat interpretation, making conditional discharge valid. Understanding this distinction is critical for drafting valid kafalah contracts and avoiding disputes over revocability.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the two views: Quduri's view (discharge is tamlik, cannot be conditional) and the Nawadir narration (discharge is isqat, can be conditional). Note that the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the latter.
The passage contrasts tamlik and isqat categories from Hanafi fiqh.
2
Identify the opponent's proof
Explain why Quduri treats discharge as tamlik: the creditor 'owns' the right to demand, so discharging transfers ownership to the kafil—a tamlik act that cannot be conditional.
Tamlik contracts (like sale) generally require immediate finality; conditions create uncertainty (gharar).
3
Analyse the Hanafi response (preferred view)
Understand the Nawadir argument: the kafil's liability is only for demand (mutalabah), not the debt itself. Dropping demand is pure isqat, which can be conditional, akin to talaq.
Rational proof (dalil aqli): isqat does not involve transfer of ownership, only waiver of a right.
4
Resolve the objection
Address the objection about payment as a condition: the text distinguishes between suitable (munasib) and unsuitable conditions. A condition that aligns with the contract's purpose (like payment) is permissible; the prohibition applies only to unsuitable conditions.
This resolution clarifies that the rule is not absolute.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: if discharge is isqat, it is irrevocable by the kafil's rejection; if tamlik, the kafil can reject and the discharge is revoked. The preferred view's consequence is that conditional discharges are binding once the condition is met.
This affects how creditors structure guarantee agreements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بالرد بخلاف ابراء الاصيل. ترجمہ اور کفالہ سے بری کرنے کو شرط پر معلق کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں مالک کرنے کے معنی ہیں جیسے دوسری براءتوں میں ہوتے ہیں اور روایت ہے کہ یہ صحیح ہے کیونکہ صحیح قول دیا اور تملیکات یعنی مالک کرنے کو شرط پر معلق کرنا ، نا جائز ہے لہذا کفالہ سے بری ہونے کو بھی شرط پر معلق کرنا نا جائز ہوگا۔ جیسا ، وسری براتوں کو شرط پر معلق کرنا نا جائز ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے کہا کہ یہاں ایک اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر فیل بالمال نے مکفول لڑ سے یہ کہا کہ اگر میں کل آ ئندہ مال ادا کر دوں تو میں کفالہ سے بری ہوں پس اس نے شرط کے مطابق مال ادا کر دیا تو کفیل، مال اور مطالبہ سے بری ہو پس معلوم ہوا کہ برات من الکفالہ اسقاط محض ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ کفیل کا کفالہ سے بری ہونا اس کے رد کرنے سے رد نہیں ہوتا لیکن اصیل یعنی مکفول عنہ اگر اپنے بری ہونے کو رد کر دے تو رد ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ جو چیز اسقاطات کے قبیلہ سے ہو وہ رد کرنے سے رد نہیں ہوتی ہے اور جو چیز تملیکات کے قبیلہ سے ہو وہ رد کرنے سے رد ہو جاتی ہے۔ بہر حال ثابت ہوا کہ کفیل کا بری ہونا اسقاط محض ہے اور اسقاط محض کو شرط پر معلق کرنا صحیح ہے۔ اسلئے برات من الکفالہ کو بھی شرط پر معلق کرنا جائز ہوگا۔
He said: Suspending discharge from kafalah upon a condition is not permissible, because there is in it a meaning of tamlik (making owner) as in other discharges. And it is narrated that it is valid, because in the correct view, upon the kafil is the demand (mutalabah), not the debt, so it is pure isqat (dropping) like talaq. And for this reason, the discharge of the kafil is not revoked by rejection, unlike the discharge of the original debtor. Translation: And discharging from kafalah by suspending it on a condition is not permissible, because in it there is a meaning of making owner, as in other discharges. And a narration holds it is valid because according to the correct view, upon the kafil is the demand, not the debt, so it is pure dropping like talaq. For this reason, the discharge of the kafil is not revoked by rejection, contrary to the discharge of the original debtor. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says that suspending discharge from kafalah on a condition is not permissible. For example, the creditor said: 'If tomorrow comes, you are free from the kafalah.' This is not permissible. The proof is that discharge from kafalah is not pure isqat, but it has a meaning of tamlik, in that due to kafalah, the creditor was the owner of the right to demand from the kafil, but when the kafil is discharged, it is as if the kafil becomes the owner of the demand, and tamlikat (making owners) cannot be suspended on a condition, so discharge from kafalah cannot be suspended on a condition. Allamah Ibn al-Humann noted an objection: if the kafil bil-mal says to the creditor, 'If I pay the property tomorrow, I am free from the kafalah,' then he pays according to the condition, the kafil becomes free from the property and demand. So it seems that suspending discharge on a condition is valid. The answer is that this condition is suitable for the kafalah contract, and the ruling mentioned in the book is about an unsuitable condition. That is, suspending discharge on a suitable condition is permissible, but on an unsuitable condition it is not. Sahib al-Hidayah says that according to the narration from Nawadir, suspending discharge from kafalah on a condition is permissible. The proof for taking this narration is that the kafil's discharge from kafalah is pure isqat, like talaq is pure isqat. Because according to the correct view, upon the kafil is the demand, not the debt, and by the kafil's discharge, the demand is dropped. So it is clear that discharge from kafalah is pure isqat. This is why the kafil's discharge is not revoked by his rejection, but if the original debtor (makful 'anhu) rejects his own discharge, it is revoked. Because what is from the category of isqat is not revoked by rejection, and what is from the category of tamlik is revoked by rejection. In any case, it is established that the kafil's discharge is pure isqat, and pure isqat can be suspended on a condition. Therefore, suspending discharge from kafalah on a condition is permissible.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about whether discharging a kafil from kafalah can be made conditional. The base position (from Quduri) holds it is not permissible because discharge in kafalah has an element of tamlik (transfer of ownership of the right to demand). However, a narration (from Nawadir) holds it is permissible because the kafil's liability is only for demand (mutalabah), not the debt itself, making it pure isqat (dropping of a right), like talaq. The passage resolves an objection by distinguishing between suitable and unsuitable conditions. The preferred position (mufta bihi) according to the text is that it is permissible because it is isqat. The practical difference: if it is isqat, the discharge is not revocable; if tamlik, it is revocable upon rejection.

Key Terms
اسقاط (isqat): Dropping or waiving a right; here, the kafil's discharge is pure isqat because it drops the creditor's right of demand.
تملیک (tamlik): Making someone owner; here, transferring the right of demand from creditor to kafil.
مطالبہ (mutalabah): The right to demand payment from the kafil; the kafil's liability is only this, not the debt itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (mufta bihi) in this passage, why is suspending discharge from kafalah on a condition permissible?
A) Because it is a form of tamlik.
B) Because the kafil's liability is for the debt itself.
C) Because it is pure isqat, like talaq.
D) Because the condition must be suitable.

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi view is that discharge from kafalah is isqat and can be conditional, with suitable conditions being permissible.

Kafalah Invalid for Hudud and Qisas
General rule invalidating kafalah for non-transferable rights like hudud and qisas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that kafalah is invalid for hudud and qisas, explain the reasoning based on niyabah, and distinguish this from kafalah for the person's presence.

Core Idea
Punishment is personal — it cannot be transferred to a kafil because niyabah does not apply to hudud and qisas.

This lesson clarifies a key limitation of kafalah (guarantee) in Hanafi fiqh: it is only valid for rights that can be lawfully exacted from the guarantor. Since hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation) are corporal in nature and tied to the actual perpetrator, they cannot be subject to kafalah. The passage presents the ruling, its proof, and a related dispute about guaranteeing the accused's presence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Find the statement that kafalah is only valid for rights exactionable from the kafil. Quote the rule in your own words.
The rule is stated by al-Quduri: 'Every right whose exaction from the kafil is not possible, kafalah for it is not valid.'
2
Apply the Rule to Hudud and Qisas
The rule is applied specifically to hudud and qisas. Note that the ruling is about the punishment itself, not the person on whom it is due.
3
Extract the Dalil and Wajh al-Dalalah
The proof is based on the nature of punishment: it is not transferable because niyabah (representation) does not operate in penal matters. The purpose is deterrence for the specific criminal.
The passage argues via qiyas that obligation as an original is impossible (kafil didn't commit crime) and by representation is also impossible (no niyabah in punishments).
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
While kafalah for the punishment itself is invalid by consensus, kafalah merely to present the accused to court is disputed: Imam Abu Hanifa holds it invalid; the Sahibayn and majority hold it valid.
This is a separate issue from the main ruling.
5
Conclude the Mufta Bihi Position
The relied-upon position is that kafalah for hudud and qisas themselves is absolutely invalid. For kafalah of presence, the mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn (permissible).

و كل حق لا يمكن استيفاء ٥ من الكفيل لا يصح الكفالة به كالحدود والقصاص معناه بنفس الحد لا بنفس من عليه الحد لأنه يتعذر ايجابه عليه و هذا لأن العقوبة لا يجرى فيها النيابة. ترجمہ اور جس حق کا کفیل سے وصول کرنا ممکن نہ ہو اس کا کفالہ صحیح نہیں ہے جیسے حدود اور قصاص اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ نفس حد( کی کفالت صحیح نہیں ہے ) نہ کہ اس شخص کی ذات کی جس پر کفالہ ہے کیونکہ کفیل پر حد یا قصاص واجب کرنا متعذر ہے اور یہ اس لئے کہ سزا میں نیابت جاری نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے ضابطہ کے طور پر فرمایا کہ ہر وہ حق جس کا کفیل سے حاصل کرنا شرعاً صحیح نہ ہو اس کا کفالہ درست نہیں ۔ مثلا نفس حد اور نفس قصاص کا کفالہ جائز نہیں ہے ہاں جس شخص پر حد یا قصاص واجب ہو اس کو مجلس قاضی میں حاضر کرنے کا کفیل ہونا اگر چہ حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے لیکن صاحبین اور جمہور علماء کے نزدیک جائز ہے البتہ نفس حداور نفس قصاص کا کفالہ بالاتفاق جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً حامد نے کہا کہ اگر خالد نے حد زنا کو یا قصاص کو نہ دیا تو میں اس کی طرف سے کفیل ہوں مجھ پر خد اور قصاص جاری کیا جائے اس عدم جواز کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفیل پر حد یا قصاص کو واجب کرنا معذ ر اور ناممکن ہے کیونکہ کفیل پر حد یا قصاص کا وجوب یا تو اصالۃ ہوگا اور یا نیا بہ ہو گا۔ اول تو خلاف مفروض ہونے کی وجہ سے باطل ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مسئلہ یہ فرض کیا گیا ہے کہ ایسے جرم کا ارتکاب جس کی وجہ سے حد یا قصاص واجب ہو کفیل نے نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ دوسرے نے کیا ہے پس جب جرم کا ارتکاب کفیل کے علاوہ دوسرے نے کیا ہے تو کفیل پر اصالۂ حد یا قصاص کیسے واجب ہو سکتا ہے اور کفیل پر نیا پہ بھی حد یا قصاص واجب نہیں ہوتی کیونک سزاؤں میں نیابت جاری نہیں ہوتی اور سزاؤں میں نیابت اس لئے جاری نہیں ہوتی کہ سزا کا مقصد مرتکب جرم کو جرم سے روکنا ہوتا ہے اور نائب کو سزا دینے سے مقصد حاصل نہیں ہوتا اس لئے حد اور قصاص یعنی سزاؤں میں نیابت بھی جاری نہ ہوگی۔ پس جب کفیل پر حد اور قصاص کا وجوب
And every right whose exaction from the kafil is not possible, kafalah for it is not valid, like hudud and qisas. Its meaning is regarding the hadd itself, not regarding the person on whom the hadd is due, because imposing it on the kafil is impossible. And this is because punishment cannot be vicarious. Translation: And every right that cannot be obtained from the kafil, its kafalah is not valid, like hudud and qisas. Its meaning is that kafalah for the hadd itself is not valid, not for the person on whom the hadd is due, because making the kafil liable for hadd or qisas is impossible. And this is because punishment does not admit representation. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri stated as a rule that every right that cannot be lawfully obtained from the kafil, its kafalah is not valid. For example, kafalah for the hadd itself and for qisas itself is not permissible. However, becoming a kafil to present the person on whom hadd or qisas is due to the court of the qadi, although according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is not permissible, according to the Sahibayn and the majority of scholars it is permissible. But kafalah for the hadd itself and qisas itself is unanimously not permissible. For example, Hamid said: 'If Khalid does not pay the hadd of zina or qisas, I am kafil on his behalf; implement the hadd and qisas on me.' The proof for its impermissibility is that imposing hadd or qisas on the kafil is impossible, because the obligation of hadd or qisas on the kafil would be either as an original (asalah) or by representation (niyabah). The first is invalid because it contradicts the assumption; the issue is assumed that the kafil did not commit the crime that necessitates hadd or qisas, but someone else did. So when the crime was committed by someone other than the kafil, how can hadd or qisas be obligatory on him as an original? And by representation, hadd or qisas is not obligatory on the kafil because punishment does not admit representation. And punishment does not admit representation because the purpose of punishment is to deter the perpetrator from crime, and punishing the representative does not achieve that purpose. Therefore, hadd and qisas do not admit representation. So imposing hadd or qisas on the kafil is impossible.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage states a general legal principle: kafalah is only valid for rights that can be lawfully exacted from the kafil. Since hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation) are corporal punishments, they cannot be executed on a kafil who did not commit the crime. The text clarifies that kafalah for the punishment itself (like hadd or qisas) is invalid by consensus, although kafalah merely to present the accused person to court is permissible according to the Sahibayn and majority (but not Imam Abu Hanifa). The proof is that liability for punishment cannot be transferred or vicarious; it must be based on the actual perpetrator. The purpose of punishment is deterrence for the specific criminal, not for a substitute. Therefore, any attempt to guarantee the execution of hadd or qisas on the kafil is legally impossible and invalid.

Key Terms
حدود (hudud): Fixed corporal punishments for specific crimes (e.g., zina, theft) defined in Shariah.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for murder or bodily harm, equivalent to the harm caused.
نیابت (niyabah): Representation or substitution; punishment cannot be carried out by proxy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is kafalah for the hadd or qisas itself invalid?
A) Because the person on whom the punishment is due is absent.
B) Because punishments cannot be transferred or executed by proxy.
C) Because the kafil has already paid a fine.
D) Because the creditor has forgiven the right.

Key Takeaway
Kafalah for hudud and qisas themselves is invalid because punishment cannot be vicarious; only the actual perpetrator can be punished.

Kafalah — Surety

Conditioning Bara'ah from Kafalah: Appropriate vs Inappropriate Conditions
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on conditioning bara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on conditioning bara'ah min al-kafalah and identify the mufta bihi position based on the distinction between appropriate and inappropriate conditions.

Core Idea
Bara'ah from kafalah can be conditioned, but only on an appropriate condition—unless you follow the Nawadir narration.

This lesson unpacks an important debate within the Hanafi school: can a guarantor (kafil) condition his release from suretyship (bara'ah min al-kafalah) on a specific event? The text from Al-Hidayah presents the dominant view that it depends on the nature of the condition. We will examine both positions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position from the book (Al-Hidayah)
The book holds that conditioning bara'ah is valid only if the condition is appropriate (munasib) to the contract of kafalah. An inappropriate condition invalidates the bara'ah.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing narration from Nawadir
The Nawadir (rare transmissions) permits conditioning bara'ah unconditionally, regardless of the appropriateness of the condition.
This is transmitted by Hasan ibn Ziyad and is a weaker riwayah.
3
Analyze the proof for each view
The book's proof: analogy to isqat (dropping) with a distinction—conditions must be appropriate. The Nawadir's proof: bara'ah is pure isqat, like talaq, which can be conditioned unconditionally.
The passage argues that bara'ah is isqat mahd (pure dropping).
4
Determine the tarjih (preference)
Al-Marghinani, the author of Al-Hidayah, prefers the distinction between appropriate and inappropriate conditions, and this is the relied-upon view.
The Nawadir narration is acknowledged but not taken as mufta bihi.
5
State the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If a guarantor uses an inappropriate condition (e.g., unrelated to the debt), the bara'ah is invalid per the book, but valid per the Nawadir. The mufta bihi is the book's position.
Thus, a condition like 'if you pay the debt by Friday' is appropriate; 'if the sun rises' is inappropriate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مال ادا کر دوں تو میں کفالہ سے بری ہوں پس اس نے شرط کے مطابق مال ادا کر دیا تو کفیل، مال اور مطالبہ سے بری ہو جاتا ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ برات من الکفالہ کو شرط پر معلق کرنا جائز ہے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ شرط عقد کفالہ کے مناسب ہے اور کتاب میں جو حکم مذکور ہے وہ شرط غیر مناسب کے بارے میں ہے یعنی شرط مناسب پر تو برات من الکفالہ کو معلق کرنا جائز ہے لیکن شرط غیر مناسب پر معلق کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نوادر کی روایت کے مطابق برأت من الکفالہ کو شرط پر متعلق کرنا جائز ہے اس روایت کو من کرنا کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفیل کا کفالہ سے بری ہونا استقاد محض ہے جیسے طلاق اسقاط محض ہے۔ کیونکہ صحیح قول کے مطابق کفیل پر مطالبہ لازم ہوتا ہے قرضہ لازم نہیں ہوتا۔ اور کفیل کے بری ہونے سے مطالبہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ برات من الکفالہ اسقاط محض ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ کفیل کا کفالہ سے بری ہونا اس کے رد کرنے سے رد نہیں ہوتا لیکن اصیل یعنی مکفول عنہ اگر اپنے بری ہونے کو رد کر دے تو رد ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ جو چیز اسقاطات کے قبیلہ سے ہو وہ رد کرنے سے رد نہیں ہوتی ہے اور جو چیز تملیکات کے قبیلہ سے ہو وہ رد کرنے سے رد ہو جاتی ہے۔ بہر حال ثابت ہوا کہ کفیل کا بری ہونا اسقاط محض ہے اور اسقاط محض کو شرط پر معلق کرنا صحیح ہے۔ اسلئے برات من الکفالہ کو بھی شرط پر معلق کرنا جائز ہوگا۔
If [the guarantor says] 'If I pay the money, I am free from the suretyship,' then he paid according to the condition, so the guarantor becomes free from the money and the claim. So it is known that it is permissible to condition bara'ah from kafalah upon a condition. The answer to this is that this condition is appropriate to the contract of kafalah, and the ruling mentioned in the book is about an inappropriate condition. That is, upon an appropriate condition, conditioning bara'ah is permissible, but upon an inappropriate condition, it is not permissible. The author of Hidayah states that according to the narration of Nawadir, conditioning bara'ah from kafalah upon a condition is permissible. The proof for adopting this narration is that the guarantor's freedom from kafalah is pure dropping [isqat], like divorce is pure dropping. Because according to the correct view, the guarantor incurs the claim, not the debt. And by the guarantor's freedom, the claim drops. So it is known that bara'ah min al-kafalah is pure dropping. For this reason, the guarantor's freedom from kafalah is not revoked by his rejection, but if the principal [makful 'anhu] rejects his own freedom, it is revoked, because what belongs to the category of dropping is not revoked by rejection, and what belongs to the category of ownership is revoked by rejection. In any case, it is established that the guarantor's freedom is pure dropping, and conditioning pure dropping upon a condition is valid. Therefore, conditioning bara'ah min al-kafalah upon a condition will be permissible.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a guarantor (kafil) can condition his release from suretyship (bara'ah min al-kafalah) on the fulfillment of a condition, such as payment by the principal. The text first presents a hypothetical: if the guarantor says, 'If I pay the money, I am free,' and then pays, he is free from both the money and the claim. This suggests that conditioning bara'ah is valid. However, the author of Al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) explains that this is only for conditions that are appropriate (munasib) to the contract; inappropriate conditions (ghayr munasib) are not valid. He then cites a narration from the Nawadir that unconditionally permits conditioning bara'ah. The reasoning is that bara'ah min al-kafalah is pure isqat (dropping of a right), analogous to talaq (divorce). In Hanafi fiqh, isqat can be conditioned. The text distinguishes between isqat and tamlik (transfer of ownership): isqat is not revoked by rejection (radd), while tamlik is. Since bara'ah is isqat, it can be conditioned. The mufta bihi position is that conditioning on an appropriate condition is valid, as per the book, while the Nawadir narration supports conditioning on any condition. The relied-upon view is the former, but the passage leans towards the Nawadir for broader validity.

Key Terms
برأت من الکفالہ (bara'ah min al-kafalah): The guarantor's release from liability and claim arising from suretyship.
اسقاط محض (isqat mahd): Pure dropping of a right without transfer, which is not revoked by rejection.
شرط مناسب (shart munasib): A condition that is appropriate and consistent with the nature of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes the Hidayah position from the Nawadir narration on conditioning bara'ah?
A) Hidayah permits unconditionally; Nawadir forbids.
B) Hidayah permits only with appropriate conditions; Nawadir permits unconditionally.
C) Hidayah forbids all conditioning; Nawadir permits only with appropriate conditions.
D) Both permit unconditionally.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, on the relied-upon view, allows conditioning bara'ah from kafalah only on conditions appropriate to the contract.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
Invalidity of Kafalah for Hudud and Qisas
Ruling with proof that suretyship for hudud and qisas is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kafalah for hudud and qisas, explain the proof based on the principle of niyaba, and distinguish the unanimous invalidity for the punishment itself from the intra-Hanafi dispute on kafalah to bring the person to court.

Core Idea
Punishments (hudud and qisas) cannot be transferred — suretyship for the punishment itself is void because representation (niyaba) does not apply in penalties.

In this passage, Al-Quduri establishes a key principle: any right that cannot be legally exacted from the guarantor renders the kafalah invalid. The specific application is to hudud and qisas — you cannot guarantee to suffer the punishment on behalf of another. The proof is based on the nature of punishments: they are personal and not transferable by representation. However, the passage also highlights an intra-Hanafi dispute about guaranteeing to bring the accused to court, which is permissible according to the majority (Sahibayn).

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage begins with a rule: Kafalah is not valid for any right that cannot be lawfully exacted from the guarantor. This is the foundation for the ruling on hudud and qisas.
2
Distinguish the two types of kafalah
Kafalah for the punishment itself (e.g., offering to serve the hadd) is unanimously invalid. Kafalah to bring the person to court is disputed: Imam Abu Hanifa says invalid, Sahibayn and majority say valid.
Do not confuse these two; they have different rulings.
3
Analyze the proof for the invalidity of kafalah for the punishment
The proof is a disjunction: the obligation on the guarantor must be either original (asalah) or by representation (niyaba). Original is impossible because the guarantor did not commit the crime. Representation is impossible because punishments do not accept niyaba, as their purpose is deterrence of the specific offender.
This is a rational (aqli) proof based on the nature of penalties.
4
Understand the rationale for the dispute on bringing to court
The Sahibayn and majority view kafalah to bring the person to court as a procedural guarantee, not a punishment itself. Imam Abu Hanifa considers it invalid because it is connected to the punishment. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn and majority.
The dispute is over the scope of 'kafalah bi al-nafs' in the context of punishments.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
For kafalah for the punishment itself: invalid by consensus. For kafalah to bring the person to court: valid according to the Sahibayn and majority, which is the operative opinion for fatwa.
This distinction is crucial for legal practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هر وہ حق جس کا استیفاء من الكفيل لا يصح الكفالة به كالحدود والقصاص معناه بنفس الحد لا بنفس من عليه الحد لأنه يتعذر ايجابه عليه و هذا لأن العقوبة لا يجرى فيها النيابة ترجمہ اور جس حق کا کفیل سے وصول کرنا ممکن نہ ہو اس کا کفالہ صحیح نہیں ہے جیسے حدود اور قصاص اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ نفس حد کی کفالت صحیح نہیں ہے نہ کہ اس شخص کی ذات کی جس پر حد واجب ہے کیونکہ کفیل پر حد یا قصاص واجب کرنا متعذر ہے اور یہ اس لئے کہ سزا میں نیابت جاری نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے ضابطہ کے طور پر فرمایا کہ ہر وہ حق جس کا کفیل سے حاصل کرنا شرعاً صحیح نہ ہو اس کا کفالہ درست نہیں ۔ مثلا نفس حد اور نفس قصاص کا کفالہ جائز نہیں ہے ہاں جس شخص پر حد یا قصاص واجب ہو اس کو مجلس قاضی میں حاضر کرنے کا کفیل ہونا اگر چہ حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے لیکن صاحبین اور جمہور علماء کے نزدیک جائز ہے البتہ نفس حد اور نفس قصاص کا کفالہ بالاتفاق جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً حامد نے کہا کہ اگر خالد نے حد زنا کو یا قصاص کو نہ دیا تو میں اس کی طرف سے کفیل ہوں مجھ پر حد اور قصاص جاری کیا جائے اس عدم جواز کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفیل پر حد یا قصاص کو واجب کرنا معذور اور ناممکن ہے کیونکہ کفیل پر حد یا قصاص کا وجوب یا تو اصالتاً ہوگا اور یا نیابۃ ہو گا۔ اول تو خلاف مفروض ہونے کی وجہ سے باطل ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مسئلہ یہ فرض کیا گیا ہے کہ ایسے جرم کا ارتکاب جس کی وجہ سے حد یا قصاص واجب ہو کفیل نے نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ دوسرے نے کیا ہے پس جب جرم کا ارتکاب کفیل کے علاوہ دوسرے نے کیا ہے تو کفیل پر اصالتاً حد یا قصاص کیسے واجب ہو سکتا ہے اور کفیل پر نیابۃ بھی حد یا قصاص واجب نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ سزاؤں میں نیابت جاری نہیں ہوتی اور سزاؤں میں نیابت اس لئے جاری نہیں ہوتی کہ سزا کا مقصد مرتکب جرم کو جرم سے روکنا ہوتا ہے اور نائب کو سزا دینے سے مقصد حاصل نہیں ہوتا اس لئے حد اور قصاص یعنی سزاؤں میں نیابت بھی جاری نہ ہوگی۔ پس جب کفیل پر حد اور قصاص کا وجوب اصالتاً ہو سکتا ہے اور نہ نیابتاً ہوسکتا ہے تو ثابت ہوا کہ نفس قصاص کا کفیل ہونا ہی درست نہیں ہے۔
Every right that cannot be exacted from the guarantor, suretyship for it is not valid, such as hudud and qisas. Its meaning is [suretyship for] the hadd itself, not for the person upon whom the hadd is due, because it is impossible to make it obligatory upon him. And this is because representation does not apply in punishments. Commentary: Al-Quduri stated as a principle: every right that cannot be obtained from the guarantor legally, its suretyship is not valid. For example, suretyship for the hadd itself and qisas itself is not permissible. Yes, suretyship to bring the person upon whom hadd or qisas is due to the court of the judge, although according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is not permissible, but according to the Sahibayn and the majority of scholars it is permissible. However, suretyship for the hadd itself and qisas itself is unanimously not permissible. For example, Hamid said: If Khalid does not submit to the hadd for zina or to qisas, then I am a guarantor on his behalf; let the hadd and qisas be executed upon me. The proof for this impermissibility is that making the hadd or qisas obligatory upon the guarantor is impossible, because the obligation of hadd or qisas upon the guarantor would be either originally (asalan) or by representation (niyabatan). The first is invalid because it contradicts the assumed situation: the crime that would necessitate hadd or qisas was not committed by the guarantor but by someone else. So when the crime was committed by another, how can hadd or qisas be obligatory upon the guarantor originally? And it is not obligatory upon the guarantor by representation either, because representation does not apply in punishments. And representation does not apply in punishments because the purpose of punishment is to deter the criminal, and punishing a representative does not achieve that purpose. Therefore, since the obligation of hadd and qisas upon the guarantor cannot be originally nor by representation, it is established that suretyship for the qisas itself is not valid.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding suretyship (kafalah) for hudud (prescribed punishments) and qisas (retribution). The principle is clear: any right that cannot be legally exacted from the guarantor renders the kafalah invalid. The specific application is that one cannot become a guarantor for the actual carrying out of a hadd punishment or qisas—that is, offering to suffer the punishment on behalf of the actual criminal. However, there is a distinction: guaranteeing to bring the accused to court is a different matter. Imam Abu Hanifa holds this invalid, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) consider it valid, and the majority follow the latter. The proof for the main ruling is based on the nature of punishments: they are personal and cannot be transferred through representation (niyaba). The purpose of punishment is deterrence of the specific offender; punishing a substitute would not fulfill this purpose. Therefore, since the guarantor cannot incur the punishment either as the original offender (he didn't commit the crime) or as a representative (niyaba is invalid in punishments), the suretyship is impossible and void.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for crimes like zina, theft, etc.
قصاص (qisas): Retributive punishment for homicide or injury, equivalent to the crime.
نیابت (niyaba): Representation or delegation of a duty to another person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is suretyship for the actual hadd or qisas invalid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the guarantor cannot be punished for a crime he did not commit.
B) Because punishments do not accept representation (niyaba).
C) Because the guarantor may not be present in court.
D) Because the crime must be proven against the actual culprit.

Key Takeaway
Suretyship for hudud and qisas themselves is invalid because punishments do not accept representation; however, guaranteeing to produce the accused to court is valid according to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn and majority).

Kafalah — Surety
beginner
6 min
Kafalah by Buyer for Price is Valid
Simple ruling statement with brief reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on kafalah for the price (thaman) in a sale and explain its basis as a debt.

Core Idea
Kafalah for the sale price is valid because the price is a debt, just like any other financial obligation.

In Hanafi fiqh, kafalah (suretyship) is a contract of guarantee. A key question is whether the price in a sale, which is a debt owed by the buyer, can be guaranteed by a third party. This lesson presents the straightforward ruling that such kafalah is valid, based on the principle that the price is a debt (dayn) like any other debt. Understanding this helps clarify the scope of kafalah in financial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a person becoming a guarantor (kafil) on behalf of the buyer (mushtari) for the price (thaman) in a sale contract. The ruling is that this is valid (ja'iz).
2
Understand the legal basis
The ruling is justified because the price is a debt (dayn). In Hanafi law, debts are suitable subjects for kafalah since they are definite financial obligations that can be enforced against the guarantor.
The text explicitly states: 'li-annahu daynun ka-sa'ir al-duyun' (because it is a debt like other debts).
3
Connect to general kafalah principles
Kafalah is generally valid for any debt that is known and enforceable. Once the guarantee is given, the creditor (seller) can claim the price from the guarantor if the buyer defaults.
This ruling aligns with the broader Hanafi view that kafalah is a valid form of security for financial obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مشتری کی طرف سے ثمن کی کفالت کا حکم
وإذا تكفل عن المشترى بالثمن جاز لأنه دين كسائر الديون
ترجمہ اور اگر مشتری کی طرف سے ثمن کا کفیل ہو گیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ ثمن بھی دوسرے دیون کی طرح دین صحیح ہے
تشریح مصنف نے فرمایا کہ ثمن کا کفیل ہونا جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثمن دین صحیح ہے۔ اور کفیل سے اس کا وصول کرنا بھی ممکن ہے۔ لہذا دوسرے دیون اور قرضہ کی طرح اس کا کفالہ بھی جائز ہوگا۔
Ruling on suretyship by the buyer for the price: And if one becomes a guarantor on behalf of the buyer for the price, it is valid because it is a debt like other debts. Commentary: The author stated that becoming a guarantor for the price is valid. The proof is that the price is a valid debt, and it is possible to recover it from the guarantor. Therefore, its suretyship is valid like other debts and loans.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling: a person can act as a guarantor (kafil) for the buyer (mushtari) regarding the price (thaman) in a sale contract. The reason is that the price is a debt (dayn) like any other financial obligation—it is a definite liability. Since debts are generally subject to kafalah, and the guarantor can be held liable for payment, this suretyship is valid. No special conditions or exceptions are mentioned; it falls under the general permissibility of kafalah for financial debts.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The price in a sale contract, which is a debt owed by the buyer.
مشتری (mushtari): The buyer in a sale contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is kafalah for the price (thaman) by the buyer's side valid?
A) Because the price is a physical item.
B) Because the price is a debt like other debts.
C) Because the seller is entitled to the price.
D) Because the guarantor must be a relative.

Key Takeaway
Kafalah for the price in a sale is valid because the price is a debt, and kafalah for debts is generally valid.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
Kafalah for Physical Items: Hanafi Classification and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling with detailed classification and inter-madhhab dispute on kafalah for specific items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi classification of physical items (madmun bi-nafsihi vs bi-ghayrihi) to determine the validity of kafalah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-position.

Core Idea
In Hanafi, kafalah for physical items is valid only if the item is guaranteed by itself, not by another.

This lesson unpacks a nuanced Hanafi ruling on kafalah for physical goods. While kafalah is usually for debts, the Hanafi school extends it to certain physical items, but with a critical distinction: items guaranteed by themselves are eligible, while those guaranteed by another (like the sold item in a valid sale) are not. The passage also records the Shafi'i objection and clarifies that kafalah for acts of delivery is always valid.

Guided Path
1
State the primary ruling
Identify the ruling: kafalah by the seller for the sold item itself is invalid. Note the reason: the sold item is 'madmun bi-ghayrihi' (guaranteed by another, i.e., the price).
This is the core rule; the rest is classification.
2
Classify items into three categories
Categorize physical items as: (1) madmun bi-nafsihi (guaranteed by self), (2) madmun bi-ghayrihi (guaranteed by another), (3) amanah (trusts). Note the examples: fasid sale item, approval item, usurped property in (1); sold item (valid sale), pawned item in (2); deposit, borrowed, leased, partnership capital in (3).
Kafalah valid only for category (1).
3
Identify the Hanafi vs Shafi'i dispute
Recognize that Shafi'i school holds kafalah for any physical item is invalid; Hanafi school permits it for category (1). The passage mentions this ikhtilaf briefly.
The thamarah (practical difference) is that Hanafis can guarantee return of usurped items, Shafi'is cannot.
4
Analyze the exception: kafalah for delivery
Note that kafalah for the act of delivery (tasleem) is valid even if the item itself cannot be guaranteed. This is because the guarantor undertakes an obligatory action, not liability for the item.
Examples: delivering sold item before possession, returning pawn, handing over leased item.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بائع سے بیع کی کفالت ممنوع ہے
و إن تكفل عن البائع بالمبيع لم تصح لأنه عين مضمون بغيره و هو الثمن والكفالة بالاعيان المضمونة وإن كانت تصح عندنا خلافاً للشافعي لكن بالاعيان المضمونة بنفسها كالمبيع بيعا فاسداً والمقبوض على سوم الشراء و المغصوب لا بما كان مضمونا بغيره كالمبيع والمرهون ولا بما كان امانة كالوديعة والمستعار والمستاجر ومال المضاربة والشركة ولو كفّل بتسليم المبيع قبل القبض أو بتسليم الرهن بعد القبض الى الراهن أو بتسليم المستاجر الى المستاجر جاز لأنه التزم فعلاً واجباً
ترجمہ اور اگر بائع کی طرف سے کوئی شخص مبیع کا کفیل ہو گیا تو صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ مبیع ایک عین ہے جو اپنے علاوہ یعنی ثمن کے بدلے مضمون ہوتی ہے اور اعیان مضمونہ کا کفالہ، امام شافعی کے برخلاف اگر چہ ہمارے نزدیک صحیح ہے لیکن انھیں اعیان کا کفالہ جائز ہے جو اپنی ذات سے مضمون ہیں جیسے بیع فاسد کی صورت میں مبیع اور وہ عین جو خریدنے کے طور پر قبضہ کی گئی ہو اور مال مغصوب۔ ان اعیان کا کفالہ صحیح نہیں ہے جو دوسری چیز کے عوض مضمون ہوں جیسے مبیع اور مال مرہون۔ اور نہ ان اعیان کا کفالہ صحیح ہے جو امانت ہوں جیسے مال ودیعت اور عین مستعار اور عین مستاجر اور مال مضاربت اور مال شرکت۔ اور اگر قبضہ سے پہلے مبیع سپرد کرنے کا یا قبضہ کے بعد راہن کو مال رہن سپرد کرنے کا یا مستاجر کو مستاجر کے سپرد کرنے کا کفیل ہو گیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ کفیل نے فعل واجب کا التزام کیا ہے۔
Suretyship by the seller for the sold item is prohibited. And if one becomes a guarantor on behalf of the seller for the sold item, it is not valid because the sold item is a specific item (ayn) guaranteed by something else, which is the price. And kafalah for guaranteed items (a'yan madmuna), although it is valid in our school contrary to al-Shafi'i, but it is only valid for items that are guaranteed by themselves, like the sold item in a fasid sale, items taken on approval (on the basis of purchase), and usurped property. It is not valid for items that are guaranteed by something else, like the sold item (in a valid sale) and pawned property. Also, it is not valid for items that are trusts, like deposits, borrowed items, leased items, partnership capital (mudaraba and shirka). And if one becomes a guarantor for the delivery of the sold item before possession, or for delivery of the pawn after possession to the pawnor, or for delivery of the leased item to the lessee, this is valid because the guarantor has undertaken an obligatory action.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage contains a complex ruling on kafalah for physical items (a'yan). The main rule is that suretyship for the sold item (mabee') by the seller is invalid. The reason is that the sold item in a valid sale is 'guaranteed by another' (madmun bi-ghayrihi) — meaning its guarantee is tied to the price; if the item is lost, the seller is not liable because ownership has transferred. Therefore, kafalah for such an item is not valid. The text then provides a classification of physical items regarding kafalah: 
1. Items guaranteed by themselves (madmun bi-nafsihi): these include the subject matter of a fasid sale, items possessed on approval to purchase, and usurped property. For these, kafalah is valid in the Hanafi school (contra Shafi'i).
2. Items guaranteed by another (madmun bi-ghayrihi): like the sold item in a valid sale and pawned property — kafalah is not valid.
3. Trusts (amanat): like deposits, borrowed items, leased items, and partnership capital — kafalah is also not valid.
The passage then makes an exception: if the kafalah is for the act of delivery (tasleem) of the item, rather than for the item itself, it is valid. For example, guaranteeing to deliver the sold item before the buyer takes possession, or to return the pawn to the pawnor, or to hand over the rented item to the lessee — these are valid because they are obligatory actions.

Key Terms
عین مضمون بغیرہ ('ayn madmun bi-ghayrihi): A specific item whose liability (damān) is tied to something else, like the price in a sale.
عین مضمون بنفسہ ('ayn madmun bi-nafsihi): A specific item that itself is subject to liability, like usurped property.
امانت (amanah): A trust held without liability for loss unless negligence occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following items does the Hanafi school consider valid for kafalah (suretyship) according to the passage?
A) The sold item in a valid sale (mabee').
B) The pawned item (marhun).
C) The subject of a fasid sale (mabee' fasad).
D) A borrowed item (musta'ar).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi, kafalah for physical items is valid only if the item is guaranteed by itself (madmun bi-nafsihi); items guaranteed by another or held as trust are not eligible.
